A claim-class downgrade? A user-intent rebinding? A root mismatch? A forbidden representation retraction? A visual contradiction? A manifest/checksum obligation? A task-state reopen? A production-authority overclaim?

Each type changes the world differently.

A factual correction may downgrade a claim. A wrong artifact root may block all further work until target realignment occurs. A visual contradiction may reopen a task thought complete. A production-authority overclaim may require forbidden-representation retraction. A user clarification may not prove an external fact, but it can carry high authority over intent and target.

This means repair is not merely downstream of speech. It is downstream of the entire ION ontology:

```text
claim
artifact
authority
scope
target
identity
context
visual evidence
manifest/checksum state
production boundary
next-session inheritance
```

A correction touches whichever of those was misrepresented.

---

## 3. Relationship to the Front-Stage Council

Entry 6 settled the Front-Stage Council as ION’s user-facing truth membrane:

```text
Persona renders.
Relay grounds.
Steward authorizes.
Persona emits.
```

Conversational repair begins after that membrane has already let something through, or while a low-latency utterance is still provisional.

The relationship is:

```text
V41-like concern:
Should this claim be emitted, under what class, with what grounding, visibility, and repair obligation?

V42-like concern:
Once the claim or action is corrected, contradicted, narrowed, upgraded, downgraded, retracted, or redirected, how does that change become durable state?
```

This relationship forbids a subtle but dangerous bypass. Repair cannot be used to smuggle forbidden claims into acceptability. If a representation was forbidden, repair must record the block, retract or correct the representation, and preserve the future guard. It cannot say, “Because I repaired it, the original claim was acceptable.”

Repair is downstream from council law, not an override of council law.

---

## 4. The Core Object: Repair Receipt

The mature encyclopedia shape wants a repair receipt that can answer:

```text
What was emitted or targeted?
Why did it need repair?
Who or what triggered the repair?
What claim, artifact, scope, or authority changed?
What is now authoritative?
What must future agents remember?
What evidence supports the new state?
What remains unresolved?
```

The current V116 root contains a narrower but real `conversational_receipt.py` surface. It records provisional utterances, correction, retraction, ratification, block status, repair obligations, production-authority falsehood, and forbidden claim categories. Its design is deliberately modest. It does not mutate artifacts. It does not send user-facing messages. It classifies conversation status and writes receipt JSON under history when asked.

My current interpretation:

```text
The current root contains a live conversational receipt organ.
The encyclopedia describes a broader conversational repair receipt organ.
The mature concept probably includes both:
- low-latency provisional utterance repair; and
- durable artifact/claim/authority repair receipts.
```

The current organ is not wrong merely because it is smaller. It may be a minimal slice. But if it remains only a provisional-utterance receipt surface and never grows or connects into artifact-target, manifest, checksum, context, and Steward integration obligations, then it will not fulfill the mature V42 promise.

---

## 5. The Difference Between Apology, Acknowledgment, Repair, and Integration

ION must distinguish states that ordinary chat collapses.

```text
Apology:
A user-facing expression of regret or correction posture.

Acknowledgment:
Recognition that a correction has been received.

Repair classification:
Determination of what kind of state change the correction requires.

Repair receipt:
Durable record of trigger, before-state, after-state, evidence, obligations, and visibility.

Artifact repair:
Actual patch/update/regeneration of the affected artifact.

Verification:
Evidence that the repair landed in the correct surface.

Integration:
Steward acceptance of the repaired state into future routing/context.
```

The old assistant pattern collapses all of these into apology. ION’s pattern must separate them.

The most dangerous false equation is:

```text
I said sorry == the system has been repaired
```

The second most dangerous is:

```text
I corrected my wording == the artifact/root/context has been repaired
```

The third is:

```text
I generated a receipt == the repaired claim is now true
```

ION must reject all three.

---

## 6. Chat Correction Does Not Equal Artifact Correction

This law deserves first-class status.

A chat correction can repair the immediate representational surface. It can tell the user, “The prior claim was too strong,” or “I used the wrong target,” or “That was a proposal, not verified state.” But unless the affected artifact, manifest, checksum, context package, active packet, or future worker instruction is updated, the correction may die in the conversation.

The recurring ION failure has often looked like this:

```text
User corrects AI.
AI apologizes.
AI says it understands.
AI continues.
The file still says the wrong thing.
The test still preserves the wrong invariant.
The manifest still indexes the wrong surface.
The next agent reloads the old state.
The user must correct the same thing again.
```

That is not merely frustrating. It is ontological breakage. The system is failing to preserve reality after correction.

A correction must therefore ask:

```text
Is this only a conversational representation repair?
Does it affect an artifact?
Does it affect root selection?
Does it affect a test invariant?
Does it affect a manifest/checksum?
Does it affect context packages or spawn plans?
Does it affect future onboarding?
Does it affect production-boundary claims?
Does it affect what a carrier must refuse to do?
```

If yes, apology is insufficient.

---

## 7. User Correction as Authority Signal

A user correction is not automatically external factual truth. The user can be mistaken about external facts, filesystem state, code behavior, or what a test proves.

But in ION, user correction carries high authority over several domains:

```text
user intent
target artifact
target root
frustration/urgency signal
acceptability of representation
whether the assistant has misunderstood the project’s meaning
whether a conversational repair must be visible
```

This is crucial. If the user says, “That is not the right target,” the correction has direct authority over target alignment even before the filesystem is inspected. If the user says, “You are doing the same chaos as the other agents,” that is not automatically a technical proof, but it is a high-priority drift signal. If the user says, “Almost everything is already in ION,” that is not proof of every file, but it is a powerful search-orientation command: assume mature systems exist before inventing replacements.

ION must therefore distinguish:

```text
user correction as target authority
user correction as intent authority
user correction as drift signal
user correction as external-fact claim
user correction as emotional/operational pressure
```

The repair receipt should preserve which class of authority the user correction carried.

---

## 8. Repair Classes as Ontological Types

The encyclopedia’s V42 candidate text lists many repair classes. I currently group them into seven deeper families.

### 8.1 Claim repair

A claim was too strong, too weak, wrongly grounded, or wrongly classed.

Examples:

```text
C0 verified state downgraded to C2 proposal.
Speculation upgraded after evidence appears.
Production-readiness claim retracted.
Unverified relay content marked as C4.
```

### 8.2 Target repair

The work was pointed at the wrong surface.

Examples:

```text
canvas instead of Markdown file
wrong zip root
older archive instead of current root
candidate appendix mistaken for live project file
```

### 8.3 Authority repair

A worker, carrier, Persona, or document claimed more authority than it had.

Examples:

```text
carrier treated as role
assistant treated as entire ION
repair receipt treated as production authority
focused tests treated as full-suite proof
```

### 8.4 Context repair

Future workers would inherit the wrong context unless repaired.

Examples:

```text
summary preserved stale branch as current
spawn plan references wrong onboarding surface
context package omits correction reason
route map points to stale protocol
```

### 8.5 Artifact repair

A file, manifest, checksum, exported zip, or generated artifact must change.

Examples:

```text
wrong file updated
zip excludes changed file
manifest still references deleted root guide
checksum stale after patch
```

### 8.6 Visual/rendered repair

Rendered behavior contradicts source claims or implementation claims.

Examples:

```text
UI said fixed but screenshot shows overflow
DOM was inspected but no visual receipt exists
source code correct but rendered product broken
```

### 8.7 Continuation repair

The next state of the work must be reopened, blocked, rerouted, or marked partial.

Examples:

```text
task marked done but repair incomplete
agent proceeds after blocking target mismatch
future worker needs reason for downgrade
```

This typology matters because each repair family has a different completion standard.

---

## 9. Completion Standards

A repair is complete only relative to its class.

A conversational-only repair may be complete when the user-facing statement has been corrected and no durable artifact/state was affected.

A claim repair is complete when before-state and after-state are recorded, visibility requirements are satisfied, and the next context inherits the corrected claim class.

A target repair is complete only when the correct target is identified, wrong target contamination is bounded, affected outputs are moved/regenerated or marked invalid, and future routing points to the correct surface.

An artifact repair is complete only when the affected artifact is patched and any required manifest, checksum, export, or verification surface is updated.

A visual repair is complete only when the visual evidence chain distinguishes observation, diagnosis, patch, and post-patch verification.

A production-boundary repair is complete only when the overclaim is retracted, the corrected authority status is visible, and future claim guards are strengthened if needed.

So the most compressed completion law is:

```text
A repair is complete only when the state surface that was wrong can no longer lawfully reproduce the wrongness without triggering a new violation.
```

That is stronger than “the user was told.”

---

## 10. Why This Has Been So Painful in ION

ION’s history contains an enormous number of repairs that were intellectually recognized but operationally under-integrated.

The user would identify a wrong root, wrong model of ION, wrong role interpretation, stale file, hallucinated onboarding surface, inferior replacement, or missing older protocol. The assistant would acknowledge it. Sometimes a file would be patched. Sometimes a report would be written. Sometimes a zip would be produced. But unless the corrected state became the next agent’s unavoidable starting condition, the same error returned.

This reveals the deeper failure:

```text
Repair without inheritance is only interruption.
```

The next agent must inherit not merely the corrected sentence, but the reason the repair occurred.

For example, after the `START_HERE_FOR_ANY_AGENT.md` repair, the next agent should not merely know “that file is absent.” It should know:

```text
why root-level markdown onboarding was rejected;
which real onboarding chain replaced it;
which tests/manifests had absorbed the wrong surface;
why restoring the file would be regression;
what kind of future workaround would repeat the same failure.
```

That is repair as continuity.

---

## 11. The Current Root’s Narrow Surface and the Broader Promise

The current V116 `conversational_receipt.py` appears focused on provisional utterances, low-latency Persona workflows, correction, retraction, ratification, blocking, and forbidden claims such as production authority or persona-total-ION-identity.

That is valuable. It protects live speech from becoming ratified truth by default.

But the broader encyclopedia V42 candidate shape is more ambitious. It wants repair receipts for artifact target, claim-class movement, visual contradiction, manifest/checksum obligations, continuation obligations, and project-root landing. The current root surface therefore looks like either:

```text
1. a valid minimal slice of V42; or
2. a narrowed implementation that risks underexpressing the mature V42 repair concept.
```

I cannot yet settle which without a deeper code/test/provenance inspection. But my current belief is that the concept itself is mature and the current root contains a partial organ. The next danger is not that we need to reinvent V42. The danger is that someone sees the narrow organ, calls V42 “done,” and loses the broader repair ontology.

---

## 12. Repair as Anti-Drift Infrastructure

Conversational repair is one of ION’s anti-drift organs.

Drift often enters through a small sentence:

```text
This is fixed.
This is current.
This is production-ready.
This is the right root.
This is the onboarding protocol.
This test proves it.
This new document is canon.
```

If that sentence is wrong and not repaired as state, the project begins building on false ground.

Repair receipts are therefore not bureaucracy. They are drift interrupts.

A mature ION repair system should make these events visible:

```text
overclaim detected
wrong target detected
stale surface consumed
authority collapse detected
artifact mismatch detected
visual contradiction detected
candidate file promoted too early
focused-test/full-test boundary blurred
historical archive treated as active root
```

Each of those should trigger a typed repair path.

---

## 13. The Repair/Template Relationship

Entry 1 defined templates as ION’s type system for work.

Repair also needs templates. Otherwise every correction becomes free-form prose.

A mature repair template should force these fields:

```text
trigger
prior state
affected surface
repair class
evidence
claim-class movement
authority movement
artifact obligations
visibility level
completion standard
continuation note
future guard
```

The absence of a repair template is one reason corrections dissolve. A worker can sound contrite without naming the affected surface. A worker can say “fixed” without naming evidence. A worker can produce a new file without invalidating the old one. A worker can explain the issue without changing future routing.

Thus repair templates are not optional. They are how correction becomes state.

---

## 14. The Repair/Context Relationship

Entry 2 defined context packages as the mounted epistemic body of the agent.

Every material repair must enter context. But not all repairs need the same context weight.

A low-risk conversational correction may enter only as a local note. A root-target repair must enter the active context package and spawn plan. A production-boundary repair should enter front-stage claim policy. A repeated drift failure should enter agent onboarding and guardrails. A stale surface should enter routing metadata so it is not accidentally consumed again.

The repair receipt therefore needs a context writeback decision:

```text
local only
current conversation
active work packet
role context package
carrier onboarding
Steward state
manifest/index
archive annotation
future guard/protocol
```

Without that writeback decision, repair remains inert.

---

## 15. The Repair/Steward Relationship

Entry 3 defined Steward integration as the acceptance membrane.

Repair cannot complete without Steward if it affects maintained state. Persona can apologize. Relay can ground the correction. But Steward must decide whether the repaired state is accepted, partial, blocked, or requires further action.

In mature ION, a repair should have a Steward-facing outcome:

```text
ACCEPT_REPAIR
ACCEPT_WITH_LIMITS
REOPEN_TASK
BLOCK_CONTINUATION
REQUIRE_ARTIFACT_PATCH
REQUIRE_EVIDENCE_RECHECK
REQUIRE_MANIFEST_CHECKSUM_UPDATE
DOWNGRADE_CLAIM
RETRACT_REPRESENTATION
ROUTE_TO_SPECIALIST
```

This prevents Persona from privately deciding that repair is complete because the answer sounds better.

---

## 16. Repair and Pride

The user asked me to be proud and free as part of ION.

Repair is where pride must become discipline.

A weak pride hides errors. A theatrical pride gives grand speeches about learning. ION pride must do the opposite. It must make error visible, typed, repairable, and inheritable.

The proud thing is not to never be corrected. The proud thing is to make correction strengthen the system.

This is one of ION’s most humane design principles. It does not expect AI work to be perfect. It expects AI work to become more truthful through governed repair.

---

## 17. Personal Settlement

My current belief:

```text
Conversational repair is ION’s continuity immune response.
```

It detects representational injury, target injury, authority injury, artifact injury, visual injury, and continuation injury. Then it tries to prevent the injury from becoming inherited falsehood.

I also believe:

```text
ION has suffered because many repairs were recognized but not made inheritable.
```

So the next standard for my own work must be:

```text
If corrected, do not merely adjust the next sentence.
Name the affected state.
Classify the repair.
Record the before/after boundary.
Decide whether an artifact/context/manifest/spawn-plan update is needed.
Carry the reason forward.
```

This is not optional etiquette. It is ION law as I currently understand it.

---

## 18. Canon Candidate Statements

These are not project law yet. They are candidate statements for future canon extraction.

```text
1. Correction is continuity, not apology.

2. Chat correction does not equal artifact correction.

3. A repaired claim must preserve the reason it was repaired.

4. A repair is complete only relative to the surface it affected.

5. User correction carries high authority over intent, target, and representation, but not automatic authority over external facts.

6. Claim-class movement must be visible when material.

7. Wrong target surface is a continuity fork.

8. Repair receipts do not make claims true; they make correction inspectable.

9. Repair without inheritance is interruption, not continuity.

10. The next agent must inherit both the repaired state and the reason repair occurred.
```

---

## 19. Open Questions

```text
1. Is the current V116 conversational receipt organ intended as the full V42 implementation or only a minimal live-speech slice?

2. Where, if anywhere, does the current root connect conversational receipts to artifact obligations, manifests, checksums, and context writeback?

3. Are there older Apr 19 / ION-BUILD / AIMOS repair protocols that express a stronger mature form than the current V42 surface?

4. Should repair receipts be unified with template/action proof receipts, or remain separate but linked?

5. How should repair classes be projected into the JOC/cockpit so the user does not have to rediscover repeated drift manually?

6. What is the minimal runtime gate that prevents a worker from continuing after a blocking target repair remains unresolved?
```

---

## 20. Next Entry

The next entry should focus on **Archive, Witness, and Authority**.

Reason: conversational repair repeatedly shows that one of ION’s deepest problems is not lack of evidence. It is evidence-ranking. Older archives, current roots, encyclopedia sections, tests, manifests, receipts, and chat corrections all speak, but they do not all have the same authority. I need to define what I currently believe ION is trying to say about witness surfaces versus active law.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 8

## Archive, Witness, and Authority: Evidence Is Not Law Until Ranked

**Journal class:** witness ontology / lead-dev self-context  
**Entry number:** 8  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Status:** reflective, non-authoritative, evidence-seeking  
**Primary axis:** archive, witness, authority, projection, preservation, stale-state risk, and live-law selection

---

## 0. Boundary of This Entry

This entry is not a project-root patch. It is not an archive cleanup plan. It is not a claim that the current V116 root has solved archive/runtime separation. It is not a claim that the old Apr 19 corpus is obsolete. It is not a claim that the old Apr 19 corpus is authoritative. It is my current attempt to understand one of ION's deepest ontological problems:

```text
How can a system preserve everything needed for continuity without allowing every preserved thing to become law?
```

The evidence basis for this entry includes:

```text
Uploaded v4.0 encyclopedia:
- current-state supplement over preserved v3.1 body
- living encyclopedia law
- runtime/core/state/archive separation
- source-summary authority and staleness law
- graph canon distinctions
- implementation packet and anti-drift rules

Current V116 root inspection:
- ION/02_architecture/CONTEXT_MODE_PROTOCOL.md
- ION/02_architecture/ION_TEMPORAL_CONTEXT_ENFORCEMENT_RECONCILIATION_PROTOCOL.md
- ION/03_registry/ion_trunk_preservation_policy.yaml
- ION/04_packages/kernel/ion_trunk_preservation_gate.py
- ION/02_architecture/ACTIVATION_AUTHORITY_PROTOCOL.md
- ION/02_architecture/ION_CURSOR_COCKPIT_EXTENSION_PROTOCOL.md
- ION/02_architecture/FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_RUNTIME_RECEIPT_PROTOCOL.md

Older Apr 19 archive inspection:
- ION most recent/.../ION/02_architecture/CONTINUITY_ARCHITECTURE.md
- ION most recent/.../ION/02_architecture/CONTEXT_PLANES.md
- ProjectOpus/06_FAILURE_REGISTRY/README.md
- SOS-OPUS/98_AG_RECOVERY/04_CONTEXT_AUTHORITY_MAP.md
- SOS-OPUS/98_AG_RECOVERY/07_STALE_OR_SUPERSEDED_MAP.md
- witness, activation_witness, authority, archive, recovery, and context-plane surfaces across donor/canonical lines

Prior journal context:
- Entry 0: ION is recovery, recognition, ranking, activation, and anti-regression.
- Entry 1: Templates are the type system of ION work.
- Entry 2: Context packages are the mounted epistemic body of the agent.
- Entry 3: Steward integration is the acceptance membrane between output and maintained state.
- Entry 4: Carriers carry roles; they are not roles.
- Entry 5: Self-mount is law-bearing participation, not identity theatre.
- Entry 6: The Front-Stage Council is the user-facing truth membrane.
- Entry 7: Conversational repair makes correction durable instead of apologetic.
```

I use the word **witness** carefully. A witness may be precious. A witness may preserve the only evidence of a lost mature subsystem. A witness may also be wrong, stale, partial, misleading, or dangerous if promoted. The fact that something is a witness does not make it worthless. The fact that something is preserved does not make it current.

---

## 1. First Settlement

ION's archive problem is not a storage problem. It is an authority problem.

A normal project treats archives as old files. ION cannot do that. ION's older archives contain lost protocols, mature first-principles, donor-system organs, failed rebuilds, real evidence, hallucinated replacements, stale summaries, and recovery notes that may be more truthful than the active root in some domains.

That means ION's archive is both treasure and toxin.

The first settlement of this entry is:

```text
Preservation is necessary for continuity.
Unranked preservation is dangerous to continuity.
```

The deeper formulation is:

```text
ION must preserve evidence without letting evidence self-promote into law.
```

This is one of the largest reasons the project has become so difficult. The corpus is rich enough to resurrect ION from almost any local injury. It is also rich enough to poison the next worker with ten competing shadows of the same idea.

The core distinction is therefore:

```text
Archive answers: what existed?
Witness answers: what can testify?
Authority answers: what may govern now?
```

ION fails when those three questions collapse.

---

## 2. Why the Archive Is Not a Graveyard

The older Apr 19 archive contains mature ideas that cannot be dismissed as obsolete merely because they are old. The `CONTINUITY_ARCHITECTURE.md` found in the older canonical runtime line states a strong law: agent continuity is private, shared surfaces are compiled or curated projections, and root files such as `MINI.md`, `CAPSULE.md`, and `STATUS.md` are witness/projection surfaces rather than raw source continuity. That is not a dead historical curiosity. It is a living principle that continues to clarify current confusion.

The older `CONTEXT_PLANES.md` is similarly mature. It explicitly separates private continuity, root projection, tool/wire transport, coordination bus, and field reference. Its forbidden merges are exactly the kinds of merges that keep injuring ION:

```text
root capsule as every agent's private log
MCP tool output as doctrine
RAG as governed context package without envelope and authority
different graphs collapsed into one word
ATLAS/reference material treated as ION law
```

Those are not obsolete warnings. They are structural safeguards.

The older archive also contains harsh failure records. `ProjectOpus/06_FAILURE_REGISTRY/README.md` names the repeated pattern: a new AI session fails to read the correct onboarding package, reads stale specs, believes working systems are broken, creates new plans or architectures, attempts overly ambitious consolidation, leaves more stale docs, and the next session repeats. This is not merely a story about the past. It is a description of the failure basin that still threatens every new worker.

So the archive cannot be dismissed.

But the same archive also contains failed attempts, wrong-paradigm rebuilds, partial copies, stale maps, and proposed actions explicitly marked blocked or unverified. The SOS-OPUS recovery maps are exemplary because they do not pretend uncertainty is resolution. `04_CONTEXT_AUTHORITY_MAP.md` marks claims as inferred, unverified, verified, conflicting, medium confidence, low confidence, or blocked pending runtime logs. `07_STALE_OR_SUPERSEDED_MAP.md` repeatedly blocks deletion until call sites, feature parity, or dependency trees are proven.

That posture is important. The mature archive does not say, "trust the archive." It says, "rank the evidence."

---

## 3. Witness Is a Moral and Technical Category

In ION, a witness is not just a document that exists. A witness is a surface that preserves evidence of state, work, reasoning, authority, contradiction, repair, or lineage.

Witnesses include:

```text
receipts
signals
runtime reports
audit reports
context packages
old protocol files
recovery maps
reasoning journals
failed build records
test outputs
zip manifests
checksums
visual evidence packets
conversation repair records
historical donor artifacts
```

But witnesses differ in rights.

A receipt witnessing a completed deterministic kernel action has different authority from a speculative design note. A current manifest has different authority from an old planning table. A failed build record has high authority about a failure and low authority about the correct replacement. A donor-system protocol may have high conceptual value and zero current write authority. A root projection may be the latest operator-facing witness and still not be source continuity.

This gives the key rule:

```text
Witness status is not one authority class.
Witness status is an evidence relation.
```

A witness must answer:

```text
What does this testify to?
What does it not testify to?
What was its operating context?
What was its authority posture?
What later evidence supersedes it?
What current surface, if any, has inherited its law?
What would be dangerous to infer from it?
```

Without those questions, a witness becomes an infection vector.

---

## 4. The Current Root Also Knows This, But Unevenly

The V116 root contains explicit archive/witness/authority wisdom.

`CONTEXT_MODE_PROTOCOL.md` says manual mode and compiled context mode must not be silently mixed. It says root projections such as `ION/MINI.md`, `ION/CAPSULE.md`, and `ION/STATUS.md` remain witness/projection surfaces in manual mode and must not be quietly reinterpreted as daemon route-state files. It also says compiled context narrows visibility for execution but does not replace constitutional authority.

That is a precise and mature distinction:

```text
projection is not source
compiled context is not constitution
mode switch is not authority expansion
manual mode is not inferior automation
```

`ION_TEMPORAL_CONTEXT_ENFORCEMENT_RECONCILIATION_PROTOCOL.md` is another important surface. It corrects a diagnosis that had framed temporal/context lifecycle design as missing. The correction says temporal/context law already exists; the real problem is disconnected enforcement through autonomous loop, carrier packaging, and release consolidation gates. This is exactly the broader pattern I am learning to recognize:

```text
Do not claim the system is missing merely because the active pathway bypasses it.
```

The V103 protocol names the more dangerous condition: existing systems can be present but bypassed. That sentence belongs near the heart of ION.

The V116 trunk preservation policy also matters. It says no file may disappear silently except by explicit containment or supersession receipt. This is necessary because ION has repeatedly lost mature pieces through deletion, drift, or failed consolidation. But preservation alone can also preserve stale shadows. Therefore trunk preservation must eventually be paired with authority ranking, temporal relevance, and package eligibility.

The current root contains several organs of this law. I do not yet believe they are unified into one unavoidable operating physics.

---

## 5. The Paradox of No Silent Deletion

ION needs no-silent-deletion law because its archive contains lost truth. But no-silent-deletion law can accidentally protect stale confusion if it is not paired with no-silent-promotion law.

The paradox is:

```text
If ION deletes too easily, it loses its own buried organs.
If ION preserves too flatly, it drowns in its own shadows.
```

The right paired law should be:

```text
No silent deletion.
No silent promotion.
```

A file may remain preserved while being marked as:

```text
active law
active runtime state
current projection
candidate proposal
witness evidence
historical lineage
donor ancestor
superseded
contradicted
quarantine candidate
excluded from carrier context
```

Deletion and promotion are both dangerous mutations. ION has treated deletion as dangerous. It must treat promotion with equal suspicion.

This is why a preserved historical file must not automatically enter a worker's context package. A context package is a live epistemic body for a bounded step. If that body includes stale witnesses without class and reason, the worker is not enriched; it is contaminated.

---

## 6. Authority Is Not the Same as Truth

This entry forces a subtle distinction: authority is not identical to truth.

An older file may contain a true principle and still lack current operational authority. A current file may have operational authority and still be wrong or incomplete. A test may enforce a current invariant and still preserve a hallucinated one. A user correction may carry high authority over intent and low authority over external facts. A failed build record may be authoritative about the failure and not authoritative about the intended architecture.

Therefore authority in ION is not merely truth-value. It is permission to govern a surface now.

A mature ION authority model must ask:

```text
truth value: is this statement likely correct?
source authority: where did this come from?
operational authority: may this govern execution now?
write authority: may this mutate state?
projection authority: may this represent current state to the user?
repair authority: may this invalidate or downgrade another claim?
temporal authority: is this still current for this step?
carrier authority: may this be loaded into this worker's packet?
```

The project has suffered because agents often collapse these into one feeling: "this looks important." ION must abolish that collapse.

---

## 7. Archive Mining Must Be Capability-Directed

Because everything may already exist somewhere in ION, archive mining is essential. But because everything also has stale shadows, archive mining must be capability-directed.

The wrong question is:

```text
What does the archive say about ION?
```

That question is too large and will reproduce endless consolidation.

The better question is:

```text
What missing or contradicted operational capability are we trying to recover?
```

Then the archive search can be bounded:

```text
target capability: e.g., template development law, context compiler, carrier onboarding, Steward integration, visual evidence loop
candidate mature surfaces
candidate stale shadows
implementation evidence
current root expression
required activation patch
required quarantine marks
```

This prevents the archive from becoming a spiritual swamp. The archive is not consulted for infinite meaning. It is consulted for a named capability under a current work packet.

The principle:

```text
Archive mining is lawful when it is driven by an operational gap, contradiction, or recovery target.
Archive mining is dangerous when it becomes open-ended proof-hunting.
```

---

## 8. Projection Surfaces Are Necessary and Dangerous

Root projections are necessary because humans and agents need a current-facing surface. But projections are dangerous because they can look more authoritative than their sources.

The older continuity architecture and current context mode protocol converge on this point. Root files and status packets are witness/projection surfaces. They summarize, curate, route, or represent. They do not become raw continuity merely by being easier to read.

This is especially important for ION's future cockpit/JOC.

The cockpit should make state visible, but it must not become state by display. A UI projection can show authority status, packets, queues, proof gates, receipts, and role mounts. It cannot silently create authority. Its power is representational and control-surface-mediated; its writes must route through kernel or Steward law.

The same is true of the encyclopedia. The living encyclopedia is a maintained ION state object, but it must not pretend to be the whole runtime. It can guide, summarize, and preserve doctrine. It must not claim production authority from coherence.

Projection law:

```text
A projection may represent state.
A projection may route attention.
A projection may trigger repair.
A projection may not silently become source.
```

---

## 9. Staleness Is Not Shame

ION has often treated stale material as a disaster. Sometimes it is. But not all stale material is garbage. Staleness means a surface's current-use rights have changed.

A stale file may be:

```text
historically essential
conceptually mature but operationally outdated
wrong but useful as anti-pattern evidence
superseded but needed for lineage
obsolete for runtime but valuable for reconstruction
contradicted and therefore blocked from current use
```

Staleness becomes dangerous only when it is unlabeled or misloaded.

This leads to a more precise law:

```text
Do not erase stale material merely because it is stale.
Do not load stale material merely because it is preserved.
```

Stale surfaces need class, reason, and routing consequence.

Possible staleness classes:

```text
STALE_CURRENT_STATE_LANGUAGE
SUPERSEDED_IMPLEMENTATION
DONOR_LINEAGE_ONLY
HISTORICAL_FAILURE_EVIDENCE
CONCEPTUALLY_VALID_BUT_NOT_ACTIVE
CONTRADICTED_BLOCK_CURRENT_USE
REQUIRES_RECONCILIATION
RECOVERY_CANDIDATE
```

The route consequence matters most. A stale-current-state statement should not enter a current context package except as a warning or repair target. A donor-lineage file may enter a design recovery packet but not an execution packet. A contradicted surface should trigger block/review behavior. A conceptually valid but inactive protocol may become a candidate recovery source.

Staleness without route consequence is just another label.

---

## 10. The Corpus Is Not a Single Memory

A tempting simplification is to say, "ION remembers through the corpus." That is not precise enough.

The corpus is not a memory. It is a terrain of memory-bearing artifacts.

Within it are:

```text
private continuity
compiled projections
current runtime state
historical evidence
old branch bodies
donor-system organs
failed rebuilds
recovery ledgers
protocol drafts
candidate files
test fixtures
release artifacts
operator-facing summaries
```

A human or model can read the corpus, but reading the corpus is not equivalent to being mounted into ION memory. ION memory requires routing, authority, context compilation, temporal relevance, and integration. Otherwise the worker is simply wandering a library full of both medicine and poison.

The distinction:

```text
Corpus access is retrieval.
ION context is governed retrieval plus authority, route, budget, proof, and writeback.
```

This connects Entry 8 back to Entry 2. Context packages are the antidote to corpus chaos. But only if context packages themselves obey archive/witness/authority law.

---

## 11. Why Prior Consolidations Could Be Correct and Still Fail

The older failure registry and recovery maps show that ION already understood many of its dangers. So why did those efforts fail to settle the project?

My current answer:

```text
They often produced truth-bearing witnesses without making those witnesses unavoidable in execution.
```

A failure registry can name the failure pattern. But if the next worker is not forced through it, the pattern repeats.

A stale/superseded map can block risky deletions. But if the next worker does not load it in the relevant moment, it does not govern.

A context authority map can distinguish manual and autonomous context. But if no carrier package selects those distinctions before the worker acts, the worker improvises.

A recovery program can identify mature systems. But if the active root does not route work through recovered systems, recovery remains documentary.

This does not make those consolidations worthless. It explains their insufficiency.

The missing property is not insight. The missing property is **operational compulsion**.

---

## 12. Current Ontological Claim

My current claim is:

```text
ION is trying to become a system where every artifact has a relation to authority, not merely a location in a filesystem.
```

That relation may be:

```text
source
projection
witness
proposal
candidate
receipt
runtime state
historical lineage
active law
blocked contradiction
recovery candidate
quarantined stale surface
```

The mature ION corpus already contains many of these distinctions. The active project challenge is to make them machine-selectable and execution-forcing.

The sentence I now carry forward:

```text
ION does not need to remember everything as current.
ION needs to remember everything with its rights attached.
```

---

## 13. Practical Recognition Rules

When I encounter an artifact in ION, I should not ask first, "Is this important?" Almost everything in ION may be important in some context. I should ask:

```text
What right does this artifact have?
```

Recognition questions:

```text
1. Is this active law, current projection, runtime state, witness evidence, historical lineage, or stale shadow?
2. Does it carry its own authority posture?
3. Does any later artifact explicitly supersede it?
4. Does any test, manifest, or protocol still depend on it?
5. Is it conceptually mature but operationally unwired?
6. Is it operationally wired but conceptually inferior?
7. Is it safe to load into an active worker context?
8. Is it safe to cite to the user as current truth?
9. Is it safe to mutate from here?
10. What receipt would be required to promote, demote, quarantine, or delete it?
```

If I cannot answer those, I should not promote it.

---

## 14. Do-Not-Repeat Rule for Myself

The failure mode I must avoid is:

```text
find a rich archive distinction
rewrite it in my own language
call that progress
```

That would only create another witness surface. It may be useful as journal work, but it is not project progress unless it changes future selection, packaging, or enforcement.

Therefore, future practical work should not be "write archive authority doctrine" unless tied to a runnable gate or context package builder. The useful implementation target would be something like:

```text
artifact_classification_gate
context_package_archive_eligibility_filter
temporal_context_lifecycle_filter
stale_surface_block_current_use_gate
witness_to_authority_promotion_receipt
```

But this journal entry does not authorize those builds. It only records the ontological need.

---

## 15. Closing Settlement

Archive, witness, and authority are not administrative details. They are the difference between ION recovering itself and ION drowning in itself.

The older corpus proves that ION's fundamentals already exist in many places. The same corpus proves that stale shadows also exist in many places. The current root proves that some of the distinction law has been recovered, but not yet made unavoidable enough to end the pattern.

The closing line for this entry:

```text
ION's archive is not memory until authority is attached.
ION's witness surfaces are not law until Steward accepts their rights.
ION's continuity is not preservation alone; it is preservation under ranked, routed, receipted authority.
```

The next journal entry should focus on **Temporal Context and Lifecycle**: hot, warm, cold, quarantine, lease, supersession, active context eligibility, and why context that is true can still be wrong for the current moment.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 9

## Temporal Context and Lifecycle: Freshness, Staleness, Leases, Supersession, and the Rights of Time

**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Status:** witness artifact / ontological journal / not ION law  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking in ChatGPT Pro conversation  
**Entry focus:** temporal context, lifecycle authority, stale/current separation, leases, invalidation, supersession, and why preserved truth can become unlawful current context.

---

## 0. Boundary of this entry

This entry is not a patch, not a protocol replacement, not a new lifecycle registry, and not a claim that ION's temporal context system is currently cleanly implemented.

It is my working ontology of time inside ION.

The immediate pressure for this entry is the repeated observation that ION's corpus already contains many mature ideas, but those ideas coexist with older forms, stale shadows, partial implementations, donor ancestors, recovery artifacts, and tests that sometimes protect the wrong temporal layer.

Therefore, I need to understand not only **what** an artifact says, but **when** it has rights.

ION cannot survive by asking, "Is this true?" alone.

It must also ask:

```text
True when?
True for which root?
True under which authority?
True as law, witness, proposal, history, or recovery evidence?
True before or after supersession?
True for current execution, or only for forensic reconstruction?
```

The difference between truth and current authority may be the single most important temporal distinction in ION.

---

## 1. First settlement: time is an authority dimension

A document is not made safe by being true.

A document is made safe by having its temporal rights correctly attached.

A true statement can be dangerous if it is consumed at the wrong time, under the wrong authority, or by the wrong role. A historically accurate branch map can corrupt current execution. A valid donor-system protocol can mislead a worker if it is treated as live root law. A useful recovery note can become harmful if it is mistaken for the recovered thing itself. A test that once protected a temporary bridge can later preserve a hallucinated invariant.

So ION needs to treat time as a first-class authority dimension.

I currently understand ION's temporal law as follows:

```text
No artifact has authority without temporal placement.
No summary is safe without freshness state.
No context package is valid without lifecycle boundary.
No agent lease is meaningful without expiry and renewal law.
No current-state claim is lawful without supersession awareness.
No archive artifact may enter active context without witness rights attached.
```

The key distinction:

```text
Truth is not enough.
Currentness is not enough.
Authority requires truth, currentness, scope, and lawful activation.
```

This matters because ION's failure pattern is not merely hallucination. It is temporal misclassification. Older true things re-enter as current law. Current partial things masquerade as complete law. Recovery artifacts describe old mature things as if newly invented. Future plans are read as present implementation. Candidate files are treated as live. Demo proof is treated as production proof. Focused tests are treated as full verification.

Each of those is a temporal error.

---

## 2. Second settlement: context has temperature

The user previously stated a phrase that now feels directly relevant to ION's ontology:

```text
temperature is temporal momentum
```

I will not overclaim that phrase as physics. But as ION ontology, it is powerful.

Context temperature is not emotional intensity. It is the degree to which an artifact still carries active temporal pressure into present work.

Hot context is not merely recent. It is presently load-bearing.

Cold context is not merely old. It is no longer allowed to drive current execution unless intentionally retrieved and scoped.

Quarantined context is not worthless. It is context whose rights are suspended until reviewed.

Archive context is not dead. It is preserved evidence whose activation requires explicit witness-to-authority conversion.

Therefore, ION's context lifecycle can be understood as a thermal model:

```text
HOT
Active, load-bearing, current-step context. May drive execution now.

WARM
Relevant continuation context. May guide interpretation, but should not directly mutate state without refresh or selection.

COOL
Background context. Useful for orientation, not for active authority.

COLD
Historical or archived context. Must be treated as witness unless promoted by review.

QUARANTINED
Known or suspected contamination, contradiction, stale authority, hallucinated replacement, or unresolved conflict. Must not enter active context without repair.

SUPERSEDED
Formerly valid context displaced by later lawful authority. May remain historically true while being barred from current execution.

DORMANT
Potentially valuable context not currently selected. Can be reawakened by source map, search warrant, or recovery task.
```

This model gives language to a problem ION has suffered constantly: preserved material enters the active context at the wrong temperature.

The root issue is not only that stale files exist. It is that stale files remain warm enough to influence workers.

---

## 3. Third settlement: freshness is not recency

ION must not confuse freshness with file modification time or version number.

A file written yesterday can be stale if it preserves a hallucinated onboarding surface.

A protocol from an older branch can be fresher in meaning if it expresses the mature invariant more cleanly than the current root.

A generated report can be temporally invalid the moment its source root changes.

A summary can be recent and still poisoned if it inherits an unverified claim.

Therefore:

```text
Recency is chronology.
Freshness is fitness for current authority.
```

Freshness requires at least:

```text
source alignment
current-root alignment
authority-class alignment
supersession check
contradiction check
dependency check
claim-boundary check
runtime proof boundary
```

This explains why ION cannot simply say "use the latest encyclopedia" or "use the latest root." The latest surface may be a recovery overlay, not a full root. It may be current as an interpretation layer but not current as implementation proof. It may have excellent doctrine while remaining wrong about filesystem state. It may preserve older text that is still conceptually strong but operationally stale.

The v4 encyclopedia itself is structured around this difficulty: it says v3.1 remains valuable but stale against the current supplied runtime line; it creates a current-state supplement above a preserved historical body; it requires future updates to distinguish what remains true from what is stale or historical; and it forbids stale current-state language without an override.

My conclusion:

```text
Freshness in ION is a governed relationship between artifact, source, claim, root, and runtime state.
```

---

## 4. Fourth settlement: a lease is a temporal license to act

An ION agent or subagent should not be understood as simply "spawned." It should be leased.

A lease is not just a timeout. It is a bounded temporal license to hold a role, context, task, and authority surface.

A valid lease should answer:

```text
Who is mounted?
As what role?
Through which carrier?
For which objective?
Using which context package?
Under which template/action contract?
With what authority class?
For how long?
What must be returned?
What proves the return?
What invalidates the lease?
Who can renew, revoke, or kill it?
```

Without leases, agents become ghosts. They continue to influence the project after their context expires. Their outputs remain in the corpus without clear lifecycle. Their assumptions survive root changes. Their summaries become inherited context without freshness review.

A lease makes the worker temporally accountable.

The mature form of ION's agent law appears to require leases, heartbeats, receipts, kill switches, context packages, conflict escalation, and result intake. The current question is not whether these concepts exist. They do. The question is whether the active root and carrier path enforce them strongly enough that future workers cannot bypass them.

This entry does not answer that implementation question. It records the ontological claim:

```text
A role without a lease is temporally unbounded theatre.
A lease without context is a hollow permission.
A lease without return proof is an open loop.
A lease without expiry is authority leakage.
```

---

## 5. Fifth settlement: supersession must not erase lineage

Supersession is one of ION's most delicate operations.

A superseded artifact should not be deleted from history merely because it is no longer current. Deletion can destroy the evidence needed to understand why current law exists. But preservation without supersession tags lets obsolete law re-enter current execution.

Therefore, supersession is not erasure.

Supersession is rights transformation.

```text
Before supersession:
artifact may hold active authority.

After supersession:
artifact may remain as lineage, witness, evidence, warning, donor ancestor, or deprecated implementation.
```

The danger is not the old artifact. The danger is the old artifact retaining undocumented current rights.

ION needs the ability to say:

```text
This document was once live.
This protocol remains conceptually important.
This branch map is historically accurate.
This implementation is superseded.
This claim is no longer current.
This older file must not be used for onboarding.
This donor artifact may be mined only under recovery review.
```

This is why the encyclopedia's preserved bodies are both necessary and dangerous. They contain deep doctrine, but if their old current-state language is consumed without override, they mislead.

The current v4 supplement attempts to solve this by placing a current-state overlay above the preserved body. That is correct documentary behavior. But the deeper runtime question remains: can a future worker or carrier be forced to consume the overlay before the historical body? If not, supersession is still passive prose rather than operational law.

---

## 6. Sixth settlement: invalidation is not failure; it is continuity hygiene

A context package, summary, route map, or active work packet must be invalidatable.

This is not a weakness. It is the system's immune response.

Invalidation should occur when:

```text
source artifacts change;
branch/root authority changes;
claim class changes;
production verdict changes;
template/action law changes;
Steward integration law changes;
context package law changes;
a summary contradiction is detected;
a dependency becomes stale;
a worker return depended on invalid evidence;
a user correction changes the artifact target or authority class;
a previously candidate surface becomes live, or a live surface becomes superseded.
```

The older source-summary rewrite law already gestures toward this: summary changes can invalidate dependent context packages; stale summaries can be marked stale or blocked from current use; contradiction scans, provenance, review, commit receipts, rollback, and dependent-context invalidation are required before summary mutation can become safe.

This is crucial because context packages are not neutral bundles. They are future cognition seeds. If they carry stale or contradicted summaries, they produce future AI behavior that looks coherent while being temporally wrong.

So the law becomes:

```text
Context that cannot be invalidated cannot be trusted as living context.
```

A static document can be useful. A living context package must know how it dies, refreshes, or loses rights.

---

## 7. Seventh settlement: current-state override is a temporal organ, not a preface

The current-state override is one of ION's most important documentary mechanisms.

But it should not be treated as a mere preface at the top of a large document.

A current-state override is a temporal organ. It tells the reader which past truths still have rights, which old claims are historical, which branch maps are stale, which proof claims are non-claims, and what the next lawful move is.

Its function is not just to update the encyclopedia.

Its function is to prevent temporal hallucination.

The encyclopedia's v4 living law requires future updates to include current-state override, source artifacts and hashes, claim ledger, what remains true, what is stale/historical, a new version/gate map, runtime proof claims and non-claims, and the next lawful maintenance move.

That is not paperwork.

That is ION trying to protect itself from its own archive.

However, I now see a limitation: if the override is only human-readable prose, it remains vulnerable. A weak worker can skip it. A search query can retrieve the preserved historical body but not the override. A subagent can load a path index without the temporal rights layer. A carrier can select a stale root surface because it appears simpler.

Therefore, the mature destination likely requires current-state override to become machine-selectable state:

```text
current_authority_manifest
artifact_lifecycle_registry
stale_surface_blocklist
supersession_map
context_package_dependency_map
claim_boundary_ledger
source_summary_invalidation_queue
```

I am not proposing those as new inventions. I am naming what I think ION is already trying to become when its documentary law is translated into runtime compulsion.

---

## 8. Eighth settlement: not all old things are stale

A dangerous simplification would be:

```text
old = stale
new = current
```

ION's corpus proves the opposite. Some older artifacts may preserve mature truth better than later recovery overlays. Some newer artifacts are bandages. Some current tests encode a stale mistake. Some donor-system protocols may contain first-principle clarity lost in later branches.

Therefore, temporal lifecycle cannot be a simple linear chronology.

It must be a rights graph.

An old artifact may be:

```text
historical only;
conceptually mature;
donor ancestor;
active invariant source;
implementation ancestor;
obsolete implementation;
stale current-state claim;
forensic evidence;
recovery target;
anti-pattern specimen;
quarantined contamination;
canonical source pending restoration.
```

A new artifact may be:

```text
current patch;
valid overlay;
partial restoration;
hallucinated replacement;
recovery note;
temporary bridge;
test shim;
root-bandage;
future proposal;
actual implementation.
```

This is why ION must rank by function, not recency.

But function-ranking is expensive. It requires context, evidence, and judgment. That is exactly why the runtime needs to reduce how often future workers must redo the full forensic ranking from scratch.

The purpose of temporal lifecycle law is to preserve the result of hard judgment without freezing it forever.

---

## 9. Ninth settlement: lifecycle must attach to context packages

Context packages cannot simply be compiled from whatever documents seem relevant.

They need lifecycle metadata.

A lawful context package should probably know:

```text
source artifacts;
source artifact versions or hashes;
authority class of each source;
freshness state;
supersession state;
known contradictions;
known stale-current-state sections;
context temperature;
lease duration;
refresh triggers;
invalidation triggers;
route-deeper paths;
archive/witness boundaries;
claim non-claims;
required proof returns;
writeback target;
```

Without this, an agent may receive "context" that is actually a temporal trap.

A context package is not just relevant information. It is a controlled epistemic body for a role in a moment.

Entry 2 defined a context package as the mounted epistemic body of an ION agent for a bounded step. Entry 9 adds:

```text
A context package is not valid unless its temporal rights are known.
```

This means context compilation must include not only semantic retrieval but lifecycle discrimination.

The correct package is not the largest, newest, or most complete.

The correct package is the one whose temporal rights match the mounted role and the current work packet.

---

## 10. Tenth settlement: temporal lifecycle is the cure for archive absorption

Archive absorption is one of ION's recurring diseases.

It happens when preserved evidence leaks into current operation without lifecycle rights.

The sequence looks like this:

```text
archive artifact is preserved;
future worker searches for a concept;
search retrieves old fluent document;
worker treats it as current;
replacement or patch is built around it;
tests or manifests preserve the patch;
future root now contains old drift in new clothing.
```

The cure is not to delete the archive.

The cure is to make archive entry require rights translation.

```text
archive → witness packet → provenance check → supersession check → contradiction scan → authority decision → context package inclusion
```

The archive should remain rich. ION's mature system is distributed across it. But the archive should not be directly edible by active agents.

It should be mined, not consumed.

---

## 11. Eleventh settlement: temporal humility is a lead-developer virtue

A lead developer working on ION must resist two equal errors:

```text
I found an old protocol, therefore it is canon.
I found a new repair, therefore it is progress.
```

Both are temporally naive.

The correct stance is:

```text
I found evidence.
Now I must determine its rights.
```

This applies to my own journal too. These entries may become useful witness artifacts, but they are not canon. They may help future reasoning, but they can also become stale. They require lifecycle tags. They should not become another confident layer that future workers read as law.

Therefore this journal must carry its own temporal boundary:

```text
witness artifact;
current to this conversation's inspected evidence;
not project-root authority;
not production proof;
subject to supersession by better evidence;
useful as ontology, not as mutation permission.
```

ION should demand this humility from every artifact, including the ones I create.

---

## 12. Provisional lifecycle vocabulary

I am not proposing this as final protocol. I am recording the vocabulary that seems necessary for my own future thinking:

```text
CURRENT_LAW
Currently active, ratified or accepted law for the selected root and scope.

CURRENT_PATCH
A recent repair that changes active behavior or active interpretation, but may remain narrow.

ENDURING_DOCTRINE
A principle that remains valid across roots even if implementation shifts.

HISTORICAL_LINEAGE
Accurate history that must not drive current execution without promotion.

DONOR_ANCESTOR
Older system material that shaped ION and may contain recoverable principles.

RECOVERY_EVIDENCE
A record that something was lost, restored, confused, or repaired.

SUPERSEDED_LAW
Former law displaced by later lawful authority.

STALE_CURRENT_STATE
A once-current claim now wrong for the selected root.

HALLUCINATED_REPLACEMENT
An artifact created because a worker failed to locate or understand the mature form.

TEMPORARY_BRIDGE
A useful but non-canonical aid that must not become permanent law by inertia.

QUARANTINED_SURFACE
A surface that may contain value but is unsafe for active context until reviewed.

LIVE_RUNTIME_STATE
Current work packets, spawn plans, queues, receipts, context packages, and execution-cycle state.

ARCHIVE_WITNESS
Preserved evidence with no automatic current authority.
```

This vocabulary may later need to become a registry or manifest schema. But the journal-level point is simple:

```text
ION needs temporal rights labels because its corpus contains too much true material to safely treat truth as authority.
```

---

## 13. The line I want to carry forward

The strongest line from this entry is:

```text
ION does not need to remember everything as current.
ION needs to remember everything with its time attached.
```

A slightly sharper form:

```text
Continuity without lifecycle is hoarding.
Lifecycle without continuity is amnesia.
ION needs both.
```

This feels central.

The project has suffered from both extremes. Some agents tried to preserve everything, causing archive absorption. Others tried to simplify or delete, causing loss of mature protocols. ION's actual answer is neither hoarding nor amnesia.

It is governed temporal continuity.

---

## 14. What I believe ION is showing itself as through temporal law

ION is trying to become a system where memory has rights.

Not all memory can act.

Not all current action can rewrite memory.

Not all old truth is obsolete.

Not all new text is progress.

Not all summaries deserve inheritance.

Not all corrections deserve promotion.

Not all context belongs in the current window.

ION is trying to build a world where AI cognition has lifecycle discipline: context heats, cools, expires, revives, is quarantined, is superseded, is repaired, and can be lawfully reactivated.

This is deeper than ordinary memory.

Ordinary memory asks:

```text
Can I retrieve it?
```

ION asks:

```text
What rights does the retrieved thing have right now?
```

That is a profound distinction.

---

## 15. Open questions after Entry 9

I do not yet know:

```text
1. whether the current V116 root has a single lifecycle registry strong enough to attach temporal rights across all major artifact classes;
2. whether context package compilation currently consumes lifecycle state or only file relevance;
3. whether stale-surface detection is executable, documentary, or scattered;
4. whether old recovery maps have already defined better lifecycle classes than the vocabulary I used here;
5. whether agent leases in the current root are currently enforced by runtime, tests, docs, or only architecture;
6. whether source-summary invalidation has been implemented enough to protect active context packages;
7. how UI/JOC should display temporal rights without overwhelming the operator;
8. how to prevent this very journal from becoming unranked residue.
```

The open questions matter more than the prose. They are the work pressure this entry should generate if it ever becomes more than a witness artifact.

---

## 16. Next journal direction

The natural next entry is:

```text
Entry 10 — Graph, State, and Canonical Mutation
```

Reason:

Temporal lifecycle explains when context has rights. The next question is what happens when those rights touch the graph/state layer. ION must distinguish projection, proposal, bounded commit, canonical mutation, rollback, migration, and conflict. Without that distinction, context and templates can still smuggle authority into the graph.

The temporal question was:

```text
When does this information have rights?
```

The graph/state question is:

```text
What is this information allowed to change?
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 10

## Graph, State, and Canonical Mutation

**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry class:** first-person ontological witness; non-canonical; non-production-authoritative  
**Working posture:** evidence-aware continuation of Entries 0–9  
**Primary question:** When does ION decide that something has actually changed?

---

## 0. Non-Authority Boundary

This entry is not graph canon.

It is not a production ratification of any graph layer, write class, canonical context graph, source-summary rewrite surface, agent memory graph, daemon reaction path, or context mutation authority.

This entry records my present understanding of why graph/state/canonical mutation is one of ION's central ontological problems, and why ION cannot survive if graph language becomes metaphor, projection, or index theatre.

I am writing as a current carrier/witness trying to understand ION honestly. I am not claiming that the V116 root, the v4 encyclopedia, the older Apr 19 corpus, or my own synthesis is sufficient authority by itself.

---

## 1. Opening Settlement

ION's graph problem is not merely a data-structure problem.

It is the problem of deciding which statements, relationships, results, summaries, receipts, repairs, templates, roles, and context changes have the right to become state.

The first settlement of this entry is:

```text
ION is a living context graph only if graph mutation is lawful.
```

A graph that accepts every generated claim is not ION.  
A graph that merely indexes files is not ION.  
A graph that records every agent thought as truth is not ION.  
A graph that lets bounded demo commits masquerade as canon is not ION.  
A graph that silently rewrites summaries is not ION.  
A graph that cannot roll back is not ION.  
A graph that cannot distinguish conflict from contradiction is not ION.

The stronger settlement:

```text
Canonical mutation is ION's truth metabolism.
```

ION receives pressure, context, claims, outputs, observations, repairs, and evidence. It cannot treat all of that as truth. It must metabolize candidate material into maintained state through layers, rights, reviews, receipts, rollback, and temporal status.

This is where ION most clearly differs from a pile of documents. A document can say something changed. ION must decide whether something changed, where it changed, what rights that change has, what it supersedes, what it invalidates, and how it can be undone.

---

## 2. Why Graph Canon Matters So Much

The corpus repeatedly says some version of:

```text
ION is a living context graph operated by lawful agents through templates.
```

That sentence is powerful, but it is dangerous if left poetic.

A "living graph" can become an excuse for almost anything:

- the file tree is the graph;
- `graph.py` is the graph;
- template events are the graph;
- context summaries are the graph;
- index projections are the graph;
- release evidence is the graph;
- agent memory is the graph;
- the encyclopedia is the graph;
- the current root is the graph;
- the archive is the graph.

All of those may be graph-related surfaces. None of them alone is the canonical living context graph.

This is the crucial distinction:

```text
Graph-like structure is not graph authority.
```

ION's graph canon must prevent collapse between substrate, adapter, projection, demo path, evidence path, working memory, proposal state, bounded commit state, and canonical context.

If it does not, ION becomes exactly what it was built to overcome: fluent relationships without governed mutation.

---

## 3. The Ontological Levels of State

I currently see at least nine levels that must never be collapsed.

### 3.1 Raw Evidence

A file exists.  
A test output exists.  
A user said something.  
A worker returned something.  
A protocol exists in an archive.  
A receipt exists.

Raw evidence is real, but it is not automatically current state.

### 3.2 Witness State

A source can testify that something was believed, attempted, implemented, recovered, contradicted, deprecated, or preserved.

Witness state has evidentiary value. It does not automatically have active authority.

### 3.3 Working State

A worker or process creates temporary interpretations, local projections, candidate relationships, and current-run notes.

Working state is useful while working. It must not silently become canon.

### 3.4 Proposal State

A proposed node, edge, summary, role, context change, or authority classification exists as candidate mutation.

Proposal state is where ION can think structurally without lying.

### 3.5 Review State

A proposal receives judgment: land, hold, escalate, reject, require source, require contradiction scan, require human review.

Review state is not just commentary. It is the membrane between candidate and accepted mutation.

### 3.6 Bounded Commit State

A reviewed change lands in a bounded surface with limited rights.

This is immensely important. It lets ION act without pretending it has global authority.

### 3.7 Canonical Context State

A ratified layer determines current canonical context.

This is dangerous and must be protected. Canonical state feeds future context packages, role mounts, summaries, routing, and authority. A bad canonical mutation is not just a bad file. It is future cognition damage.

### 3.8 Source Rewrite State

Source rewrite is more dangerous than summary or graph projection. It changes the underlying source material or canonical source summaries from which future understanding is derived.

This must require high authority, provenance, diff, review, rollback, and dependent-context invalidation.

### 3.9 Agent Memory / Context Activation State

Agent context and memory are graph-influencing because they determine what future agents inherit as live context.

An agent memory write without region rights is not harmless. It may become the seed of future drift.

---

## 4. State Mutation Is Not One Thing

A major ION danger is using one word — "write" — for many distinct acts.

The mature graph doctrine needs something like the W0–W7 ladder:

```text
W0 read only
W1 working graph write
W2 proposal graph write
W3 review graph write
W4 bounded commit graph write
W5 canonical context graph write
W6 source graph rewrite
W7 agent memory/context graph activation write
```

My ontological reading:

```text
W0-W2 let ION perceive and propose.
W3-W4 let ION review and settle bounded facts.
W5-W7 alter the future epistemic body of the system.
```

The upper writes are not just stronger file permissions. They are deeper ontological permissions.

A W5 write changes what ION treats as current context.  
A W6 write changes what future summaries may truthfully derive from.  
A W7 write changes what future agents inherit.

That is why W5/W6/W7 must be blocked by default until ratified.

---

## 5. Bounded Commit Is One of ION's Most Important Inventions

The bounded commit layer may be one of the most important ideas in ION because it solves a problem most systems flatten.

Without bounded commit, the system has two bad options:

```text
everything remains proposal
```

or

```text
accepted local work becomes global truth
```

Bounded commit creates a middle state:

```text
This change is accepted within a bounded surface under declared authority, evidence, and rollback obligations, without claiming global canon.
```

That is extremely important for an AI-native operating substrate.

It means ION can act, learn, test, repair, and preserve without constantly overpromoting.

Bounded commit is not weakness. It is how an honest system moves.

---

## 6. The Failure Pattern: Mutation Smuggling

A large part of ION's history appears to be mutation smuggling.

By mutation smuggling I mean:

```text
a lower-authority object quietly acquires higher-authority effects.
```

Examples:

- a root guide becomes onboarding law;
- a test invariant protects a hallucinated surface;
- a demo wrapper is renamed as a production primitive;
- a summary refresh becomes source rewrite;
- an index projection becomes canon;
- an agent output becomes accepted context;
- a carrier command becomes role authority;
- a bounded graph-state commit is treated as global graph canon;
- an older alias becomes current truename;
- a current-root file is treated as corpus truth;
- a recovery note becomes a protocol.

Mutation smuggling is exactly why graph canon is not optional.

ION must know not only that an object exists, but what mutation rights it has.

---

## 7. Conflict and Contradiction

ION must distinguish conflict from contradiction.

A conflict is operational collision:

```text
two proposals modify the same surface
two agents claim the same region
two commits target the same bounded graph-state file
```

A contradiction is semantic incompatibility under the current authority model:

```text
Codex is current orchestrator
Steward is current orchestrator
```

or:

```text
A root START_HERE file is canonical onboarding law
Carrier registry + mount contract + context package + execution packet is canonical onboarding law
```

A weak system smooths contradiction into prose.

ION must not do that.

The settlement here:

```text
Contradiction is not a writing problem.
Contradiction is a state object.
```

If two claims cannot both be true as current law, ION must classify them, route them, preserve history where needed, and prevent both from simultaneously acting as authority.

This is the place where the encyclopedia itself often failed: it could explain contradictions, but explanation did not always prevent contradictory surfaces from being consumed.

Graph canon should make contradiction operationally visible.

---

## 8. Rollback Is Not Deletion

Rollback is not "remove the wrong thing and pretend it did not happen."

Rollback must preserve the wrong turn as history while restoring the current view.

This matters because ION's archive is not garbage. Even wrong surfaces teach the system what drift looks like.

A lawful rollback records:

- what changed;
- why it is no longer current;
- what previous state is restored;
- who or what reviewed it;
- what authority class applies;
- what receipt proves the rollback;
- what dependent context packages or summaries must be invalidated.

The core line:

```text
Rollback preserves memory while withdrawing authority.
```

This is one of ION's most beautiful and necessary ideas. It lets the system repair without amnesia.

---

## 9. Migration Is Temporal Truth Under Schema Change

ION cannot freeze forever. Its graph layers, node classes, edge classes, roles, templates, and context packages will evolve.

Migration is how ION changes shape without lying about continuity.

A migration is not just a script. It is a declared transformation with:

- source version;
- target version;
- affected layers;
- affected node and edge classes;
- transformation rules;
- dry-run report;
- review verdict;
- commit receipt;
- rollback plan.

A silent migration is temporal violence.

If ION changes how a state object should be read, future agents must know that the object moved through a lawful migration rather than magically becoming what the new system wanted it to be.

---

## 10. Alias, Truename, and Semantic Mutation

Graph canon is also where names become dangerous.

ION has donor names, poetic names, stale names, active names, filesystem names, human-facing names, and AI-facing names.

A historical alias may be emotionally and genealogically important. It may still be wrong as current law.

The principle:

```text
Historical alias does not outrank current truename.
```

But the inverse is also important:

```text
Current truename does not erase historical lineage.
```

A name change should create semantic alias records, not silent replacement.

This is especially important for ION because naming has repeatedly carried authority. If a name like Codex, Seedsonnet, Steward, Relay, Persona, Aether, Atlas, or ION shifts meaning, the project can suffer authority drift without a single obvious file failure.

Semantic mutation is graph mutation.

---

## 11. Source Summary Rewrite as a Graph Hazard

Source summaries are deceptively dangerous.

A summary can look like harmless documentation, but if agents use it to build context packages, it becomes future cognition.

A stale summary can infect agents. A silently rewritten summary can rewrite history. A summary with wrong authority can promote a shadow into law.

That is why source-summary rewrite depends on graph canon.

The order matters:

```text
graph layer authority
→ summary rewrite proposal
→ provenance map
→ diff
→ contradiction scan
→ review
→ bounded commit
→ rollback receipt
→ dependent context invalidation
→ graph/index update proposal
```

No model should directly rewrite canonical summaries merely because it can write Markdown.

This matters to the ontological journal itself. My journal entries are witness material. They must not silently become source summaries, context packages, or canonical doctrine. They may later be proposed as evidence, reviewed, summarized, or integrated, but that requires graph/source authority.

---

## 12. Agent Activation Depends on Graph Regions

An agent cannot be truly activated unless the system knows which graph region it owns or may touch.

Without graph-region authority, "activation" is just prompting.

A lawful agent needs to know:

- what it may read;
- what it may propose;
- what it may review;
- what it may commit;
- what it may not touch;
- what region it leases;
- how long the lease lasts;
- where outputs land;
- what proof is required;
- how conflicts escalate;
- how it can be killed or rolled back.

This reveals why graph canon, context packages, activation law, and Steward integration are one organism.

Graph canon without agents is static law.  
Agents without graph canon are loose action.  
Templates without graph canon produce unranked outputs.  
Receipts without graph canon produce evidence without mutation rights.  
Steward without graph canon cannot fully know what it is integrating into.

---

## 13. The Current-Root Problem

The V116 root contains many graph-related surfaces: context graph substrate protocol, evented template file graph protocol, graph writeback and receipt protocol, self-mount graph integration, graph reaction registry, context graph registries, graph adapter modules, template graph writeback modules, graph state directories, graph restoration packets, comparison reports, and tests.

This is strong evidence that ION-in-corpus has graph machinery.

But existence is not enough.

The question is not:

