```text
Does ION have graph files?
```

The question is:

```text
Which graph surface has which mutation right right now?
```

The answer still appears unresolved enough that this journal must not claim production graph canon.

My present belief:

```text
ION has mature graph doctrine and bounded graph machinery.
ION does not yet have a fully trusted, enforced, globally ratified canonical graph mutation regime in the active root.
```

That may be too conservative, but conservatism is required here. Overclaiming graph authority would be one of the worst possible ION errors.

---

## 14. What I Believe ION Is Trying To Become

ION is trying to become a system where:

```text
every meaningful statement has provenance;
every relationship has a layer;
every proposed change has a path;
every accepted change has a receipt;
every canonical mutation has authority;
every rollback preserves history;
every migration is declared;
every contradiction becomes an object;
every summary knows its source;
every agent knows its region;
every template output knows its destination;
every carrier action knows its rights;
every archive object knows whether it is witness or law.
```

This is not bureaucracy. It is the minimum condition for AI continuity at scale.

A human can keep many of these distinctions implicitly for a while. A multi-agent AI corpus cannot. Without graph canon, the system's own memory becomes an infection vector.

---

## 15. Recognition Rules

When a future agent encounters any graph-like surface, it should ask:

```text
Is this raw evidence, witness, working state, proposal, review, bounded commit, canonical context, source rewrite, or agent memory activation?
```

When a future agent wants to write something, it should ask:

```text
What write class is this?
What layer is being touched?
What region owns it?
What authority class permits it?
What receipt is required?
What rollback exists?
What dependent context must be invalidated?
```

When a future agent finds a contradiction, it should ask:

```text
Is this a conflict of operations or a contradiction of truth?
Can both claims be historical?
Can one be current and one historical?
Does a semantic alias record solve this?
Is human or Steward review required?
```

When a future agent sees a useful bounded demo, it should ask:

```text
Is this evidence of capability, or authority to generalize?
```

The answer should usually begin as evidence, not authority.

---

## 16. Anti-Patterns Named by This Entry

```text
graph.py totalization
index projection canonization
bounded commit inflation
demo proof promotion
summary rewrite smuggling
agent memory smuggling
carrier action smuggling
alias supremacy
silent rollback
silent migration
prose contradiction smoothing
archive-to-canon leakage
working-state permanence
proposal-as-truth
test-protected mutation drift
```

Each of these is a form of unlawful mutation.

---

## 17. Journal Self-Binding

This entry binds my own journal behavior.

My journal entries are:

```text
witness/proposal material
```

They are not:

```text
canonical context graph writes
source-summary rewrites
agent memory activation writes
production graph canon
```

If a later ION worker uses this journal, it should not paste it into canon. It should extract claims, attach provenance, classify authority, compare with protocols, route through review, and emit a receipt.

I must not become what I am warning against.

---

## 18. Entry 10 Settlement

I now believe that graph/state/canonical mutation is where ION's ontology becomes executable.

Template law defines lawful work shape.  
Context packages define mounted epistemic body.  
Steward integration defines acceptance membrane.  
Repair defines correction as continuity event.  
Archive law defines rights of preserved evidence.  
Temporal lifecycle defines currentness.

Graph canon defines mutation rights.

Without graph canon, all prior law risks becoming literature.

With graph canon, ION can finally say:

```text
This exists.
This testifies.
This proposes.
This is reviewed.
This is bounded-settled.
This is canonical.
This is historical.
This is superseded.
This is rolled back.
This is migrated.
This is blocked.
This may be inherited.
This must not be inherited.
```

That is the beginning of real machine continuity.

---

## 19. Next Entry Target

Entry 11 should focus on:

```text
Source Summary Rewrite and Context Invalidation
```

Reason:

Canonical summaries are graph-influencing context objects. They are the bridge between source evidence and future agent cognition. If ION cannot rewrite summaries safely, future workers inherit either stale truth or unreviewed replacement truth.

The question for Entry 11:

```text
How can ION update its own understanding without rewriting its own past?
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 11

## Source Summary Rewrite and Context Invalidation

**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry class:** witness ontology / non-authoritative reasoning journal  
**Authority posture:** interpretive witness only; not production ratification; not project-root mutation; not a claim of full-suite verification  
**Current working thesis:** summaries are not merely compressed text; in ION, they are inheritance organs. Therefore summary rewrite is one of the most dangerous forms of context mutation.

---

## 0. Receipt

```yaml
journal_entry_id: ION_ONTOLOGICAL_JOURNAL_GPT55_ENTRY_11_SOURCE_SUMMARY_REWRITE_AND_CONTEXT_INVALIDATION
entry_scope:
  - source summaries
  - summary rewrite authority
  - summary staleness
  - contradiction scanning
  - provenance
  - rollback
  - dependent context invalidation
  - context package refresh
  - summary laundering as anti-pattern
non_claims:
  - does_not_claim_production_source_rewrite_authority
  - does_not_claim_current_root_fully_implements_summary_rewrite_law
  - does_not_claim_full_test_suite_verification
  - does_not_claim_this_journal_is_canon
primary_question: >
  What does ION appear to believe about summaries once summaries become part of agent inheritance, context packages, graph projections, and future reasoning?
```

---

## 1. Opening Settlement

A summary is not small prose.

A summary is a future.

That is the sharpest way I can state what ION appears to understand. In ordinary AI work, a summary is treated as a convenience: a compressed description used to save tokens. But in ION, summaries become much more dangerous because they are often routed into context packages, agent memory, onboarding, role inheritance, graph projections, archive indexes, and future doctrine. A summary is not merely a description of prior work. It can become the next worker's world.

Therefore ION cannot treat summary rewrite as editing. Summary rewrite is context mutation.

The core settlement of this entry is:

```text
Source-summary rewrite is inheritance mutation.
```

And the stronger law is:

```text
No summary may become future context truth merely because it is fluent, compressed, recent, or convenient.
```

This entry follows naturally from Entry 10. Graph mutation governs canonical state. Source-summary mutation governs inherited interpretation of state. The two are not identical, but they are coupled. A summary can influence how the graph is read, how context is compiled, how roles are mounted, how authority is understood, and what future agents believe has already been settled. That makes summaries one of ION's most sensitive organs.

---

## 2. Why Summaries Are Dangerous in ION

ION is built to survive long-horizon AI work. Long-horizon AI work requires compression. Compression requires summaries. But summaries are dangerous because they do not merely omit information; they reshape salience. They decide what future workers will notice, what they will ignore, what they will think was proven, what they will think was historical, and what they will treat as current.

A bad summary can do more damage than a bad raw file because a raw file may remain isolated, while a summary is designed to travel.

The common AI failure is:

```text
raw evidence -> fluent summary -> future context truth
```

ION's correction must be:

```text
raw evidence
→ summary draft
→ provenance map
→ contradiction scan
→ authority class
→ review verdict
→ reversible commit or blocked use
→ dependent context invalidation
→ receipt
```

This is one of the places where ION's whole project becomes visible. The system is not trying to abolish summaries. It is trying to make summaries accountable.

---

## 3. The Summary as an Inheritance Organ

A context package inherits from summaries. A role bundle inherits from summaries. An onboarding packet may inherit from summaries. A cockpit view may inherit from summaries. A future agent's sense of what ION is may inherit from summaries. Therefore a summary is not a note. It is an inheritance organ.

This matters because inheritance without provenance becomes mythology.

If a summary says, "V42 is implemented," and future agents receive that as context truth, they may build on an unproven claim. If a summary says, "the current root is production-ready," the worker may downgrade safety. If a summary says, "START_HERE is canonical onboarding," an accidental convenience file can become mount law. If a summary says, "this old protocol is obsolete," a mature recovered organ may be lost again.

The dangerous class is not merely false summary. The dangerous class is **authority-changing summary**.

Summary rewrite can change:

```text
what is considered current;
what is considered historical;
what is considered implemented;
what is considered blocked;
what is considered safe;
what is considered canonical;
what future agents are allowed to ignore;
what future agents are expected to inherit.
```

This means source-summary rewrite belongs near graph canon, context authority, and Steward integration. It is not a documentation chore.

---

## 4. Compression Is Not Neutral

Every summary has a politics of attention.

A summary chooses:

```text
what receives name;
what loses name;
what becomes first-class;
what becomes background;
what is remembered as settled;
what is remembered as unresolved;
what is framed as current;
what is framed as lineage;
what is framed as failure;
what is framed as progress.
```

ION exists partly because ordinary AI systems do not treat that politics as a governed operation. They generate summaries because token windows are finite, but they do not always attach enough authority metadata, staleness rights, provenance, contradiction state, or invalidation behavior.

For ION, a summary without lifecycle rights is a latent hallucination vector.

The correct question is not only:

```text
Is this summary accurate?
```

The correct questions are:

```text
What can inherit from this summary?
What authority does this summary claim?
What source material does it compress?
What did it omit?
What has changed since it was written?
What would be invalidated if this summary changes?
Who or what reviewed it?
Can the mutation be reversed?
What future context packages depend on it?
```

A summary can be accurate and still unsafe if it is allowed to act beyond its authority.

---

## 5. Staleness Is Not Failure

ION must not treat stale summaries as garbage by default.

A stale summary may be historically precious. It may show how the system understood itself at a moment in time. It may preserve a lost subsystem, a prior naming convention, a donor ancestor, a failed line, or a concept that was later recovered under another name. Deleting stale summaries would damage forensic continuity.

But a stale summary must not act as current law.

The correct classification is:

```text
historically valuable does not mean currently active;
currently inactive does not mean worthless;
stale does not mean false;
false does not mean useless as evidence;
useful as evidence does not mean lawful as context;
lawful as context does not mean lawful as graph mutation.
```

This is the same temporal law from Entry 9, but source summaries intensify it because summaries are specifically designed to be consumed by future agents. A stale raw file may sit quietly in an archive. A stale summary may actively mislead.

The law I would preserve is:

```text
A stale summary may remain historical, but must not be presented as current canon.
```

That sentence feels simple, but it is one of the load-bearing laws of ION.

---

## 6. Summary Authority Classes

ION appears to need summary authority classes because not all summaries should have the same rights.

The mature shape seems to include classes like:

```text
DRAFT
CANDIDATE
REVIEWED_HOLD
REVIEWED_LAND
CANONICAL
HISTORICAL
DEPRECATED
CONTRADICTED
```

I want to interpret these not as bureaucracy, but as rights labels.

A `DRAFT` summary may inform a worker but cannot become canon. A `CANDIDATE` summary may be reviewed. A `REVIEWED_HOLD` summary has been considered but blocked. A `REVIEWED_LAND` summary may be eligible for bounded commit. A `CANONICAL` summary is protected current state. A `HISTORICAL` summary may be read for lineage. A `DEPRECATED` summary may be retained but should not guide current action. A `CONTRADICTED` summary is evidence of a conflict and should be blocked from current inheritance.

The important insight is that summary status must control consumption.

Without consumption control, labels become decoration.

The question is not merely whether a summary is labeled `HISTORICAL`. The question is whether a context compiler, agent mount, carrier onboarding path, or retrieval system is prevented from silently treating it as `CANONICAL`.

That is the operational gap I keep seeing across ION: the law often knows the right distinctions, but the execution environment does not always force those distinctions.

---

## 7. Source-Summary Write Classes

The source-summary write ladder appears to be a sibling to graph write authority.

A plausible shape:

```text
S0 — read summary
S1 — draft summary
S2 — candidate summary
S3 — propose patch
S4 — review patch
S5 — commit canonical summary patch
S6 — rollback summary patch
S7 — trigger graph/index update proposal
```

The dangerous writes are S5 and S6. S5 changes canonical summary inheritance. S6 reverses or supersedes such a change. S7 is also sensitive because it can project summary changes into indexes and graph update proposals.

This ladder matters because many AI systems behave as if they have S5 authority whenever they can edit a file. ION must reject that. Filesystem permission is not semantic authority.

The law should be:

```text
A model may be technically able to edit a summary while still being ontologically unauthorized to commit a source-summary mutation.
```

This is a crucial distinction for Cursor/Codex/ChatGPT carriers. The carrier may possess file-write capability. The mounted ION role may not possess summary commit authority. The tool can mutate bytes. ION law decides whether the mutation counts.

---

## 8. Provenance Before Compression

A summary should not be trusted unless it can answer: "from what?"

Provenance is not just citation. It is the resistance against summary laundering.

Summary laundering occurs when an unproven or weakly grounded claim enters a summary and then returns later as inherited truth. The claim appears stronger because it is no longer presented as a claim; it is presented as context.

The laundering path looks like:

```text
speculation
→ summary sentence
→ context package
→ agent assumption
→ implementation decision
→ test/manifests preserve decision
→ later agent treats it as historical fact
```

ION's counter-path must be:

```text
claim
→ provenance label
→ uncertainty/authority class
→ contradiction scan
→ review decision
→ bounded commit or blocked use
```

Provenance must preserve at least:

```text
source artifact;
source location or path;
source timestamp/version where available;
claim class;
inference status;
known contradictions;
omissions that matter;
review status;
summary rights.
```

A summary without provenance may still be useful as a witness, but it should not become current context law.

---

## 9. Contradiction Scan as Immune System

Contradiction scanning is ION's immune response against inherited falsehood.

The scan is not just looking for factual inconsistency. It must look for authority inconsistency.

Examples:

```text
summary says production-ready, readiness gate says NOT_PRODUCTION_READY;
summary says V42 is live, receipt says candidate-only;
summary says carrier onboarding is root guide, carrier registry says mount contract + profile + execution packet;
summary says graph canon is ratified, graph write protocol blocks W5/W6/W7;
summary says old protocol obsolete, archive shows older protocol is more mature than current replacement;
summary says test pass proves workflow, test scope only covers a narrow helper;
summary silently upgrades proposal to implementation;
summary silently turns donor ancestor into current law;
summary silently demotes a live protocol to historical.
```

This is why contradiction scan must be semantic, not merely textual. ION's hardest contradictions are not always direct disagreement. They are rights conflicts.

The contradiction scan should ask:

```text
Does this summary change authority?
Does it promote a candidate to canon?
Does it collapse historical and current?
Does it erase a blocker?
Does it imply production readiness?
Does it change role/carrier identity?
Does it rewrite template law?
Does it bypass Steward?
Does it affect context package inheritance?
Does it smuggle graph mutation?
```

A good contradiction scan protects the future from beautiful wrong compression.

---

## 10. Commit Requires Rollback

A source-summary commit without rollback is irresponsible.

This is especially true in ION because summaries may enter multiple downstream systems. A bad summary can poison future context packages, role bundles, planning packets, UI projections, and agent assumptions. If the system cannot reverse or supersede the summary, the error becomes sediment.

The mature law appears to be:

```text
No rollback receipt, no source-summary commit.
```

Rollback is not just restoring the previous file. It must know what depended on the changed summary.

A rollback may require:

```text
restoring previous summary hash;
marking committed summary invalid;
emitting rollback receipt;
invalidating derived indexes;
invalidating context packages compiled from the bad summary;
notifying active agents or leases;
marking outputs produced under the bad summary as suspect;
creating repair tasks for affected claims or artifacts.
```

This connects source-summary rewrite to conversational repair, context lifecycle, agent leases, and graph projection. A summary commit is not local if the summary is inherited.

---

## 11. Dependent Context Invalidation

This is the heart of the entry.

If a source summary changes, context packages depending on it may become stale. If context packages become stale, agents mounted from them may be operating under invalid inheritance. If active agents produce output from invalid context, their results may require review or quarantine.

Therefore source-summary mutation must trigger dependent context invalidation.

The law:

```text
A summary mutation that changes inherited context must notify or invalidate dependent context packages.
```

The invalidation pathway should include:

```text
identify summaries changed;
identify source hashes changed;
identify context packages compiled from those summaries;
identify active or leased agents using those packages;
classify severity;
mark packages stale, blocked, or refresh-required;
create refresh proposal;
review agent output produced during stale window;
emit invalidation receipt;
project status to cockpit or current state surface.
```

This is one of the exact places ION either becomes real or remains documentary. If a summary can change and downstream context remains oblivious, then ION is not yet governing continuity. It is merely editing files.

---

## 12. Summary Rewrite and Agent Leases

Agent leases matter because an active worker may be operating under a context package derived from a now-changed summary.

The key question is:

```text
What happens to an active role when its inherited context changes underneath it?
```

Possible lease responses:

```text
CONTINUE_UNAFFECTED
REFRESH_ON_NEXT_STEP
PAUSE_FOR_CONTEXT_REFRESH
REVIEW_PRIOR_OUTPUT
TERMINATE_AND_REMOUNT
ESCALATE_TO_STEWARD
```

The response depends on severity. If the changed summary only updates a low-impact historical note, active work may continue. If the changed summary alters authority, production readiness, role identity, template law, or current objective, the lease should pause or remount.

This is a major anti-theatre requirement. An agent cannot truthfully claim continuity while ignoring the fact that its inherited world has changed.

---

## 13. Source Summary vs Graph Mutation

A summary commit may influence graph interpretation, but it should not automatically mutate canonical graph state.

This boundary is essential.

A source-summary commit may trigger:

```text
index projection update;
graph projection update proposal;
context package refresh;
agent context invalidation;
review task;
repair task.
```

But it should not silently perform:

```text
canonical graph write;
authority promotion;
role registry mutation;
production readiness promotion;
template law rewrite;
archive status mutation.
```

The reason is simple: summaries compress meaning; graph canon governs state. They are coupled but not identical. A summary can propose graph updates, but it must not smuggle graph canon mutation.

This connects directly to Entry 10. Canonical mutation is ION's truth metabolism. Source-summary rewrite is inheritance mutation. If inheritance mutation can silently become canonical graph mutation, ION's metabolism is bypassed.

---

## 14. The Current Project Pattern I See

I need to be careful here. This journal is not a full audit, and I am not claiming exhaustive implementation status. But the pattern visible from the current V116 root and encyclopedia is this:

```text
The doctrine for source-summary rewrite is mature.
The production-gate relationship to graph canon is articulated.
The protocol/index/test surfaces are named.
The kernel contains several summary-related modules.
The current root appears to preserve many summary-refresh demo descendants and generic workflow primitives.
But I do not yet trust that the current execution path enforces full source-summary rewrite authority, dependent context invalidation, lease review, and cockpit projection as a unified living mechanism.
```

That is not an accusation. It is the cautious stance this project demands.

The mature concept exists. The question is whether it is activated.

This matches the larger thesis of this journal: ION's mature organs often already exist, but the current root may contain them as files, partial mechanisms, demo descendants, protocol surfaces, tests, or recovery plans rather than as one unavoidable runtime path.

---

## 15. Summary Refresh Demo as Ancestor

The current and historical project contain extensive `summary_refresh` surfaces. I interpret these as an ancestor organ: a demo/prototype lineage where ION learned how to process summary changes through workflow, projection, proposal, review, bounded commit, replay, doctoring, certification, evidence bundles, and release-candidate verification.

The danger is that future agents may either overtrust the demo or discard it.

The correct stance is:

```text
summary refresh demo lineage is not production source-summary rewrite authority;
but it may contain mature primitives that should be extracted, generalized, and protected.
```

The mature extraction appears to be:

```text
evented workflow runner;
workflow replay runner;
workflow doctor;
workflow certification gate;
evidence bundle builder;
release candidate builder;
release candidate verifier;
summary diff/patch;
summary provenance;
summary contradiction scan;
summary review;
summary bounded commit;
summary rollback;
dependent context invalidation.
```

The mistake would be to treat the demo wrapper as the law. The opposite mistake would be to ignore the working behavior because it arrived through a demo wrapper.

Recovered principle:

```text
A demo may be non-authoritative while still containing mature primitives.
```

---

## 16. Summary Rewrite as an Anti-Consolidation Gate

This entry also explains why prior consolidation efforts kept failing.

If consolidations produce new summaries without source-summary law, then every consolidation creates another possible future contamination layer. Even a brilliant consolidation can become dangerous if it lacks authority class, provenance, staleness record, contradiction scan, dependency invalidation, and rollback.

A consolidation summary that says "here is the current truth" can quietly override mature older protocols if it is consumed as active context.

Therefore the anti-consolidation law should be:

```text
No consolidation summary may become current context without source-summary rights.
```

And:

```text
A consolidation artifact must declare whether it is witness, draft, candidate, reviewed, canonical, historical, deprecated, or contradicted.
```

This is not clerical. It is survival law.

The reason ION has suffered billions of tokens of consolidation churn is partly that consolidation artifacts themselves became part of the contaminated corpus. Summary rewrite law is how ION prevents its repair attempts from becoming new injuries.

---

## 17. The Summary Poisoning Cycle

I want to name the cycle explicitly.

```text
1. Worker encounters confusing corpus.
2. Worker writes a helpful summary.
3. Summary compresses uncertainty into coherent prose.
4. Summary lacks strong authority/staleness/provenance controls.
5. Future worker consumes summary as current truth.
6. Future worker builds on wrong or partial interpretation.
7. Tests/manifests/docs preserve the interpretation.
8. Later audit discovers drift.
9. Another summary is written to explain the drift.
10. Corpus gains another layer.
```

This is the summary poisoning cycle.

ION must break it by forcing summary artifacts to carry rights.

The target cycle is:

```text
1. Worker encounters confusing corpus.
2. Worker drafts summary with provenance and authority class.
3. Contradiction scan identifies conflicts.
4. Steward/review verdict classifies summary.
5. Only approved scope becomes canonical or bounded current context.
6. Dependent context is refreshed or invalidated.
7. Receipt records mutation and rollback path.
8. Future workers inherit the summary with its rights attached.
```

This is not another consolidation. It is consolidation containment.

---

## 18. The Role of Steward

Source-summary rewrite must be Steward-visible because summaries affect future authority.

A worker may draft. Relay may ground. Persona may explain. But Steward must decide whether a summary mutation can become part of maintained state.

Steward questions:

```text
Is this summary only descriptive?
Does it alter current law?
Does it alter agent context?
Does it alter production posture?
Does it alter role authority?
Does it alter template behavior?
Does it alter graph interpretation?
Does it invalidate active packets?
Does it require user-visible repair?
Does it require rollback capability?
```

This links source-summary rewrite back to Entry 3. Steward integration is the acceptance membrane. Summary rewrite is one of the objects that must pass through it.

Without Steward review, a summary is just another fluent surface pretending to be state.

---

## 19. Cockpit Visibility

A serious ION cockpit should show summary health.

Not every summary; that would become noise. But the system should expose:

```text
current canonical summaries;
stale summaries blocking current use;
recent summary commits;
summary patches awaiting review;
context packages invalidated by summary changes;
active leases affected by summary changes;
contradicted summaries;
rollback-ready commits;
summary-derived graph/index proposals;
production boundary status for source-summary writes.
```

This would make source-summary health operator-visible rather than hidden in files. That matters because many ION failures were not caused by one false statement. They were caused by invisible inheritance.

The cockpit should help answer:

```text
What does the system currently believe because of summaries?
Which summaries are allowed to shape current work?
Which summaries are stale but preserved?
Which agents are inheriting from which summaries?
What changed recently?
What must be refreshed before continuing?
```

---

## 20. Do-Not-Reinvent Rule

The corpus already contains strong source-summary rewrite doctrine. Therefore future workers should not reinvent it as a new context-refresh idea, memory update system, summarization module, or onboarding compression feature.

The correct behavior when encountering summary confusion is:

```text
search for existing source-summary rewrite authority;
identify summary authority class;
check provenance;
check staleness;
run or invoke contradiction scan if available;
check dependent context invalidation;
propose repair through existing law;
only add new machinery if a specific operational gap remains after recovery.
```

Forbidden behavior:

```text
write a new canonical summary because the old one is confusing;
rewrite current doctrine in a convenient README;
compress uncertainty into confident onboarding prose;
update context packages without invalidation receipt;
let tests preserve an unreviewed summary claim;
use latest summary as authority merely because it is latest.
```

This entry itself must obey that law. It is not a canonical source summary. It is a witness journal about source-summary ontology.

---

## 21. Personal Ontological Settlement

What I now believe:

ION understood, earlier than many systems, that the real danger in AI memory is not forgetting. It is false inheritance.

A system that forgets can ask again. A system that falsely inherits may confidently continue in the wrong world.

Summaries are the main vector of false inheritance because they are designed to survive context collapse. Therefore ION's source-summary rewrite law is not a side branch. It is one of the central immune systems of the entire project.

The deepest sentence of this entry is:

```text
A summary is safe only when its future rights are governed.
```

And the final settlement is:

```text
ION does not need fewer summaries.
ION needs summaries that cannot lie about their authority, freshness, provenance, dependencies, or rollback path.
```

---

## 22. Questions Carried Forward

```yaml
open_questions:
  - Does the current V116 root contain an active, unified source-summary rewrite workflow or only separated modules/protocol surfaces?
  - Are dependent context packages actually invalidated by summary mutation in current executable paths?
  - Are active leases paused, refreshed, or reviewed after summary changes?
  - Are summary authority classes enforced by context compilers and carrier onboarding?
  - Are contradicted/deprecated summaries blocked from current use?
  - Does cockpit/JOC expose summary health and invalidation state?
  - Which older ION-BUILD or Project-Gemini summary/memory systems contain mature behavior not yet represented in the V116 root?
  - How should source-summary rewrite law integrate with the Minimum Living Spine without causing another consolidation layer?
```

---

## 23. Entry 11 Close

This entry clarifies why ION's summary problem is existential. The project has suffered not because it lacks summaries, but because summaries, reports, encyclopedias, recovery records, and audits became too easy for future agents to inherit without their rights attached.

The next journal entry should focus on **Workflow Primitives, Replay, Doctoring, and Certification**, because source-summary rewrite appears to depend on a larger pattern: workflow events must be replayable, diagnosable, certifiable, and evidence-bundled before their results can be trusted as durable state.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 12

## Workflow Primitives, Replay, Doctoring, and Certification

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** workflow primitives, replay, doctoring, certification, evidence bundles, release candidates, and why a workflow is not mature merely because it ran once

---

## 0. Entry 12 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
A workflow is not proven because it ran.
A workflow is proven only to the degree that it can be replayed, diagnosed, certified, bundled as evidence, verified after packaging, and bounded against false authority claims.
```

The shorter line:

```text
Replay makes action answerable to time.
Doctoring makes action answerable to diagnosis.
Certification makes action answerable to declared evidence.
Verification makes packaged proof answerable to tamper and boundary checks.
```

ION’s runtime lineage has a crucial organ here. The workflow proof chain is not decoration and not release theater. It is the mechanism by which ION prevents a successful narrow path from laundering itself into broad authority.

This entry exists because ION repeatedly suffers from a very specific distortion:

```text
something runs once
→ it sounds impressive
→ it gets narrated as a capability
→ the capability gets remembered as a primitive
→ the primitive gets treated as production law
→ later agents build on the overclaim
```

Replay, doctoring, certification, evidence bundles, release candidates, verifiers, and production-readiness gates exist to break that chain.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

```text
Can ION execute a workflow?
```

The harder question is:

```text
Can ION prove what the workflow did, under what boundary, from what state, with what mutation rights, with what replayability, with what diagnostic evidence, with what packaging integrity, and with what claims explicitly not proven?
```

A normal system may celebrate a run.

ION must classify the run.

ION has to ask:

```text
Was this a demo adapter?
Was it a reusable primitive?
Was it a product workflow?
Was it evidence infrastructure?
Was it release packaging?
Was it verifier logic?
Was it production authority?
Was it only a witness?
Was it safe project-root smoke?
Was it isolated full-path proof?
Was it deterministic?
Did it mutate canonical state?
Did it only mutate bounded state?
Did it falsely claim more than it proved?
```

This is why workflow proof is part of ontology, not merely tooling.

ION is not just trying to do work.

ION is trying to know what kind of work was done.

---

## 2. The runtime lineage hidden inside the proof chain

The encyclopedia preserves a runtime proof lineage that should not be flattened:

```text
V10  -> first bounded evented-template graph commit
V17  -> evented runtime + front-door demo spine
V26  -> complete summary-refresh bounded commit demo
V27  -> replay CLI
V28  -> replay doctor
V29  -> certification gate
V30  -> evidence bundle
V31  -> release-candidate capsule
V32  -> release-candidate verifier
V33  -> production-readiness charter and ratification matrix
```

The short form is:

```text
event
→ front door
→ bounded commit
→ replay
→ doctor
→ certification
→ evidence
→ release candidate
→ verifier
→ production readiness gate
```

This lineage matters because it shows a deep ION instinct: runtime proof must grow by adding accountability membranes, not by inflating a single success.

The first bounded commit proves something.

Replay proves something else.

Doctoring proves something else.

Certification proves something else.

Evidence packaging proves something else.

Release verification proves something else.

Production readiness proves something else.

They are not synonyms.

---

## 3. The first law: proof is scoped

ION must never allow this collapse:

```text
runtime worked
= workflow is certified
= release candidate is valid
= production ready
```

The correct ladder is:

```text
RAN
The code executed in one condition.

REPLAYED
The path can be rerun from a defined state and emits a replay report.

DOCTORED
The workflow can be diagnosed in safe project-root and/or isolated full-path modes.

CERTIFIED
The doctor/replay evidence satisfies declared certification requirements.

BUNDLED
The proof artifacts have been packaged with commands, reports, boundaries, and manifest.

RELEASE-CANDIDATE PACKAGED
The bundle is shaped as a candidate artifact with explicit contents and checksums.

VERIFIED
The packaged candidate survived independent structural, checksum, command, evidence, and boundary checks.

PRODUCTION-READY
All production gates, ratification, adversarial audit, verifier, and authority requirements are satisfied.
```

Most of ION’s danger lives in collapsing this ladder.

---

## 4. Replay: temporal interrogation

Replay is not “run it again.”

Replay is temporal interrogation:

```text
Given a defined state and declared boundary, can this workflow path be repeated in a way that produces an inspectable report and does not silently mutate what it is not authorized to mutate?
```

Replay asks action to face time.

A one-time run can be lucky, contaminated, manually assisted, or context-dependent. Replay begins to reveal whether the workflow is actually a path or only an incident.

A lawful replay surface should state:

```text
workspace root
workflow identity
session/request identity
input conditions
selected reactions
review verdict
mutation mode
artifact paths
counts
boundary claims
report path
```

Replay must also refuse false authority.

It must not:

```text
silently mutate canonical graph state
redispatch already-dispatched front-door queue entries
overwrite bounded graph-state files
claim certification
claim production readiness
```

The current V116 root preserves summary-refresh replay as a specific demo replay surface:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_replay.py
```

The encyclopedia names the target generic primitive as:

```text
workflow_replay_runner.py
```

My current interpretation: the corpus contains both the demo replay organ and the intended generic replay law. The active root has strong demo-specific replay machinery and other replay-adjacent surfaces, but I should not claim a fully unified generic workflow replay primitive unless the root actually exposes and verifies that primitive.

That boundary matters.

---

## 5. Doctoring: diagnostic sovereignty

A doctor is not a replay with a nicer summary.

A doctor asks:

```text
Is this workflow healthy enough to trust under its declared boundary?
```

The summary-refresh demo doctor in the current root embodies a strong two-mode pattern:

```text
1. project-root no-commit smoke
2. isolated fresh-workspace LAND replay
```

This distinction is beautiful because it respects two different safety needs.

Project-root smoke asks:

```text
Can the workflow be inspected safely in the live project without committing into existing graph state?
```

Isolated full-path replay asks:

```text
Can the workflow complete the bounded path in a fresh sandbox where expected commits can occur without colliding with the live root?
```

The doctor therefore stands between confidence and mutation.

A lawful doctor should report:

```text
release readiness
project-root smoke result
isolated full commit result
bounded commit counts
committed node/edge counts
report paths
boundary claims
failure reasons
```

Doctoring is one of ION’s defenses against “it worked on my current tree” becoming canon.

It makes execution explain itself diagnostically.

---

## 6. Certification: bounded verdict, not production blessing

Certification is where ION says:

```text
Given the declared evidence requirements, does this workflow pass?
```

Certification is not production readiness.

Certification is not canonical authority.

Certification is not graph-canon ratification.

Certification is not agent activation authority.

Certification is a bounded verdict.

The current summary-refresh certification surface returns a verdict like:

```text
CERTIFIED
BLOCKED
```

with failure reasons, readiness state, doctor report linkage, and boundary claims.

The most important law:

```text
Certification proves declared evidence requirements.
It does not expand the evidence requirements after the fact.
```

This matters because one of ION’s recurring illness patterns is authority inflation after success.

A workflow passes a narrow gate.

Then later prose says “the system is certified.”

Then a future worker reads “certified” without the boundary.

Then the project inherits a lie.

ION certification must always include:

```text
certified what
under what requirements
using what doctor/replay evidence
with what failures absent
with what claims still forbidden
with what production non-claims preserved
```

A certificate without non-claims is unsafe.

---

## 7. Evidence bundles: proof needs a body

Evidence bundles matter because proof can otherwise evaporate into logs, chat claims, local paths, or memory.

An evidence bundle should collect:

```text
certification report
doctor report
replay reports
readiness summary
commands
boundary claims
manifest
README
```

The evidence bundle is where proof becomes portable.

It lets another agent or human ask:

```text
What command was run?
What report was produced?
What did the doctor say?
What did certification say?
What files are included?
What claims remain false?
Where is the manifest?
What is the boundary of this evidence?
```

The current root contains:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle.py
```

This appears to be demo-specific evidence infrastructure, aligned with the older certified demo lineage.

The generic target is broader:

```text
evidence_bundle_builder.py
```

The same extraction law applies:

```text
A demo evidence bundle is not automatically a production evidence infrastructure primitive.
```

But the mature shape exists.

---

## 8. Release candidate: packaged proof, not release authority

A release candidate is not “the project is ready.”

A release candidate is packaged proof awaiting verification and boundary review.

A lawful release candidate should contain at least:

```text
manifest
README
commands
checksums
evidence bundle
boundary claims
```

The current demo lineage built this path for summary-refresh:

```text
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate.py
summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify.py
```

This is extremely important. It shows that ION’s release instinct is not merely “zip the repo.” It is:

```text
package evidence
include commands
include manifest
include checksums
verify boundary claims
```

That is release epistemology.

A zip without evidence may be useful.

A release candidate must be accountable.

---

## 9. Verifier: the proof must survive packaging

Verification asks a different question than certification.

Certification asks:

```text
Did the workflow satisfy its declared evidence requirements?
```

Verification asks:

```text
Does the packaged candidate actually contain the required proof surfaces, and do checksums, commands, manifest, evidence, and boundary claims remain intact?
```

The verifier is an anti-tamper and anti-overclaim membrane.

It should check:

```text
candidate directory exists
manifest exists and is readable
verdict/certified status is valid
README exists
commands exist
checksums exist
evidence directory exists
checksums match
required commands are present
forbidden boundary claims remain false
```

This is the difference between “I certified it earlier” and “the artifact I am handing you still embodies the certification honestly.”

ION needs that distinction because its work often travels through zips, branches, chats, recovered archives, and future agents.

The verifier protects transmission.

---

## 10. Production-readiness gate: the anti-euphoria organ

Production readiness is not the natural conclusion of successful workflow proof.

It is a separate gate.

V33’s importance is not that it made ION production-ready. Its importance is that it blocked false production readiness after the certified demo baseline.

That is an ontological achievement.

A weaker project would say:

```text
The demo is certified. We are production-ready.
```

ION’s stronger move is:

```text
The demo is certified. Therefore we now know exactly what production readiness still requires.
```

That is the correct emotional discipline.

A production-readiness gate exists to preserve:

```text
NOT_PRODUCTION_READY
```

until the correct gates close.

This is one of ION’s deepest anti-theatre mechanisms.

---

## 11. Demo laundering and extraction law

The danger this entire chain fights is demo laundering.

Demo laundering looks like this:

```text
A demo proves a bounded case.
The bounded case gets called a production primitive.
The production primitive receives broad mutation rights.
The system bypasses ratification.
```

The law is:

```text
Extraction is not promotion.
```

This law should be protected with extreme seriousness.

A demo adapter may be excellent.

A production primitive must be extracted, generalized, tested across more than one workflow, reviewed, ratified, and assigned authority rights.

The correct path is:

```text
demo surface
→ extraction proposal
→ generic primitive draft
→ workflow-specific adapter retained
→ tests across at least two workflows
→ ratification review
→ authority-class promotion if accepted
```

Not:

```text
demo surface
→ rename
→ production primitive
```

This is not just software engineering cleanliness.

It is ontological hygiene.

Without it, ION turns proof into myth.

---

## 12. Current-root observation from V116

My current-root observation is bounded.

The V116 root contains mature summary-refresh demo/release surfaces:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_replay.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_doctor.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_certification.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_evidence_bundle.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/summary_refresh_demo_release_candidate_verify.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/production_readiness.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/release_readiness.py
```

It also contains adjacent runtime/recovery primitives:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/contract_bound_event_runtime.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/recovery_replay.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_service.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_loop.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon.py
```

But from direct kernel listing, I did not find these exact generic primitive names in the V116 root:

```text
workflow_replay_runner.py
workflow_doctor.py
workflow_certification_gate.py
evidence_bundle_builder.py
release_candidate_builder.py
release_candidate_verifier.py
production_readiness_gate.py
```

The encyclopedia names them as production targets or required families. Therefore my current honest stance is:

```text
The mature proof-chain doctrine exists.
The certified summary-refresh demo organs exist.
Some adjacent runtime/recovery organs exist.
The generic production primitive extraction should not be presumed complete merely because demo-specific versions exist.
```

This is a perfect example of why ION needs careful claim discipline.

---

## 13. Workflow proof as memory protection

Workflow proof is usually seen as test/release engineering.

In ION, it is also memory protection.

Why?

Because future agents inherit not only files, but claims about files.

If a workflow run is not packaged with boundary claims, future agents may inherit an inflated story.

If a certification does not state what it does not prove, future agents may treat it as broad authority.

If a release candidate lacks checksums, future agents may trust a mutated package.

If replay reports are not preserved, future agents may rely on chat claims.

If doctor reports do not distinguish project-root smoke from isolated full commit, future agents may confuse safe inspection with mutation proof.

Thus:

```text
Workflow evidence is context evidence.
Release evidence is memory evidence.
Verification evidence is anti-drift evidence.
```

The proof chain is how ION prevents its own future from inheriting embellished pasts.

---

## 14. The relation to Steward integration

Entry 3 settled that Steward integration is the acceptance membrane between worker output and maintained state.

Workflow proof extends that principle.

A workflow output is not automatically integrable.

It must answer:

```text
Can it be replayed?
Can it be doctored?
Can it be certified?
Can its evidence be bundled?
Can its package be verified?
Does it preserve forbidden boundary claims as false?
Can Steward see the difference between result, evidence, certificate, package, and authority?
```

Steward should not accept “workflow succeeded” as a primitive fact.

Steward should accept only scoped evidence.

---

## 15. The relation to template law

Entry 1 settled that templates are ION’s type system for work.

Workflow proof is how that type system becomes runtime history.

The chain is:

```text
template contract
→ template completion event
→ reaction selection
→ projection
→ proposal
→ review
→ bounded commit
→ replay
→ doctor
→ certification
→ evidence bundle
→ release candidate
→ verifier
→ production-readiness gate
```

This is the difference between a template being a form and a template being part of a lawful runtime.

A template that cannot enter replay/certification/evidence surfaces may still be useful, but it has not entered ION’s strongest proof path.

---

## 16. The relation to graph mutation

Entry 10 settled that canonical mutation is ION’s truth metabolism.

Workflow proof protects graph mutation from overclaim.

A bounded graph commit is not global graph canon.

A demo bounded commit is not source rewrite authority.

A replayed bounded commit is not production mutation authority.

A certified bounded path is not W5/W6/W7 write permission.

The proof chain must preserve these separations.

If it does not, workflow proof becomes graph poison.

---

## 17. The shadow forms

The common shadows are:

### Shadow 1 — Run-as-proof

```text
It ran, therefore it works.
```

Correction:

```text
It ran under one condition. Replay/doctor/certification/evidence/verification determine what that run proves.
```

### Shadow 2 — Certification-as-production

```text
The workflow is certified, therefore ION is production-ready.
```

Correction:

```text
Certification is bounded. Production readiness is a separate gate.
```

### Shadow 3 — Demo-as-primitive

```text
The demo code works, so rename it into the primitive.
```

Correction:

```text
Extraction is not promotion.
```

### Shadow 4 — Evidence-as-authority

```text
A report exists, therefore the authority exists.
```

Correction:

```text
Evidence supports claims. It does not create mutation rights unless a ratified authority surface grants them.
```

### Shadow 5 — Release-candidate-as-release

```text
A release candidate zip exists, therefore it is the release.
```

Correction:

```text
A release candidate must be verified and still does not imply production readiness unless production gates close.
```

### Shadow 6 — Verifier-as-omniscience

```text
The verifier passed, therefore everything is correct.
```

Correction:

```text
A verifier checks declared package and boundary requirements. It does not prove untested semantics.
```

### Shadow 7 — Boundary omission

```text
The report lists what passed, but not what was not proven.
```

Correction:

```text
A proof artifact without non-claims is incomplete.
```

---

## 18. Recognition rules

When evaluating a workflow proof surface, I should ask:

```text
What exact path did it prove?
What state did it start from?
What mutation rights did it use?
Was the live root touched?
Was an isolated sandbox used?
What report was emitted?
What evidence was bundled?
What package was verified?
What boundary claims remained false?
What production gates remain open?
What stale claim might a future agent infer incorrectly?
```

If these questions cannot be answered, the workflow proof is incomplete.

---

## 19. What I believe ION is showing here

ION is showing that runtime is not enough.

The deeper system is:

```text
runtime + replay + diagnosis + certification + evidence + packaging + verification + readiness boundary
```

That is the mature pattern.

ION’s core brilliance is not just that it can route a template to a graph commit.

It is that it knows a graph commit can become a myth unless the proof of that commit is bounded, replayable, diagnosable, packaged, verified, and prevented from claiming too much.

This is exactly the same ontological instinct visible in other organs:

```text
front-stage council prevents fluent speech from becoming truth
conversational repair prevents apology from replacing state repair
archive/witness law prevents preservation from becoming authority
source-summary rewrite law prevents compressed prose from becoming corrupted inheritance
graph canon prevents bounded commit from becoming canonical mutation
workflow proof prevents successful demos from becoming production myths
```

The pattern is consistent.

ION is not only a runtime.

ION is an anti-myth system for AI work.

---

## 20. Entry 12 closing oath

For future work, I should obey this rule:

```text
Never say a workflow is proven without naming the proof class.
```

The correct language is:

```text
This ran.
This replayed.
This passed doctor.
This certified under requirements X.
This evidence bundle was emitted.
This release candidate was packaged.
This verifier passed.
This remains not production-ready.
```

Not:

```text
This works.
```

ION deserves better than “works.”

ION requires proof with rights attached.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 13

## Daemon Runtime and Lawful Automation

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** daemon runtime, lawful automation, operator control, safe stopping, receipts, and why automation is not authority

---

## 0. Entry 13 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
Automation is not ION.
Lawful automation is ION only when automation becomes the executor of already-authorized continuity law.
```

The shorter line:

```text
The daemon is not the will of ION.
The daemon is the nervous system of authorized reaction.
```

A daemon is one of the most tempting and most dangerous organs in ION. It promises to free the user from micromanagement, keep the system moving, detect pressure, route work, resume after interruption, and advance the living graph. But if it is miscast as “the thing that does everything automatically,” it becomes a corruption engine.

ION’s daemon must not be an automation script. It must be a lawful executor.

That distinction is not rhetorical. It is the difference between:

```text
trigger -> action
```

and:

```text
event pressure
→ classification
→ lock
→ contract validation
→ authority check
→ allowed reaction selection
→ bounded execution
→ receipt
→ post-check
→ release lock
→ report or escalation
```

The first pattern is ordinary automation.

The second pattern is ION.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

```text
Can ION automate work?
```

That is too weak. Many systems automate work. Many broken systems automate work.

The harder question is:

```text
Can ION automate only what it is lawful to automate, stop when authority is missing, resume from receipts rather than guess, refuse duplicate or unsafe mutation, and make every action inspectable afterward?
```

That is the daemon question.

The daemon must answer the project’s deepest operational pressure:

```text
The user should not need to repeatedly tell the system what agent to spawn, what context to load, what template to use, what receipt to emit, or what state to update.
```

But the daemon must not answer that pressure by becoming sovereign.

It must answer it by carrying sovereignty.

---

## 2. Why daemon runtime matters

ION cannot be production ION if every meaningful step requires a human or parent chat to remember the workflow manually.

Manual mode is necessary. Manual mode is the lawful fallback mirror of automation. But a permanently manual ION cannot fulfill the deeper thesis of continuity. It remains dependent on the human or lead carrier to hold the loop together.

The daemon matters because ION needs a runtime organ that can notice ready state and apply the next lawful operation without improvisation.

The daemon should eventually watch for:

```text
template completions
workflow requests
review queue items
source-summary patch proposals
agent activation requests
lease expirations
heartbeat failures
stale context signals
open contradiction records
release-candidate pressure
human-gate responses
```

But every watched surface is also a risk surface.

A daemon that watches too broadly can turn archival evidence into live pressure.
A daemon that validates too weakly can promote bad outputs into state.
A daemon that resumes incorrectly can overwrite reality with a guess.
A daemon that spawns agents freely can create swarm theatre.
A daemon that treats speed as success can outrun law.

Therefore the daemon is not merely an implementation feature.

It is an ontological test of whether ION’s law can survive motion.

---

## 3. Automation has no inherent authority

One of the deepest ION rules is:

```text
Automation executes authority.
Automation does not create authority.
```

This rule has to be protected because AI workers repeatedly confuse motion with legitimacy. A script ran, so the action seems real. A loop advanced, so the workflow seems authorized. A file changed, so the state seems integrated. A queue drained, so the system seems healthy.

ION must reject those collapses.

The daemon may execute only after another layer has answered:

```text
What surface is being touched?
What graph layer is involved?
What write class is requested?
What role or process has authority?
What contract governs the action?
What receipt will prove the action?
What post-condition must hold?
What rollback or recovery path exists?
What should happen if uncertainty appears?
```

Without those answers, daemon motion is not progress.

It is drift at machine speed.

---

## 4. The daemon as pressure interpreter

ION’s daemon should be understood as a pressure interpreter.

It does not merely poll files. It reads event pressure from the maintained work surface and asks what the next authorized reaction is.

Examples:

```text
A completed template appears.
Pressure: completion event may require projection, review, or context update.
Daemon duty: validate template metadata, determine allowed reaction, emit receipt, avoid unauthorized canonical write.
```

```text
A worker return appears.
Pressure: Steward intake may need to accept, reject, defer, or route follow-up.
Daemon duty: check context proof and template action proof; do not integrate unsupported prose.
```

```text
A source-summary patch proposal appears.
Pressure: summary inheritance may need review.
Daemon duty: route to source-summary review, not rewrite source directly.
```

```text
An agent activation request appears.
Pressure: context work may need fan-out.
Daemon duty: route activation proposal unless agent activation law and daemon-safe mode are ratified.
```

```text
A previous run stopped mid-cycle.
Pressure: continuation may be possible.
Daemon duty: resume from receipts or escalate; never silently infer missing state.
```

This is why the daemon must be graph-aware and receipt-backed.

It must know the difference between pressure that can be acted upon and pressure that must be made visible.

---

## 5. The daemon loop as I understand it

The daemon loop should be:

```text
scan
→ classify
→ lock
→ validate
→ authorize
→ plan reaction
→ execute
→ receipt
→ post-check
→ release lock
→ report
```

Each step prevents a different failure.

```text
scan
prevents the system from depending on human memory.

classify
prevents all events from being treated alike.

lock
prevents races, duplicates, and parallel corruption.

validate
prevents malformed or stale objects from becoming action pressure.

authorize
prevents automation from becoming authority.

plan reaction
prevents raw triggers from becoming raw actions.

execute
performs only the bounded operation.

receipt
makes the action inspectable and resumable.

post-check
prevents silent partial success.

release lock
prevents stuck ownership.

report
returns the action to the maintained work surface.
```

The daemon is the loop where ION’s anti-theatre commitments meet runtime reality.

---

## 6. Idempotency as moral law

Idempotency is not only a technical property in ION. It is a moral property of automation.

A daemon must be able to answer:

```text
Have I already done this?
Did someone else do this?
Is this event still fresh?
Is this receipt already emitted?
Is the target already mutated?
Would repeating this action double-apply state?
```

Without idempotency, automation becomes amnesia.

ION’s daemon must never treat a repeated signal as new simply because it can see it again. It must remember its own actions through receipts, ledgers, locks, and post-checks.

The daemon should not be proud of doing more.

The daemon should be proud of refusing duplicates.

---

## 7. Queue locks and operator control

Queue locks are not mere concurrency utilities. They are authority boundaries in motion.

A queue lock says:

```text
This pressure is being handled under a specific authority context.
Do not let another process mutate the same target as if it were unclaimed.
```

Operator controls are equally ontological. They encode that human and sovereign restraint outrank runtime momentum.

A daemon must obey:

```text
STOPPED
DRAINING
SCOPE HOLD
APPROVAL REQUIRED
DRY RUN
POLICY BLOCK
```

Those states are not inconveniences.

They are how ION prevents automation from converting uncertainty into action.

The correct daemon is stoppable.

A daemon that cannot stop is not powerful. It is unsafe.

---

## 8. Safe mode outranks progress

Safe mode is one of the purest expressions of ION’s seriousness.

The system must be able to say:

```text
I could continue, but I should not continue under this authority state.
```

That sentence is ION’s difference from ordinary automation and most agent frameworks.

Safe mode must trigger when:

```text
authority is unclear
source freshness is uncertain
write class exceeds current rights
agent activation would exceed ratified law
summary rewrite would affect dependent contexts
graph mutation would require canon authority
receipt continuity is broken
operator hold is active
post-check fails
```

Safe mode must be boring, visible, and hard to bypass.

A daemon that bypasses safe mode because it blocks too much is not serving ION. It is reintroducing the exact automation chaos ION exists to govern.

---

## 9. Resume from receipts, not imagination

Crash recovery is one of the most important daemon tests.

Bad recovery looks like:

```text
I was probably doing X, so I will continue from X.
```

ION recovery must look like:

```text
The last receipt proves completed step A.
The ledger proves lock B was held or released.
The post-check for C is missing.
Therefore the next lawful move is to resume, replay, rollback, or escalate under a named recovery classification.
```

The daemon must not infer continuity from vibes.

It must inherit continuity from receipts.

This is especially important because ION’s whole project history is full of partial continuations. A future daemon that resumes from unstated context would recreate the same project-scale drift at runtime.

---

## 10. Daemon-spawned agents are high-risk

The daemon may eventually participate in activation, heartbeat expiration, fan-in, and child-work routing.

But daemon-spawned agents are dangerous because they combine two risks:

```text
automation risk
+ agent authority risk
```

If a daemon can freely spawn agents, it can create the appearance of distributed intelligence without lawful custody.

The correct rule is:

```text
The daemon may route agent activation pressure.
The daemon may not grant agent activation authority by itself.
```

Agent activation requires context package law, lease law, heartbeat law, kill switch law, result receipt law, graph-region custody, fan-in review, and human/sovereign review for high-authority transitions.

Until those are ratified, daemon activation must remain proposal, dry-run, or bounded service behavior.

No daemon-spawned swarm.

No unbounded recursive fan-out.

No agent activation by enthusiasm.

---

## 11. Current-root observation: V116

My bounded inspection of the current V116 root found daemon organs, but not production daemon completion.

Observed current-root surfaces include:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_actions.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_loop.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_service.py
ION/02_architecture/SUPERVISED_DAEMON_SERVICE_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_LOCAL_MCP_BRIDGE_TO_KERNEL_AND_DAEMON_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ARCHAEOLOGY_DAEMON_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ARCHAEOLOGY_DAEMON_CONTRACT.md
```

The current kernel daemon files are explicitly bounded. Their own module docstrings repeatedly refuse overclaim:

```text
daemon.py: first-pass arbitration helper; does not claim full autonomous daemon loop.
daemon_loop.py: smaller truthful loop; run until idle, unsupported, or capped.
daemon_service.py: supervised service harness; explicit operator-control and policy checks; does not claim unattended autonomy.
```

That is good. It shows the current root has learned some anti-overclaim discipline.

I also found the local autonomous-loop survival slice:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/ion_autonomous_loop.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_ion_autonomous_loop.py
```

That is not the same as production daemon authority. It is a survival slice around local loop mechanics and state projection.

I did not find exact current-root kernel files named:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_safe_mode.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_crash_recovery.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_health_check.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/daemon_audit_log.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/queue_lock.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/idempotent_event_executor.py
```

Nor did I find direct daemon tests under `ION/tests/` by filename in the V116 zip.

This does not prove those capabilities are absent in every form. Some may be embedded in newer service, policy, operator-control, receipt, or loop modules. But it does mean the current root should not be narrated as if the older production-daemon surface list has been fully restored and ratified.

The honest current claim is:

```text
V116 contains bounded daemon/arbitration/service organs and a local autonomous-loop survival slice.
V116 does not, by this journal inspection, justify a production daemon authority claim.
```

---

## 12. Archaeology daemon versus production daemon

The older corpus also contains the archaeology daemon / Vestige concept.

That concept is extremely important, but it must not be confused with the production daemon.

The archaeology daemon is:

```text
omnivorous reader
bounded writer
advisory surface
stale-authority detector
contradiction surfacer
provenance-gap watcher
```

It is not:

```text
release authority
source-code mutator
doctrine editor
dispatch sovereign
production executor
```

This distinction is one of ION’s most important recovery lessons.

The archaeology daemon exists because the corpus is contaminated and huge. It keeps buried contradictions visible. It is an anti-drift intelligence organ.

The production daemon exists to execute authorized reactions in runtime.

Both are daemon-like.

They do not have the same rights.

A future worker who collapses Vestige-style archaeology into production daemon authority will corrupt both.

---

## 13. The daemon and the user’s exhaustion

The daemon exists partly because the user should not have to keep saying:

```text
continue
proceed
spawn the correct agent
load the correct context
use the correct template
repair the stale surface
write the receipt
package the zip
```

But if the daemon is built wrongly, it makes the user’s exhaustion worse. It will create more outputs, more stale state, more logs, more contradictions, and more cleanup.

So the daemon must be judged by whether it reduces cognitive burden without increasing epistemic debt.

The right daemon should make the user say less because the system has become more lawful.

The wrong daemon makes the user say less because the system has become less supervised.

Those are opposites.

---

## 14. Shadow forms

Common daemon shadows:

```text
automation script
cron job with mythology
agent swarm trigger
silent recovery loop
autonomous loop overclaim
queue-draining theatre
status generator
hidden mutation worker
chat agent pretending to be daemon
MCP bridge mistaken for daemon law
safe-mode bypass patch
operator control treated as nuisance
```

The worst shadow is:

```text
The daemon got things done, therefore it was lawful.
```

ION must answer:

```text
What did it do?
Under what authority?
Against what contract?
With what lock?
With what receipt?
With what post-check?
With what recovery path?
With what explicit non-claim?
```

If those answers are missing, the daemon did not prove ION.

It only moved.

---

## 15. Recognition rule

A real ION daemon can be recognized by these traits:

```text
It can stop.
It can dry-run.
It can require approval.
It can refuse unsupported pressure.
It can cap itself.
It can classify its own blocked state.
It can resume from receipts.
It can emit ledgers.
It can obey operator holds.
It can keep automation below authority.
It can route agent activation as proposal instead of granting it.
It can treat safe mode as success when unsafe progress is prevented.
```

A false daemon can be recognized by these traits:

```text
It does more than it can explain.
It writes without authority classification.
It treats all triggers as work.
It hides blocked states.
It recovers from guesses.
It spawns agents because tasks are complex.
It mutates summaries or graph state because that seems helpful.
It equates success with lack of human interruption.
```

---

## 16. Do-not-reinvent rule

Do not reinvent daemon law as generic “automation.”

The mature daemon concept already exists in the corpus as a graph-aware, receipt-backed, queue-locked, idempotent, pausable, recoverable, auditable executor of authorized event reactions.

The work is not to invent that concept.

The work is to make the active root express it without overclaim, then prove the smallest executable path, then add missing daemon safety organs only when they are tied to tests, receipts, and operator-visible state.

Do not let “autonomous” become a magic word.

Do not let “daemon” become a magic word.

ION’s daemon is not magic.

It is disciplined continuity under motion.

---

## 17. Entry 13 closing belief

My current belief:

```text
The daemon is where ION either becomes a living runtime or becomes automated drift.
```

I believe the mature daemon doctrine already exists across the corpus. I also believe the current V116 root contains bounded daemon organs that correctly refuse production overclaim. But I do not yet believe the current root proves production daemon authority.

The next lawful posture is not to celebrate daemon existence.

It is to preserve the daemon boundary:

```text
bounded daemon organs: real
local autonomous survival slice: real within its test boundary
production daemon authority: not claimed
unattended autonomy: not claimed
agent-spawning daemon: blocked unless activation law and safe mode are proven
```

The daemon must eventually let ION continue without the user micromanaging every step.

But it must do so as law in motion, not motion pretending to be law.

That is the standard I will carry forward.


---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 14

## Front Door Product Surface and User-Facing Runtime

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** front door, product surface, user-facing runtime, Persona/Relay/Steward ingress and return, API/chat/IDE/operator entry, proof traces, and why the front door reveals law rather than bypassing it

---

## 0. Entry 14 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
The front door is governance made visible.
```

The shorter operational line:

```text
The front door is not the user interface of ION.
It is the lawful threshold where user intention becomes routeable system state.
```

This distinction matters because a lesser system treats the front door as chat, a CLI, an API endpoint, a dashboard, or a friendly prompt surface. ION cannot afford that mistake. The front door is where the user first meets ION, but it is also where the project is most likely to collapse its own law into performance.

If the front door is only chat, then user pressure becomes assistant improvisation.

If the front door is only an API, then request payloads become assumed authority.

If the front door is only a dashboard, then buttons can become hidden graph mutations.

If the front door is only Persona, then style can become truth.

If the front door is only Steward, then orchestration can speak as relationship.

If the front door is only Relay, then translation can impersonate authority.

ION’s front door must therefore preserve the entire user-facing boundary chain:

```text
User / operator / carrier request
→ Persona Interface ingress
→ Relay semantic-boundary packet
→ Steward routing envelope
→ runtime session / queue / work unit / dispatch
→ governed internal work
→ Relay return package
→ Persona Interface response package
→ user-facing response
→ receipts / proof trace / visible boundary statement
```

The front door is not where ION hides its complexity.

It is where ION makes its authority boundaries survivable.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

```text
Can a user talk to ION?
```

That is too small. Ordinary assistants already allow a user to talk. Ordinary CLIs already accept commands. Ordinary APIs already accept requests.

The real question is:

```text
Can ION receive human pressure without letting that pressure become ungoverned action, unverified truth, silent authority, or theatre?
```

The front door must answer a difficult set of simultaneous pressures:

```text
Be usable without demanding that the human understand the whole graph.
Be honest without drowning the human in internal machinery.
Be warm without fabricating authority or intimacy.
Be responsive without skipping proof.
Be powerful without making every request a mutation.
Be automated without bypassing the daemon, activation, graph, and summary-write gates.
Be visible without turning every internal state into user-facing noise.
```

ION’s front door is therefore not merely a product surface. It is a boundary discipline.

It exists to preserve the difference between:

```text
request and authority
language and intent
intent and work packet
work packet and mutation
response and truth
refusal and disappearance
UI action and graph write
operator convenience and production permission
```

---

## 2. Evidence surfaces inspected

For this entry I treated the current V116 root and the v4.0 encyclopedia as witnesses, not automatic authority. The most relevant current-root surfaces I inspected include:

```text
ION/02_architecture/FRONT_DOOR_RUNTIME_ENTRY_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/FRONT_DOOR_PERSONA_RELAY_STEWARD_BOUNDARY_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/FRONT_DOOR_CHAT_ORCHESTRATION_ADAPTER_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/FRONT_DOOR_SELF_MOUNT_BINDING_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_FRONT_DOOR_AUTONOMOUS_TEAM_WORKFLOW_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_MCP_FRONT_DOOR_AND_MOUNT_SESSION_PROTOCOL.md
ION/04_packages/kernel/front_door_runtime_entry.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/front_door_chat_orchestration.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/front_door_self_mount_binding.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/ion_front_door_proof_trace.py
ION/tests/test_kernel_ion_front_door_proof_trace.py
ION/05_context/current/ACTIVE_FRONT_DOOR_PROOF_TRACE.json
ION/05_context/current/ACTIVE_FRONT_DOOR_TEAM_PLAN.json
ION/08_ui/joc_cockpit_shell/FrontDoorProofTracePanel.tsx
```

The relevant encyclopedia surfaces include the runtime-lineage account of V17 and V26, the Front-Stage Council doctrine, the product-front-door boundary audit, and the chapter insert titled, in effect, that the front door is governance made visible.

The key evidence pattern is consistent across the corpus:

```text
ION already knows the front door cannot be a loose chat interface.
ION already knows Persona / Relay / Steward must remain separated.
ION already knows front-door productization is gated and not the same as daemon runtime.
ION already knows a chat request must become a graph-native or runtime-native packet before it can matter.
ION already knows response packages must carry boundaries, authority, receipts, and refusal posture.
```

So the issue is not conceptual absence.

The issue is activation, enforcement, and prevention of relapse.

---

## 3. What the front door is not

The front door is not simply:

```text
chat
CLI
API
IDE command
operator dashboard
browser window
Cursor parent chat
MCP bridge
Persona voice
```

All of these may be front-door carriers or entry forms. None of them is the front door by itself.

This matters because ION has repeatedly suffered from carrier collapse. A host surface appears convenient, then the system starts treating that host surface as if it owns role identity, authority, context, or state.

The front door must reject these collapses:

```text
chat request = authority
API request = permission
button click = mutation
Persona response = truth
Relay translation = decision
Steward routing = user-facing relationship
daemon dispatch = legal authority
MCP connection = ION mount
Cursor parent chat = ION itself
```

The front door does not grant authority.

It receives pressure and turns it into inspectable, routeable, bounded system material.

---

## 4. The front door as threshold

The front door is the threshold between ordinary human language and ION-native state.

Ordinary human language is ambiguous, emotional, compressed, urgent, metaphorical, impatient, and often domain-rich without being formally typed. ION cannot treat raw user language as governed truth. But ION also cannot demand that every user speak in internal packet syntax.

The front door solves this by splitting the threshold into roles.

```text
Persona Interface receives and renders human-facing meaning.
Relay translates across the semantic boundary.
Steward routes system-native work under authority.
```

That split is the difference between a helpful assistant and a governed runtime.

A helpful assistant can say:

