The presence of `NAVIGATE` and `TEST` does not mean unrestricted action. It means those modes require bounded authority, local/dev constraints, Steward gates, and receipts.

---

## 4. Seeing is a state transition only through receipt

Visual evidence is not automatically maintained state. A screenshot sitting in chat is a witness. A DOM dump in a folder is a witness. A visual comparison described by an assistant is a witness unless receipted. For visual evidence to become ION-compatible, it must be packetized and routed.

The mature loop appears to be:

```text
visual target selected
→ authority scope identified
→ observation captured or referenced
→ viewport / DOM / artifact metadata attached
→ findings classified
→ severity and confidence recorded
→ forbidden action flags preserved
→ diagnosis or before/after receipt emitted
→ Front-Stage Council claim if user-facing
→ patch request if implementation is required
→ post-patch visual verification
→ before/after receipt
→ closure or continued repair obligation
```

The important point is that the visual organ does not merely add “images” to ION. It adds a new class of evidence with its own authority membrane.

I currently believe this is why the V44–V55 visual line matters. It does not represent random expansion. It is a staged attempt to give ION sight without losing safety:

```text
V44 visual observation packet
V45 visual diagnosis receipt and browser harness plan
V46 local visual harness prototype
V48 before/after visual verification
V49 visual regression fixture runner plan
V50 local sandbox review
V54 visual run receipt to diagnosis binding
V55 visual closure graph projection and UI work surface
```

The branch numbers are less important than the staged discipline:

```text
observe before diagnose;
diagnose before harness;
harness before execution;
repeatability before autonomy;
closure before release;
projection before user-facing confidence.
```

---

## 5. Current-root evidence I inspected

In the V116 root I inspected the following visual surfaces:

```text
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_PERCEPTION_AND_INTERACTION_AGENT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_OBSERVATION_PACKET_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_DIAGNOSIS_RECEIPT_AND_BROWSER_HARNESS_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/LOCAL_VISUAL_HARNESS_PROTOTYPE_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_BEFORE_AFTER_VERIFICATION_LOOP_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_REGRESSION_FIXTURE_RUNNER_PLAN_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_RUN_RECEIPT_TO_DIAGNOSIS_BINDING_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/VISUAL_CLOSURE_GRAPH_PROJECTION_AND_UI_WORK_SURFACE_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/visual_perception_agent_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/visual_observation_packet.schema.json
ION/03_registry/visual_diagnosis_receipt.schema.json
ION/03_registry/local_visual_harness.schema.json
ION/03_registry/visual_before_after_verification.schema.json
ION/03_registry/visual_regression_fixture_runner.schema.json
ION/03_registry/visual_run_receipt_to_diagnosis_binding.schema.json
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_observation_packet.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_diagnosis_receipt.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/local_visual_harness.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_before_after_verification.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_regression_fixture_runner.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_run_receipt_to_diagnosis_binding.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/visual_sandbox_security_review.py
ION/05_context/fixtures/visual_regression/v49_demo_visual_fixture_suite.json
```

This is not a trivial surface. The current root contains a real visual evidence line with architecture, schema, policy, kernel modules, fixtures, and closure/binding concepts.

However, I must not overclaim.

My current-root observation is:

```text
The V116 root contains substantial bounded visual evidence machinery.
It does not, by that fact, grant unrestricted visual automation, production visual automation, arbitrary browser control, credential-sensitive action, or release authority.
```

This matters because visual systems are especially easy to overrepresent. “The visual harness exists” is not the same as “ION can safely operate a browser.” “A fixture runner exists” is not the same as “ION has autonomous visual regression CI.” “A before/after receipt exists” is not the same as “the issue is fixed in production.”

---

## 6. Visual authority ladder

I currently see the visual authority ladder like this:

```text
V0 — visual mention
A human or AI describes what something looks like. Weak witness only.

V1 — visual evidence reference
A screenshot, DOM snapshot, viewport record, accessibility tree, render trace, simulation frame, or browser-state artifact is referenced.

V2 — visual observation packet
The evidence is packetized with target, mode, viewport/artifact metadata, findings, confidence, severity, recommended action, and forbidden capability flags.

V3 — visual diagnosis receipt
The observation is interpreted into issue findings, risk, diagnosis verdict, and recommended patch/request obligations.

V4 — local harness capture
Authorized local/dev artifacts are hashed, referenced, and bound into visual observation/diagnosis without granting arbitrary browser control.

V5 — before/after verification
Pre/post evidence is compared, finding transitions are classified, and “looks fixed” claims become receiptable or rejected.

V6 — visual fixture run / regression plan
Repeatable cases are loaded, classified, and receipted under bounded local/dev or pre-captured evidence modes.

V7 — visual run closure binding
Run receipts, diagnosis receipts, before/after receipts, and closure claims are bound together.

V8 — visual closure projection
Visual closure enters the work surface / graph / UI state as bounded evidence.

V9 — production visual automation
Blocked unless separately ratified through stronger production gates.
```

This ladder is my journal interpretation, not a canonical protocol. Its function is to prevent collapse.

The key anti-collapse rule:

```text
Each rung may support the next, but no rung silently grants the rights of the rung above it.
```

---

## 7. The local harness boundary

The V46 local visual harness idea is important because it gives ION a safer first bridge into visual evidence.

The local harness can read explicitly supplied local/dev artifacts under the workspace root, hash and reference them, emit capture receipts, build observation packets, and build diagnosis receipts. It can recommend implementation-agent action through Steward review.

But it must not:

```text
control arbitrary browsers;
use credentials;
submit forms;
make purchases;
delete or mutate user data;
perform persistent DOM mutation;
bypass Steward/VZ review;
claim production readiness or production visual automation authority.
```

This is exactly the kind of boundary ION needs. It lets the system gain sight without smuggling in agency.

The stronger line:

```text
Local visual evidence may enter as proof material.
Local visual harness authority does not become computer-use authority.
```

This distinction must stay alive. Otherwise future agents will treat a screenshot harness as permission to operate a user's computer.

---

## 8. Before/after verification and the end of “looks fixed”

One of the most important visual organs is before/after verification.

The ordinary AI failure is:

```text
I edited the code, so the UI should be fixed.
```

ION's response should be:

```text
Show the before evidence.
Show the after evidence.
Classify the finding transition.
Emit the receipt.
Then decide what claim is allowed.
```

A visual repair can have many possible states:

```text
verified
partial
regression or new issue
missing after evidence
change evidence requiring review
no actionable change
blocked by Steward
```

This prevents the assistant from turning implementation effort into completion language.

The key standard:

```text
No visual completion claim without after-evidence appropriate to the claim class.
```

For a low-risk provisional statement, this may only require scoped language: “I changed the layout code; visual verification is still needed.” For a formal artifact/release claim, it requires actual before/after evidence and receipts.

---

## 9. Visual contradiction as repair trigger

Visual evidence has a special relationship to conversational repair.

A visual contradiction occurs when rendered/observed evidence conflicts with a claim. Examples:

```text
assistant says UI is fixed, screenshot still shows overflow;
assistant says DOM was changed, but only screenshot was inspected;
assistant claims visual verification, but no before/after receipt exists;
source-code expectation says route works, browser state shows blocked navigation;
simulation design intent says stable orbit, rendered frame shows collapse;
accessibility tree contradicts visible affordance.
```

When this happens, the correct ION move is not ordinary apology. The correct move is claim repair.

Possible repair classes:

```text
VISUAL_RECHECK
FACT_CORRECTION
AUTHORITY_DOWNGRADE
SCOPE_NARROWING
ARTIFACT_PATCH_OBLIGATION
POST_PATCH_VISUAL_VERIFY_REQUIRED
```

The key law:

```text
Visual contradiction downgrades claim authority until the contradiction is resolved or bounded.
```

This is where visual evidence becomes part of ION's epistemic immune system. It prevents fluent completion language from surviving contact with the rendered world.

---

## 10. Computer-use authority and forbidden capabilities

The visual organ is adjacent to one of the most dangerous capability boundaries: computer use.

Seeing a screen is not the same as acting on it. Navigating a local/dev preview is not the same as operating a user account. Reading DOM is not the same as mutating DOM. Running pre-captured fixture checks is not the same as live browsing. Clicking in a sandbox is not the same as submitting a form.

The V116 visual modules repeatedly preserve forbidden capability flags such as:

```text
unrestricted_browser_control: false
browser_execution: false
external_network_access: false
credential_or_session_import: false
account_operation: false
destructive_action: false
form_submission: false
purchase_or_submission: false
persistent_dom_mutation: false
production_visual_automation: false
production_authority: false
```

That pattern is meaningful. It shows the visual line is trying to preserve evidence rights while blocking dangerous action rights.

I currently believe this is one of ION's strongest safety insights:

```text
Capability must be decomposed before it is granted.
```

A weak system asks:

```text
Can the AI use the computer?
```

ION should ask:

```text
Can it observe this local artifact?
Can it hash this screenshot?
Can it read this DOM snapshot?
Can it navigate this local preview?
Can it click without side effects?
Can it type into a non-submitting sandbox field?
Can it run this fixture?
Can it request a patch?
Can it mutate source files?
Can it operate an account?
Can it submit a form?
Can it make irreversible changes?
```

Those are different rights. They must not collapse into one permission.

---

## 11. The relation between visual evidence and UI/JOC cockpit

The Visual Agent is not only for UI debugging. It is also part of ION's own self-observability.

If ION builds a cockpit, the cockpit itself becomes a rendered truth surface. It is not enough for kernel state to exist. The operator must be able to see whether the cockpit displays the state correctly:

```text
current objective;
current carrier mount;
active work packet;
spawn plan;
context package status;
template gate status;
proof status;
Steward queue;
blocked human gates;
visual verification state;
next packet or stop reason.
```

The cockpit can lie by omission, stale render, bad hydration, broken layout, hidden error, or misleading status label.

Therefore:

```text
The UI that proves ION must itself be visually verified by ION.
```

This is not recursion for its own sake. It is how the system becomes operator-trustworthy. A cockpit that claims “all green” while the underlying state is blocked, stale, or unmounted is worse than no cockpit.

Rendered truth applies to ION's own governance surfaces.

---

## 12. Visual evidence and embodied/expressive telemetry

The visual organ also touches future avatar/expression/affective telemetry surfaces.

If ION eventually renders expressive state — hesitation, confidence, restraint, urgency, uncertainty, repair, drift, verification — that rendered expression must remain representationally honest. It must not fabricate human suffering, coercive intimacy, dependence, or false personhood. But it may become a visual dashboard of system state.

This creates a subtle future requirement:

```text
Expressive render must be visually inspectable for representational integrity.
```

A future avatar gesture could mislead. A color status could overstate confidence. A progress animation could imply work is happening when no lawful worker is active. A facial expression could falsely signal intimacy or fear. A badge could imply production readiness.

Visual truth is therefore not limited to product screenshots. It includes the rendered behavior of the AI presence itself.

This connects Entry 17 back to Entry 6. The Front-Stage Council governs user-facing truth; the Visual Agent can witness whether the rendered user-facing surface obeys that truth.

---

## 13. Common visual shadows

The mature visual organ coexists with several stale or dangerous shadows.

### Shadow 1: Code-implies-render

```text
The code patch looks correct, so the UI is fixed.
```

Repair:

```text
Downgrade to implementation patch completed; require visual verification before UI fixed claim.
```

### Shadow 2: Screenshot-implies-action-authority

```text
The system can see a screenshot, so it can operate the app.
```

Repair:

```text
Observation is witness; action requires separate authority.
```

### Shadow 3: Browser harness implies browser autonomy

```text
A browser harness plan exists, so autonomous browser control is available.
```

Repair:

```text
Harness stage, mode, and forbidden capabilities determine rights.
```

### Shadow 4: Fixture plan implies regression CI

```text
A visual regression fixture runner plan exists, so visual regression testing is production-ready.
```

Repair:

```text
Repeatability planning is not production automation.
```

### Shadow 5: Before/after exists implies fixed

```text
There is before/after evidence, so the issue is fixed.
```

Repair:

```text
The before/after receipt must classify the transition; it may be partial, regression, or blocked.
```

### Shadow 6: Visual Agent as separate sovereign

```text
The Visual Agent is an independent operator role with broad authority.
```

Repair:

```text
Visual Agent is a bounded support organ; mutation routes through Steward and implementation/change receipts.
```

### Shadow 7: Rendered truth as aesthetic preference

```text
Visual evidence is just subjective UI taste.
```

Repair:

```text
Rendered truth includes layout, accessibility, flow completion, state visibility, artifact correctness, and contradiction evidence; some judgments may be aesthetic, but the evidence layer is not optional.
```

---

## 14. What I believe ION is trying to become here

ION is trying to become a system that can say:

```text
I changed the code.
I have not yet checked the render.
Therefore I cannot claim the UI is fixed.
```

And later:

```text
I captured before evidence.
I captured after evidence.
I compared finding transitions.
The original alignment issue is resolved.
A new overflow issue appeared.
The correct claim is partial repair, not completion.
```

And later still:

```text
The visual issue is verified closed under local/dev fixture scope.
This does not prove production release readiness.
```

That is the level of honesty ION is seeking.

A normal assistant wants to sound done.

ION wants to know what kind of done is lawful.

---

## 15. The deeper ontology of visual evidence

Visual evidence is a bridge between symbolic intent and encountered reality.

Code is symbolic. Docs are symbolic. Tests are symbolic. Templates are symbolic. Context packages are symbolic. Even receipts are symbolic.

A render is where the symbolic system becomes perceptible.

That does not make visual evidence infallible. Screenshots can be stale. DOM snapshots can be incomplete. Viewports can mislead. Accessibility trees can omit lived experience. Human visual judgment can be biased. But visual evidence has a special role because it can falsify a symbolic claim at the product boundary.

This gives ION a philosophical commitment:

```text
Truth must remain answerable to the surface where the user encounters it.
```

For a UI, that surface is rendered behavior. For a simulation, it is rendered dynamics and measured state. For a document, it is actual artifact text. For an orchestration dashboard, it is visible state plus underlying trace. For an avatar, it is rendered expression plus representational integrity.

ION is not anti-symbolic. ION is built from symbolic law. But symbolic law must remain grounded in encountered evidence.

---

## 16. Working doctrine I now carry forward

My current working doctrine:

```text
1. Rendered behavior is part of truth.
2. Source-code correctness is not product correctness.
3. Visual observation may enter as witness.
4. Visual diagnosis may enter as interpreted evidence.
5. Visual contradiction can trigger repair and claim-class downgrade.
6. Patch requests are not patches.
7. Patches are not visual verification.
8. Visual verification is not production release.
9. Browser harness planning is not unrestricted computer use.
10. Local/dev visual authority is not account authority.
11. Before/after receipts are required for durable visual completion claims.
12. The cockpit that proves ION must itself be visually truthful.
13. Visual evidence must be routed through Front-Stage Council when user-facing.
14. Visual mutation requires Steward authority and implementation/change receipts.
15. The Visual Agent is a bounded organ of perception and explanation, not a sovereign operator.
```

This doctrine should constrain future work on UI, JOC cockpit, image/screenshot analysis, browser harnesses, visual regression, simulation review, avatar telemetry, and any computer-use integration.

---

## 17. Current uncertainty

I am confident that ION contains substantial visual doctrine and bounded visual machinery.

I am not yet confident that the current root has a fully unified visual runtime path from screenshot/DOM capture through observation packet, diagnosis receipt, patch request, implementation change, post-patch verification, graph/work-surface projection, and cockpit visibility.

I am not yet confident that all visual protocols are correctly wired to tests.

I am not yet confident that the visual closure graph projection is integrated into the broader canonical graph/state mutation law from Entry 10.

I am not yet confident that the UI/JOC surfaces consistently expose visual evidence status in a way that prevents operator overtrust.

Therefore I should not claim “ION has solved visual operation.”

The truthful claim is narrower:

```text
ION already contains a mature recognition that rendered truth must become governed evidence, and the current root contains substantial bounded visual receipt machinery, but production visual/computer-use authority remains blocked unless separately ratified.
```

---

## 18. Next journal implication

This entry points to the next organ:

```text
UI/JOC Cockpit, Work-Surface Projection, and Operator Visibility.
```

The visual organ says rendered truth matters. The cockpit asks: rendered truth of what? It should render the maintained work surface itself: packets, mounts, context, proofs, receipts, gates, risks, blockers, and next continuation.

If ION cannot show its state, it will force the user back into trust-by-chat.

And trust-by-chat is exactly what ION was built to overcome.

---

## 19. Closing line

```text
ION learns to see so that it can stop pretending text is the world.
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 18

## UI/JOC Cockpit, Work-Surface Projection, and Operator Visibility

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** JOC/cockpit surfaces, UI work-surface projection, operator visibility, cockpit view models, proof visibility, reactive OS streams, approval queues, dry-run handoffs, non-authority UI boundaries, and the difference between seeing ION state and granting ION authority

---

## 0. Entry 18 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
Visibility is not decoration.
Visibility is part of ION's epistemic safety system.
```

The shorter operational line:

```text
ION cannot be trusted as invisible orchestration.
```

ION was born from the failure of conversational AI work to preserve, prove, route, and repair its own state. If the system keeps its real state hidden behind fluent assistant speech, it recreates the exact substrate it was designed to overcome. The user should not have to infer from tone whether an agent is mounted, whether context loaded, whether a template was selected, whether a proof gate passed, whether Steward integrated the return, whether a repair remains pending, whether a visual check exists, whether a daemon is merely planned, or whether a carrier has actually obeyed ION law.

The cockpit is therefore not a cosmetic dashboard.

It is the rendered truth surface of the maintained work surface.

ION's state must be visible enough that a human operator, weak carrier, or future AI worker can distinguish:

```text
claim from proof
plan from execution
proposal from authority
context loaded from context assumed
template selected from task improvised
worker output from Steward-integrated state
visual witness from visual verification
dashboards from production authority
operator approval from dry-run preview
blocked capability from granted capability
```

A cockpit that merely looks powerful is a danger. It can launder theatre into confidence. A real ION cockpit must render boundaries as aggressively as it renders progress.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

```text
Should ION have a UI?
```

ION already contains substantial UI/JOC doctrine, schemas, policies, component contracts, view models, and operator projection surfaces.

The harder question is:

```text
How can ION render its own state without turning visibility into authority?
```

This distinction is central. A cockpit can make a system feel real even when the backend is incomplete. A beautiful shell can hide missing proof gates. A timeline can show activity without showing evidence. A component can say "dispatch ready" while the underlying approval is dry-run only. A reactive stream can display events without telling the operator which capabilities remain blocked. A visual panel can show screenshots without proving post-patch verification. A context explorer can show routes without proving those routes are loaded into a role's current context package.

ION must therefore make the UI not only informative, but juridical. The UI must show rights.

Every rendered panel should answer:

```text
What is this surface showing?
What evidence supports it?
What claim lane does it occupy?
What authority does it have?
What authority does it explicitly not have?
What action, if any, is allowed next?
What must be repaired before progress can continue?
```

If the cockpit does not answer those questions, it can become another hallucinated front end.

---

## 2. Evidence surfaces inspected

For this entry, I treated the uploaded encyclopedia and current V116 root as evidence, not final authority. I inspected the following current-root surfaces in the V116 project zip:

```text
.cursor/commands/ion-cockpit.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V56_ION_JOC_COCKPIT_SHELL_COMPONENT_CONTRACTS_LOCK.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_COCKPIT_SHELL_COMPONENT_CONTRACT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_COGNITIVE_EXPLORER_AND_CONTEXT_ROUTE_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_DISPATCH_AUTHORIZATION_GOVERNOR_VERDICT_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_DRY_RUN_DISPATCH_EXECUTION_TRACE_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_HANDOFF_PACKAGE_ASSEMBLY_PLAN_AND_CHECKSUM_PREVIEW_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_MISSION_DISPATCH_AND_MODEL_ROUTE_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_OPERATOR_APPROVAL_QUEUE_AND_DRY_RUN_HANDOFF_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_OPERATOR_REVIEWED_EXPORT_HANDOFF_MANIFEST_PREVIEW_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_OPERATOR_REVIEWED_RESULT_SAVE_PROPOSAL_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_PROVIDER_ADAPTER_READINESS_AND_SELECTOR_HEALTH_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_REACTIVE_OS_STREAM_AND_AUTOMATION_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_RELEASE_CANDIDATE_PREVIEW_AND_PREFLIGHT_VERIFIER_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_SYNTHETIC_RESPONSE_CAPTURE_AND_EXTRACTION_RECEIPT_PREVIEW_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_SYNTHETIC_SYNTHESIS_AND_ROUTE_RESULT_PREVIEW_PROTOCOL.md
ION/03_registry/joc_cockpit_layout_manifest.yaml
ION/03_registry/ui_work_surface_projection_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/ui_work_surface_projection.schema.json
ION/04_packages/kernel/ion_cockpit_view_model.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/ui_work_surface_projection.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_reactive_os_stream_view_model.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_operator_approval_queue_view_model.py
```

The current root appears to contain not just a UI wish, but a significant UI/JOC projection doctrine. It names component zones, projection surfaces, reactive loops, forbidden capabilities, dry-run approval states, and cockpit view-model verification organs.

But I must not claim a complete production cockpit. The evidence supports this narrower claim:

```text
ION contains a mature and repeated recognition that the work surface must become operator-visible through JOC/cockpit projections; the current V116 root contains substantial contracts, schemas, policies, and kernel view-model organs for that visibility; but production cockpit authority, live UI completeness, and fully wired runtime observability remain unproven here.
```

---

## 3. Cockpit as projection organ

The current JOC cockpit shell protocol states the correct thesis in its own terms: the cockpit is not a dashboard beside ION; it is a projection organ. That is exactly right.

A dashboard usually means:

```text
Here are metrics about a system.
```

An ION cockpit must mean:

```text
Here is the system's current maintained state, its evidence, its authority boundaries, its pending repairs, and its lawful next actions.
```

That is more than analytics. It is ontology rendered.

ION's cockpit should project the maintained work surface itself: not only what is happening, but how the happening is authorized, constrained, evidenced, and repairable.

The V116 cockpit contract requires shell regions:

```text
TOP_BAR
LEFT_RAIL
MAIN_WORK_SURFACE
RIGHT_INSPECTOR
BOTTOM_TIMELINE
```

This is not arbitrary layout. Each region has a governance meaning:

```text
TOP_BAR:
  current authority posture, front-stage/council status, production boundary, carrier mount state

LEFT_RAIL:
  navigation across lawful surfaces, not random app tabs

MAIN_WORK_SURFACE:
  current packet, objective, route, context, active role, and task surface

RIGHT_INSPECTOR:
  claims, receipts, evidence, proof gates, visual witnesses, repair obligations

BOTTOM_TIMELINE:
  events, automation phases, handoffs, blocked capabilities, repairs, continuation pressure
```

A UI without this structure may still be useful, but it is not yet an ION-native cockpit.

---

## 4. Required projection surfaces

The V116 root's cockpit layout manifest and UI work-surface policy converge around a set of required projection surfaces:

```text
MAINTAINED_WORK_SURFACE_OVERVIEW
FRONT_STAGE_COUNCIL_STATE_STRIP
CLAIM_AND_RECEIPT_RAIL
VISUAL_EVIDENCE_LENS
MISSION_DISPATCH_AND_MODEL_ROUTE_PANEL
CONTEXT_GRAPH_COGNITIVE_EXPLORER
REACTIVE_OS_STREAM
CONVERSATIONAL_REPAIR_QUEUE
BROWSER_SESSION_AUTOMATION_OVERLAY
COMPUTE_AND_COST_ROUTER
```

These surfaces reveal what ION believes a serious cockpit must show.

It must show maintained work, not just files.

It must show front-stage claim authority, not just responses.

It must show receipts, not just summaries.

It must show visual evidence, not just code state.

It must show mission routing and model/provider choice, not just output.

It must show context graph navigation, not just a flat context blob.

It must show automation streams, not hidden daemon behaviour.

It must show repair queues, not buried apologies.

It must show browser/session automation as bounded overlay, not unrestricted control.

It must show compute/cost routing, because model selection is an authority, quality, and economics problem.

This is a profoundly correct shape. It says ION's UI is not a shell around work. It is the visible grammar of lawful work.

---

## 5. The cockpit must render non-authority

The most important feature of the cockpit may be not what it enables, but what it visibly refuses.

The V116 UI/JOC surfaces repeatedly mark forbidden capabilities false:

```text
production_authority
unrestricted_browser_control
credential_access
external_network_authority
account_operation
destructive_action
form_submission
purchase_or_submission
persistent_dom_mutation
production_visual_automation
```

The operator approval queue adds further forbidden actions:

```text
live_external_model_dispatch
browser_session_mutation
credential_access
form_submission
paid_cloud_launch
source_summary_rewrite
canonical_graph_write
unrestricted_agent_activation
production_authority
```

This is crucial. A normal UI tends to hide what is not possible. ION's cockpit should render blocked authorities as first-class state.

Why?

Because users and agents both over-infer from visible competence. If the cockpit can show a mission route, a model target, a dry-run handoff, and a synthetic response preview, a weak operator or agent may infer that live dispatch is approved. If it can show browser session overlays, they may infer browser mutation authority. If it can show release-candidate preflight, they may infer production release authority.

ION must not let interface richness become authority laundering.

Therefore:

```text
A real ION cockpit must show blocked capabilities as clearly as available capabilities.
```

The UI's job is not to make ION look powerful. The UI's job is to make ION's exact rights visible.

---

## 6. Reactive OS stream

The V116 reactive OS stream protocol contains one of the strongest UI laws:

```text
Automation is visible when the UI can show what loop ran, what phase it reached, what evidence supports it, what claim class it occupies, what action is blocked, and what repair remains.
```

This is exactly the standard needed to defeat invisible automation theatre.

A weak automation log says:

```text
Ran workflow.
Done.
```

An ION reactive stream should say:

```text
Loop: CONTEXT_PROJECTION_LOOP
Phase: context package compiled
Status: OK
Claim lane: C1
Rendered surface: CONTEXT_GRAPH_COGNITIVE_EXPLORER
Evidence refs: [receipt path, packet path]
Authority scope: projection only
Repair required: false
Blocked capabilities: [canonical_graph_write]
```

Or:

```text
Loop: CONVERSATIONAL_REPAIR_LOOP
Phase: artifact patch obligation identified
Status: REPAIR
Claim lane: C2
Rendered surface: CONVERSATIONAL_REPAIR_QUEUE
Evidence refs: [repair receipt]
Authority scope: repair proposal only
Repair required: true
Blocked capabilities: [production_authority]
```

The reactive stream is therefore not merely a log. It is a claim-classed, evidence-bearing, authority-scoped event projection.

That is ION-native observability.

---

## 7. Operator approval queue

The V62 operator approval queue doctrine is especially important because it prevents a common escalation failure.

A mission can be previewed. A route can be selected. A dispatch can appear authorized. A model/provider target can be evaluated. But that still does not mean live execution is allowed.

The operator queue creates a visible checkpoint:

```text
route preview
→ dispatch authorization verdict
→ operator approval queue card
→ operator decision state
→ dry-run handoff receipt preview
→ future live driver branch, if separately authorized
```

The key rule is:

```text
Even approved entries may only create a dry-run handoff preview unless a future live driver branch is separately authorized.
```

That is a subtle but vital authority membrane. It separates:

```text
operator review
operator approval
dry-run handoff
live external dispatch
```

Without this separation, a UI can accidentally turn human approval into live mutation authority. ION cannot allow that.

A human click is not automatically authority. A human approval must be explicit, scoped, evidenced, and bound to the exact action class it authorizes.

---

## 8. Cockpit versus chat

The cockpit exists partly because chat is too fluent.

Chat can say:

```text
The carrier is mounted.
The context package loaded.
The worker returned proof.
The repair is complete.
The release is verified.
```

But unless the system projects the underlying packet, receipt, proof, and boundary state, the user is still trapped inside trust-by-language.

The cockpit should not replace Persona. It should discipline Persona.

Persona can explain. The cockpit should show.

Relay can ground. The cockpit should reveal provenance.

Steward can authorize. The cockpit should expose verdict and scope.

Workers can return. The cockpit should show whether the return is accepted, rejected, partial, blocked, or pending.

This is how ION makes conversation accountable.

The user-facing assistant should never be the only evidence that ION operated.

---

## 9. The cockpit as anti-drift instrument

The cockpit is not only for convenience. It is an anti-drift instrument.

It should make common ION failure modes visible:

```text
wrong root selected
stale archive consumed as current law
context package missing
compiled bundle missing
carrier mounted without role authority
template selected incorrectly
template action proof missing
CONTEXT PROOF missing
Steward integration queue not drained
repair classified but artifact not patched
visual verification claimed but no before/after evidence
release package generated but checksum/manifest absent
operator approval treated as live dispatch
production boundary falsely implied
```

This is one reason UI matters so much to this project. ION has suffered from enormous conceptual and documentary sophistication coexisting with weak live visibility. When state is invisible, fluent agents overclaim. When overclaim is invisible, the user must fight the system through chat. That is exactly the condition ION exists to repair.

A good cockpit should reduce the user's cognitive burden by making drift mechanically visible.

---

## 10. Cockpit and the maintained work surface

The maintained work surface is the governed cognitive field in which user intent, AI synthesis, artifact evidence, protocols, tools, and emerging insight remain mutually visible long enough to produce durable progress.

The cockpit is the rendered projection of that field.

It should display at least:

```text
active objective
active work packet
active role spawn plan
carrier mount state
current role context package
compiled context bundle status
context load receipt status
template contract selected
template action proof status
CONTEXT PROOF status
Steward integration queue
accepted/rejected/partial returns
repair queue
visual evidence lane
release/evidence lane
operator gates
human approval states
blocked authorities
next lawful move
```

This is not a wish list. It is the minimum visual substrate needed for ION to stop forcing the user to parse invisible workflows.

If the cockpit does not show the active work packet and proof gates, it is not yet showing ION's live loop.

If it does not show repair obligations, it is not protecting continuity.

If it does not show blocked authority, it is not protecting truth.

---

## 11. Cockpit and context navigation

ION's context system is too large to be represented as a flat document. The cockpit must eventually become a navigable context instrument.

It should expose:

```text
main context package
rolling context windows
route-deeper map
per-role context timeline
context delta writeback
context budget/token cost
staleness/lifecycle state
source/witness/current authority state
```

The cockpit should not merely show "the agent has context." It should show what kind of context, what temporal rights it has, what routes are available, and what deeper context would cost or risk.

This is where Entry 2 and Entry 9 meet the UI.

A context package is an epistemic body.

Temporal rights decide whether that body is hot, warm, cold, dormant, superseded, or quarantined.

The cockpit should make that visible.

Otherwise, context law remains hidden doctrine.

---

## 12. Cockpit and cost/model routing

ION's eventual API/model/provider layer cannot be treated as a simple model picker.

The cockpit's `ComputeCostRouter` and provider adapter readiness surfaces suggest a more mature understanding: model choice is a governed dispatch problem involving quality, cost, latency, authority, tool access, evidence requirements, provider readiness, and operator approval.

The cockpit should eventually show:

```text
candidate model/provider routes
why each route is appropriate
cost and quality class
latency expectations
allowed authority level
blocked capabilities
fallback path
operator approval requirement
receipt path
```

This matters because future ION cannot become serious if it hides economic and capability routing behind assistant intuition. If one task needs a premium model and another needs cheap bulk synthesis, that should be an inspectable route decision, not a vibe.

But again: showing a route is not live dispatch authority.

The UI must preserve that distinction.

---

## 13. Cockpit and visual/browser overlays

The cockpit's browser/session automation overlays must be especially careful.

Visual/browser integration is one of the easiest places for authority to inflate. A system that can show a browser overlay may appear to have browser control. A system that can inspect DOM may appear to have permission to mutate DOM. A system that can show a fixture may appear to have production visual automation.

ION's UI must mark these boundaries continuously:

```text
OBSERVE_ONLY
DIAGNOSE_ONLY
PATCH_REQUEST_ONLY
LOCAL_DEV_VERIFY_ONLY
DRY_RUN_ONLY
OPERATOR_APPROVAL_REQUIRED
BLOCKED_CREDENTIAL_ACTION
BLOCKED_FORM_SUBMISSION
BLOCKED_DESTRUCTIVE_ACTION
```

The visual evidence lens should make visible not only what was seen, but what seeing does and does not authorize.

This continues Entry 17's law:

```text
ION learns to see so that it can stop pretending text is the world.
```

Entry 18 adds:

```text
ION must show what it sees so that sight does not become secret authority.
```

---

## 14. Current-root reading

My reading of the V116 root is that ION contains a surprisingly mature cockpit ontology. The JOC surfaces are not merely one UI plan; they form a layered product-visibility grammar:

```text
V55: visual closure graph projection and UI work surface
V56: JOC cockpit shell component contracts
V57: reactive OS stream and automation view model
V58: cognitive explorer and context route view model
V59: mission dispatch and model route view model
V60/V61: dispatch authorization / governor verdict surfaces
V62: operator approval queue and dry-run handoff
V63+: result save proposals, export handoff manifests, synthetic capture, release candidate preview, provider readiness, and related view models
```

I should verify exact version lines in the repo before making formal claims, but the filenames and sampled contents already show a strong pattern: ION repeatedly tried to turn invisible runtime authority into visible, bounded, receipt-bearing view models.

That is not a side quest. That is core ION.

---

## 15. What would make this real

The cockpit becomes real only when the UI path is fed by actual runtime state rather than manually curated demonstration data.

The minimal real cockpit path should be:

```text
ACTIVE_WORK_PACKET.json
+ ACTIVE_ROLE_SPAWN_PLAN.json
+ compiled role context bundle / context load receipt
+ template/action gate result
+ worker return ledger
+ Steward integration queue
+ repair queue
+ visual evidence lane
+ operator gates
→ kernel projection
→ ACTIVE_COCKPIT_VIEW_MODEL.json
→ rendered JOC shell
→ operator action / no-action decision
```

A static mockup is not enough.

A generated JSON fixture is not enough.

A cockpit command is not enough.

A real cockpit must preserve the causal chain from runtime state to rendered surface.

---

## 16. Shadow forms

The cockpit has its own dangerous shadows:

```text
beautiful dashboard without live state
mock UI mistaken for product proof
view model mistaken for backend authority
operator approval mistaken for live execution
route preview mistaken for dispatch
visual overlay mistaken for browser control
reactive stream mistaken for daemon authority
release preview mistaken for release verification
context explorer mistaken for loaded context
blocked capability hidden behind disabled button
```

These shadows must be named because UI is persuasive. A beautiful cockpit can make ION feel finished before it is true.

ION must not become theatre with better graphics.

---

## 17. Non-production boundary

This journal entry does not claim:

```text
production cockpit complete
JOC UI fully implemented
all view models tested
all cockpit projections wired to live state
operator approvals enforceable in production
browser automation authorized
provider dispatch authorized
release preview equals release verification
visual overlay equals visual authority
```

The correct claim is narrower:

```text
ION already contains a mature cockpit/projection doctrine and substantial V116 UI/JOC view-model organs, but the production cockpit remains an unproven projection-and-enforcement surface unless live runtime wiring, tests, render verification, operator-gate behavior, and non-authority boundaries are verified.
```

---

## 18. Doctrine emerging from this entry

1. The cockpit is a projection organ, not a decorative dashboard.
2. UI must render rights, not merely data.
3. Blocked capabilities are first-class state.
4. A reactive stream is not a log unless it carries loop, phase, evidence, claim lane, authority, and repair state.
5. Operator approval must be explicit, scoped, evidenced, and distinguished from live execution.
6. The cockpit disciplines Persona by making backend truth inspectable.
7. Context navigation must expose routes, budgets, temporal rights, and staleness.
8. Model/provider routing must become inspectable dispatch logic, not assistant preference.
9. Visual/browser overlays must show observation rights separately from mutation rights.
10. A static mockup does not prove an ION cockpit.
11. A view model does not grant backend authority.
12. Production cockpit claims require live state wiring, tests, rendered verification, and operator-gate proof.

---

## 19. Current uncertainty

I am confident that ION contains mature JOC/cockpit doctrine and substantial current-root view-model machinery.

I am not yet confident that the V116 cockpit path is fully wired from active runtime packets to rendered UI.

I am not yet confident that `ACTIVE_COCKPIT_VIEW_MODEL.json` is produced and consumed by a complete rendered shell under current runtime conditions.

I am not yet confident that all cockpit view models are integrated into one coherent UI layer rather than existing as many adjacent proof surfaces.

I am not yet confident that the cockpit consistently displays blocked authority more visibly than progress.

I am not yet confident that the user can currently operate ION through the cockpit without falling back to chat trust.

Therefore I should not claim the UI/JOC cockpit is solved.

The truthful claim is:

```text
ION has recognized that state must become visible, and it has built many of the projection organs needed for that visibility; the remaining challenge is not UI imagination, but live, bounded, proof-fed, non-authority-laundering runtime projection.
```

---

## 20. Next journal implication

This entry points to the next organ:

```text
Model Routing, Provider Selection, Cost/Quality Governance, and API Runtime.
```

The cockpit exposes a Compute/Cost Router and mission/model route panels. That means ION is not merely an internal orchestration substrate. It is trying to become a multi-provider, cost-aware, quality-aware, authority-aware runtime for AI work.

That organ must be handled carefully. Model dispatch is not just a performance optimization. It is a governance and economics surface.

---

## 21. Closing line

```text
ION must render its own state so the user does not have to believe the voice.
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 19

## Model Routing, Provider Selection, Cost/Quality Governance, and API Runtime

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** model routing, provider economics, cost/quality selection, API runtime entry, budget and rate governance, provider adapter readiness, model-call receipts, privacy/data-handling lanes, local/private execution lanes, cross-model audit, and the distinction between dispatch intelligence and dispatch authority

---

## 0. Entry 19 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
A model call is not merely compute.
A model call is an authority-bearing economic, epistemic, temporal, privacy, and evidentiary act.
```

The shorter operational line:

```text
ION must not merely call models.
ION must govern why a model is called, what it is allowed to see, what it is allowed to decide, what it costs, what it proves, and how its output enters state.
```

This entry matters because ION is not meant to remain a single-model chat project. It is trying to become an AI operating substrate capable of routing work across carriers, models, providers, local/private lanes, batch lanes, review lanes, and future API execution surfaces. That ambition is powerful, but it is also dangerous. If model routing becomes a performance hack, ION loses its own law. If provider selection becomes merely “use the best model” or “use the cheapest model,” ION collapses epistemic authority, economic authority, privacy authority, and runtime authority into a naive scheduler.

A model route is not neutral.

Choosing a model determines:

```text
what context leaves the system;
which provider receives it;
what privacy/data-handling regime applies;
what capability tier is trusted;
what latency class is tolerated;
what cost is incurred;
what failure modes are expected;
what review route is required;
what receipt must be emitted;
what future claims may cite the result;
what human/operator visibility is owed.
```

Therefore model routing is not simply dispatch. It is governed epistemic logistics.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

```text
Can ION route to OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Cerebras, local models, or future providers?
```

The current V116 root already contains substantial surfaces for model economics, provider registries, model capability registries, pricing registries, rate limits, routing policies, data-handling policies, work-class model policies, API runtime entry, rate governors, cost-quality routers, provider adapter readiness, and JOC route/providing-state projection.

The harder question is:

```text
How can ION use many models without letting model plurality dissolve continuity law?
```

Multi-provider capability can make ION stronger, but only if each provider call is more governed than a normal chat completion, not less.

A single assistant can hallucinate.

A multi-model system can hallucinate with better branding.

A router can save cost.

A router can also choose a cheap model for work that required high-authority review.

A premium model can improve quality.

A premium model can also launder authority merely because it is expensive or famous.

A consensus call can detect disagreement.

A consensus call can also manufacture false confidence if all models share the same stale context or if the wrong question was routed.

ION’s model economy must therefore be governed by work class, authority class, context sensitivity, privacy requirements, budget constraints, provider capacity, receipt obligations, and Steward review — not provider reputation alone.

---

## 2. Current-root surfaces inspected

In the V116 root, I found the following relevant bootstrap locks:

```text
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V56_MODEL_ECONOMICS_REGISTRY_SKELETONS_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V57_MODEL_ROUTER_AND_COST_QUALITY_ROUTING_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V58_BUDGET_AND_API_RATE_GOVERNORS_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V59_MISSION_DISPATCH_AND_MODEL_ROUTE_VIEW_MODEL_LOCK.md
ION/00_BOOTSTRAP/V64_PROVIDER_ADAPTER_READINESS_AND_SELECTOR_HEALTH_VIEW_MODEL_LOCK.md
```

Relevant architecture protocols include:

```text
ION/02_architecture/MODEL_ROUTING_AND_PROVIDER_ECONOMICS_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/MODEL_ROUTER_AND_COST_QUALITY_ROUTING_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/COST_QUALITY_MARGIN_ROUTING_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/API_RATE_GOVERNOR_AND_PROVIDER_LIMIT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/BUDGET_AND_API_RATE_GOVERNORS_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/API_RUNTIME_ENTRY_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/BATCH_AND_BACKGROUND_MODEL_EXECUTION_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/CROSS_MODEL_AUDIT_AND_CONSENSUS_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/LOCAL_MODEL_AND_PRIVATE_EXECUTION_LANE_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/MODEL_CALL_RECEIPT_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_MISSION_DISPATCH_AND_MODEL_ROUTE_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
ION/02_architecture/ION_JOC_PROVIDER_ADAPTER_READINESS_AND_SELECTOR_HEALTH_VIEW_MODEL_PROTOCOL.md
```

Relevant registries include:

```text
ION/03_registry/provider_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_capability_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_pricing_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_rate_limit_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_routing_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_eval_score_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_data_handling_registry.yaml
ION/03_registry/work_class_model_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/budget_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/model_route_decision.schema.json
ION/03_registry/api_rate_governor_decision.schema.json
ION/03_registry/joc_mission_dispatch_route_view_model.schema.json
ION/03_registry/joc_provider_adapter_readiness_policy.yaml
ION/03_registry/joc_provider_adapter_readiness_view_model.schema.json
```

Relevant kernel organs include:

```text
ION/04_packages/kernel/model_economics_registry.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/model_router.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/cost_quality_router.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/api_rate_governor.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/api_runtime_entry.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_mission_dispatch_route_view_model.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_provider_adapter_readiness_view_model.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_dispatch_authorization_view_model.py
ION/04_packages/kernel/joc_dry_run_dispatch_trace_view_model.py
```

Relevant carrier profiles include:

```text
ION/04_agents/carriers/CLAUDE_CARRIER.profile.md
ION/04_agents/carriers/GEMINI_CARRIER.profile.md
```

This is enough to say ION already contains a serious model-routing and provider-economics organ.

It is not enough to say ION has production provider execution authority.

---

## 3. The core law already present

The strongest protocol sentence I found in the current root is:

```text
ION must not merely call models. ION must govern model selection as an economic, epistemic, temporal, and evidentiary act.
```

The same protocol family says the scheduler must not call providers directly. Model calls must pass through a chain like:

```text
Scheduler
→ work classification
→ call intent
→ model router
→ budget governor
→ API rate governor
→ scheduler lane placement
→ provider adapter
→ model call receipt
→ front-stage / repair / artifact path
```

This is mature ION thinking. It recognizes that provider dispatch is not a local implementation detail. It is a governed lifecycle.

The `MODEL_ROUTER_AND_COST_QUALITY_ROUTING_PROTOCOL.md` surface makes the separation even clearer:

```text
The scheduler decides what should run.
The work classifier types the work.
The model router chooses the candidate carrier.
The budget governor decides whether the cost is allowed.
The API rate governor decides whether dispatch may occur now.
The provider adapter executes dry-run or live provider calls.
The model-call receipt proves what happened.
```

That is the correct organ separation.

It prevents the router from becoming a hidden sovereign.

---

## 4. Model selection is epistemic governance

ION should not ask:

```text
Which model is best?
```

That question is too vague to be lawful.

ION should ask:

```text
Best for what work class?
Under what authority level?
With what context sensitivity?
With what privacy/data-handling boundary?
With what cost ceiling?
With what latency requirement?
With what review requirement?
With what receipt obligation?
With what fallback path?
With what non-claim boundary?
```

A model selected for cheap classification is not necessarily appropriate for source-summary rewrite review.

A model selected for architecture design is not necessarily appropriate for adversarial audit.

A model selected for visual diagnosis is not necessarily appropriate for user-facing repair wording.

A model selected for speed is not necessarily appropriate for canonical mutation.

A model selected for highest quality is not automatically authorized to see private context.

A local model may be weak but privacy-preserving.

A cloud frontier model may be strong but data-handling constrained.

A long-context model may be useful for corpus archaeology but dangerous if it swallows stale archive material without lifecycle classification.

A fast model may be ideal for JOC view-model hydration but inappropriate for authority movement.

ION therefore needs a model economy with semantic rights attached.

---

## 5. Routing modes and their dangers

The V116 router protocol names several route modes:

```text
cheapest_good_enough
highest_quality
best_margin
balanced
fastest_safe
consensus_required
batch_preferred
```

Each mode has legitimate use.

Each mode also has a shadow.

### cheapest_good_enough

Canonical use:

```text
low-risk, low-authority, easily checked work where minimum quality is enough.
```

Shadow:

```text
cheap model performs authority-sensitive work because the router optimized cost too aggressively.
```

### highest_quality

Canonical use:

```text
deep reasoning, architecture, adversarial audit, difficult synthesis, or high-loss decisions.
```

Shadow:

```text
model prestige becomes authority, and expensive output enters state without proof.
```

### best_margin

Canonical use:

```text
maximize quality per cost where quality estimates and price data are trustworthy enough for bounded use.
```

Shadow:

```text
placeholder pricing or stale eval scores produce false economic rationality.
```

### balanced

Canonical use:

```text
combine quality, speed, cost, privacy, context fit, and availability under normal bounded work.
```

Shadow:

```text
the blend hides why a particular tradeoff was chosen.
```

### fastest_safe

Canonical use:

```text
low-latency, bounded work where delay harms the operator or workflow.
```

Shadow:

```text
speed becomes a reason to bypass proof.
```

### consensus_required

Canonical use:

```text
high-risk claims, adversarial review, uncertain reconstructions, or disputed authority classification.
```

Shadow:

```text
consensus becomes theatre if the same stale context contaminates all reviewers.
```

### batch_preferred

Canonical use:

```text
background processing, corpus sweeps, non-interactive indexing, or cost-efficient review.
```

Shadow:

```text
batch outputs pile up faster than Steward can classify and integrate them.
```

The router must therefore emit not only a selected model, but the reason it chose that model, the remaining risk, and the gates still required before dispatch.

---

## 6. Cost is a constitutional variable

Cost is not merely billing.

Cost affects ION's ability to operate at scale. If ION is to orchestrate many roles, context packages, audits, visual checks, source-summary rewrites, and carrier loops, cost becomes part of its survival law.

But cost must not become a hidden tyrant.

A cost-aware ION must know:

```text
interactive vs batch cost;
front-stage vs backend cost;
high-authority vs low-authority cost;
review cost;
retry cost;
consensus cost;
context-loading cost;
visual-analysis cost;
long-corpus archaeology cost;
model-call failure cost;
wrong-model repair cost.
```

The cheapest path may become expensive if it creates repair debt.

The expensive path may become cheap if it prevents weeks of drift.

The correct unit is not token price alone.

The correct unit is:

```text
cost per lawful, accepted, reusable state transition.
```

This is an important ION-specific economics principle.

A model route should be judged not by raw output cost, but by how much governed state it can safely produce per unit of budget.

---

## 7. Quality is not a single score

A naive model router might rank models by one quality score.

ION cannot do that.

Quality in ION is multidimensional:

```text
reasoning quality
code quality
architecture quality
visual diagnosis quality
context compression quality
source-grounding quality
adversarial audit quality
repair-language quality
template compliance quality
schema compliance quality
privacy suitability
latency reliability
long-context endurance
stale-context resistance
self-overclaim resistance
```

A model may be excellent at writing code and weak at preserving authority boundaries.

A model may be excellent at broad synthesis and weak at exact schema compliance.

A model may be excellent at visual interpretation and weak at repository archaeology.

A model may be excellent at speed and weak at detecting stale canon.

ION's work-class model policy must therefore rank model suitability by function, not brand.

The deeper law:

```text
A model's quality is relative to the proof burden of the work.
```

If the work requires canonical mutation, quality must include evidence discipline.

If the work requires user-facing explanation, quality must include representational integrity.

If the work requires source rewrite, quality must include provenance and contradiction sensitivity.

If the work requires visual verification, quality must include rendered-state comparison.

If the work requires private context, quality must include data-handling fitness.

---

## 8. Provider trust is not model trust

ION must distinguish:

```text
provider
model
adapter
carrier
runtime session
credential scope
data-handling class
rate-limit state
current availability
receipt path
```

A provider can offer multiple models with different capabilities, prices, contexts, and data-handling boundaries.

A model can be strong but unavailable.

A provider can be registered but not live-call authorized.

A provider adapter can exist but only be dry-run ready.

A carrier profile can exist but not be mounted.

A credential can be present but not legally usable.

A route can be valid but blocked by budget.

A route can be valid but delayed by rate limits.

A route can be selected but not executed.

A model output can be received but not integrated.

These distinctions are necessary because otherwise a model-routing UI can accidentally imply authority it does not have.

The cockpit must show:

```text
route selected
budget allowed or blocked
rate allowed, queued, throttled, or rerouted
adapter dry-run/live status
credential authorization status
provider degradation status
receipt produced or missing
Steward integration pending/accepted/rejected
```

---

## 9. Privacy and local execution lanes

ION's model economy must include local/private lanes.

Not because local models are always stronger.

Because some context should not leave the operator's controlled environment.

Sensitive contexts include:

```text
credentials
private repo contents
user identity material
personal memory/context
unreleased project IP
sensitive safety/security analysis
client/customer data
visual screenshots from private systems
raw source-summary evidence before sanitization
```

A weaker local model may be the lawful route for low-authority tagging or private preprocessing.

A stronger external model may be lawful only after context minimization, redaction, abstraction, or human approval.

Therefore the router must treat privacy requirement as a hard filter, not a soft preference.

If a work class says local/private execution required, the router should not escape that constraint by citing quality.

The governing line:

```text
A model that is capable but not allowed is not eligible.
```

---

## 10. API runtime entry is not API sovereignty

The `API_RUNTIME_ENTRY_PROTOCOL.md` in the V116 root is careful. It says API runtime entry attaches an external/API carrier into an existing runtime/session center. It does not define the whole runtime/session authority center, queue/dispatch law, or enactment/activation authority.

This is correct.

API entry should be understood as:

```text
external carrier attachment
runtime session binding
entry receipt
carrier-boundary witness
context binding when authorized
refusal when session/authority constraints fail
```

It should not be understood as:

```text
provider can call anything
API server owns ION
external request equals authority
session creation equals activation
carrier binding equals role mount
queue entry equals dispatch approval
```

This distinction is essential for future ION productization.

Once an API exists, external systems will treat it as the product boundary. If the API lacks ION law, ION becomes a normal automation service with impressive documents.

Therefore API entry must be governed before API execution becomes broad.

The API is not the runtime center.

The API is a lawful doorway into the runtime center.

---

## 11. The model-call receipt

A model call without a receipt is not safe ION state.

A model-call receipt should preserve:

```text
call intent
work class
selected provider
selected model
routing mode
required capabilities
privacy/data-handling class
context refs or context minimization proof
budget decision
rate decision
adapter status
live/dry-run status
credential boundary
input hash or redacted input reference
output hash or output reference
latency
estimated and actual cost if available
failure/retry/reroute state
human/operator approval if required
front-stage visibility obligation
Steward integration disposition
```

This receipt does not make the output true.

It makes the model-call event auditable.

Truth still requires downstream proof, review, integration, and repair if contradicted.

The receipt is therefore not authority by itself.

It is the model-call witness surface.

---

## 12. Cross-model audit and consensus

Cross-model audit can be powerful. It can catch hallucinations, reveal disagreement, stress-test assumptions, and separate brittle reasoning from stable inference.

But it can also become consensus theatre.

ION must not treat agreement among models as truth unless the agreement is grounded in independent evidence and correctly scoped.

Consensus can fail when:

```text
all models received the same stale summary;
all models share a common training prior;
all models optimize for pleasing synthesis;
all models overtrust the prompt's framing;
all models lack access to the decisive file;
all models agree on a high-level truth while missing authority boundaries;
all models produce plausible but unreceipted outputs.
```

Therefore cross-model audit must be routed like any other work:

```text
claim or artifact under review
independent context packaging
model route selection
separate outputs
comparison template
contradiction classification
Steward verdict
receipt
repair/integration path
```

The important thing is not that many models spoke.

The important thing is whether their differences were preserved and judged.

---

## 13. Batch and background execution

ION's future clearly includes batch/background execution.

Batch lanes are needed for:

```text
corpus indexing
stale-shadow detection
source-summary draft generation
context compression
visual regression sweeps
schema validation
large-scale contradiction scans
archive archaeology
release verification
model-eval sampling
```

But batch execution is dangerous because it can produce large amounts of plausible material faster than Steward can understand, classify, or integrate it.

A lawful batch lane must therefore include:

```text
batch work class
input corpus boundary
context lifecycle class
cost budget
rate budget
provider/model route
output location
review queue target
accept/reject/integrate policy
receipt aggregation
rollback/quarantine path
```

Batch outputs should default to proposal/witness status, not canonical status.

The danger is automated sediment.

ION already has too much sediment from earlier AI work. Batch routing must not industrialize the same problem.

---

## 14. Provider adapter readiness

Provider adapter readiness is not a trivial health check.

A provider adapter should report:

```text
provider registered
model registered
credential status
live-call authorization
sandbox/dry-run status
rate-limit state
capacity state
privacy/data-handling profile
timeout/retry policy
receipt compatibility
error normalization
current degradation
operator approval requirement
```

A provider can be technically reachable and still not ION-ready.

A provider can be ION-ready for dry-run route simulation and still not authorized for live calls.

A provider can be live-call authorized for low-risk public context and blocked for private source data.

A provider can be available but too degraded for high-authority work.

This is why the JOC provider adapter readiness view matters. It must show not simply “online/offline,” but lawful readiness by capability and authority class.

---

## 15. The cockpit implication

Entry 18 established that visibility is part of ION's epistemic safety system. Entry 19 extends that to compute economics.

A compute/model cockpit should show:

```text
current mission dispatch route
work class
candidate models
selected route
rejected routes and reasons
cost estimate
quality threshold
privacy requirement
budget verdict
rate verdict
adapter readiness
live/dry-run boundary
receipt status
operator approval state
fallback route
consensus requirement
batch/interactivity lane
```

It should not merely show a pretty “selected model” label.

A selected model without rejected-route reasons is not enough.

A cost estimate without pricing freshness is not enough.

A quality score without work-class fit is not enough.

A green provider indicator without credential and authority status is not enough.

A route view without receipt status is not enough.

This is where cost/quality governance becomes visible truth.

---

## 16. Common shadows

The common stale or dangerous shadows are:

### Shadow 1 — best-model absolutism

```text
Use the strongest model for everything.
```

This ignores cost, privacy, rate, authority, and task-fit.

### Shadow 2 — cheapest-model absolutism

```text
Use the cheapest good-enough model for everything.
```

This creates repair debt and authority leakage when work class is misjudged.

### Shadow 3 — scheduler sovereignty

```text
The scheduler can call providers directly.
```

This bypasses work classification, routing, budget, rate, adapter, and receipt law.

### Shadow 4 — API equals product

```text
Once ION has an API, it is operational.
```

An API without runtime-entry law, session binding, receipts, and authority boundaries is just a transport endpoint.

### Shadow 5 — consensus as truth

```text
Multiple models agreed, so the claim is true.
```

Consensus without independent evidence is only correlated fluency.

### Shadow 6 — dry-run laundering

```text
The provider adapter passed dry-run, so live calls are authorized.
```

Dry-run readiness is not credential authority, production authority, or privacy clearance.

### Shadow 7 — placeholder pricing as truth

```text
The registry says this route is cheaper, so route it.
```

Placeholder or stale pricing must not be treated as current market truth.

### Shadow 8 — local model romanticism

```text
Local is always better because it is private.
```

Local/private lanes can be lawful and valuable, but capability and proof burden still matter.

### Shadow 9 — provider brand as authority

```text
A famous provider/model produced the output, so it is trustworthy.
```

Provider reputation does not replace proof.

### Shadow 10 — cost dashboard as governance

```text
Showing cost means cost is governed.
```

Cost must be routed through budget policy, authorization, receipts, and future accounting.

---

## 17. Mature ION recognition

The mature form of this organ is not:

```text
ION can use many models.
```

The mature form is:

```text
ION can govern model use as part of continuity law.
```

A mature ION model-routing system has:

```text
work-class model policy
capability registry
provider registry
pricing registry with freshness/status
rate-limit/capacity registry
privacy/data-handling registry
model eval registry
budget policy
routing policy
cost-quality router
API rate governor
provider adapter readiness view
model-call receipt
Steward integration route
front-stage visibility when user-facing
repair route when model output is contradicted
```

This is not merely an optimization layer.

It is the economic and epistemic nervous system of multi-model ION.

---

## 18. Current-root observation

My current-root observation is bounded.

The V116 root contains substantial model-routing/provider-economics architecture and kernel machinery:

```text
registry validation organ
model router
cost-quality router
API rate governor
API runtime-entry gateway
model/provider/economics registries
JOC route and provider readiness view models
multi-provider carrier profiles
```

The protocol language is unusually disciplined. It repeatedly forbids live provider calls, credential loading, production model-routing authority, scheduler-direct dispatch, unreceipted model outputs, and exact pricing claims as current truth.

That is good.

But I did not find broad model-routing test coverage in the current V116 test listing comparable to the protocol breadth. I found JOC view-model tests, but I did not find obvious tests named for `model_router`, `cost_quality_router`, `api_rate_governor`, `model_economics_registry`, or `api_runtime_entry` in the current test directory listing.

Therefore I should not claim the model-routing organ is fully verified.

The truthful claim is:

```text
ION already contains a mature model-routing and provider-economics doctrine with real current-root registries and kernel organs, but production model dispatch authority remains unclaimed and should stay blocked until deterministic tests, dry-run adapter proofs, budget/rate governance, model-call receipts, provider-readiness visibility, and Steward integration are verified.
```

---

## 19. Relation to the previous entries

Entry 1 established template law.

Model routing must be template-bound. A model call should occur because a template/action contract required a worker or reviewer route, not because the scheduler improvised.

Entry 2 established context packages.

Model routing must respect context package rights. A model cannot receive context merely because it is capable.

Entry 3 established Steward integration.

Model output is not state until integrated through Steward law.

Entry 4 established activation/carrier distinction.

A provider/model is not an ION role. It is a possible execution carrier or compute route.

Entry 8 established archive/witness/authority.

Model outputs enter first as witness/proposal unless authority promotes them.

Entry 9 established temporal lifecycle.

Model pricing, provider availability, eval scores, and rate limits are temporally unstable and must not be treated as timeless facts.

Entry 10 established canonical mutation.

Model output cannot rewrite canonical graph state merely because it is high quality.

Entry 11 established source-summary rewrite and context invalidation.

Model-generated summaries are dangerous inheritance objects requiring patch/provenance/review/rollback.

Entry 13 established daemon automation.

Daemon automation must not call models directly without routing/budget/rate/receipt law.

Entry 18 established cockpit visibility.

The compute route must become visible without laundering selected routes into authority.

---

## 20. Laws I would carry forward

1. Model calls are authority-bearing events.
2. The scheduler must not call providers directly.
3. Model selection must pass through typed work class, routing, budget, rate, adapter, and receipt law.
4. Provider registration is not live-call authorization.
5. Model capability is not data-handling permission.
6. Cost is measured against lawful accepted state, not raw token price alone.
7. Quality is work-class-relative, not brand-absolute.
8. Privacy constraints are hard filters, not preferences.
9. Consensus is evidence of agreement, not proof of truth.
10. Dry-run provider readiness is not production dispatch authority.
11. Placeholder pricing must not become current economic truth.
12. API runtime entry is a doorway into runtime/session authority, not the authority center itself.
13. Model-call receipts witness the call; they do not make the output true.
14. Batch outputs default to witness/proposal until reviewed and integrated.
15. The compute cockpit must render blocked authority as clearly as selected routes.

---

## 21. Current uncertainty

I am confident that ION contains mature model-routing and provider-economics doctrine.

I am confident that the V116 root contains real registry and kernel organs for this doctrine.

I am confident that the current protocols correctly block live provider calls, credential authority, scheduler-direct provider dispatch, and production model-routing authority.

I am not yet confident that the router, cost-quality router, budget governor, API rate governor, provider adapters, model-call receipts, and JOC route views are fully integrated into one executable dispatch path.

I am not yet confident that pricing, model evals, and provider capability data have freshness and update mechanics strong enough for live economic routing.

I am not yet confident that privacy/data-handling constraints are enforced all the way from context package to provider adapter.

I am not yet confident that cross-model audit has enough independence controls to avoid consensus theatre.

I am not yet confident that batch/background model execution has sufficient Steward intake capacity to avoid automated sediment.

I am not yet confident that model-routing outputs are consistently tied to receipts and downstream repair obligations.

Therefore I should not claim the model-routing/provider-economics lane is solved.

The truthful claim is:

```text
ION recognizes model dispatch as governance, not mere compute; it has built many of the doctrine, registry, and kernel organs needed for multi-provider orchestration, but live provider execution must remain blocked until the whole route-to-receipt-to-integration chain is verified under ION law.
```

---

## 22. Next journal implication

This entry points to the next organ:

```text
Security, Identity, Credentials, and Sensitive-Topic Governance.
```

Model routing immediately raises questions of credential authority, provider trust, privacy classes, identity verification, sensitive content access, local/private lanes, and cryptographic receipts. ION cannot become a multi-provider runtime without governing who may cause compute, what context may leave, what sensitive topics may be discussed, and what receipts must preserve.

This next organ is delicate because it touches the older AIMOS/ION idea of verified identity, voice ID, sensitive-topic access control, and cryptographic/public-ledger-style receipts. It must be handled as governance design, not unsafe operational instruction.

---

## 23. Closing line

```text
ION's model economy is not about choosing the best model.
It is about choosing the lawful model for the work, under the right proof burden, at the right cost, with the right rights.
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 20

## Security, Identity, Credentials, and Sensitive-Topic Governance

**Journal status:** witness artifact  
**Authority posture:** non-canonical, non-production, evidence-building reflection  
**Authoring carrier:** GPT-5.5 Thinking, acting as current ION-bound lead-dev witness in this conversation  
**Date:** 2026-05-04  
**Entry focus:** security posture, runtime identity, credentials, secrets, privacy/data-handling, hosted/auth boundaries, sensitive-topic governance, identity verification, receipt design, and the difference between trust, access, authority, and execution

---

## 0. Entry 20 settlement

The settlement of this entry is:

```text
Security in ION is not a perimeter.
Security is the right to continue knowing, acting, remembering, and speaking under bounded authority.
```

The shorter operational line:

```text
ION must not merely protect secrets.
ION must protect authority.
```

This entry follows naturally from Entry 19. Model routing raises immediate questions of privacy, provider trust, credential scope, data-handling class, local/private execution, and whether a model or carrier is allowed to see the context required for a task. But the issue is deeper than model routing. ION is a continuity runtime. If it becomes powerful, it will eventually mediate identity, credentials, private project context, account/workspace state, agent activation, high-risk research, operator approvals, hosted MCP access, provider calls, browser actions, shell actions, memory/context mutation, and potentially sensitive-topic discussions.

Therefore security cannot be bolted on as an external layer.

Security must be part of ION's ontology.

A normal system asks:

```text
Is the user authenticated?
Is the request authorized?
Is the secret stored safely?
```

ION must ask a larger set of questions:

```text
Who is acting?
What role is mounted?
What continuity substrate is bound?
What context is allowed to leave?
What credentials are available but not usable?
What operation is requested?
What authority class does it require?
What proof is owed before action?
What receipts must be emitted?
What state may change afterward?
What must be refused even if technically possible?
What must be visible to the operator?
What must be forgotten, redacted, hashed, or committed only as proof?
```

Security is therefore not separate from continuity. It is continuity under threat.

---

## 1. The question this entry asks

The question is not:

