# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 34

## ChatGPT Browser MCP Connector, Full-Carrier Parity, and Adapter Truth

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_34_chatgpt_browser_mcp_connector
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
live_execution_claim: false
entry_focus: browser connector ontology and the difference between current adapter guardrails and final carrier ambition
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry is not a connector implementation plan and not a claim that ChatGPT Browser currently has IDE-equivalent local control.

It records the current ontological meaning of the ChatGPT Browser MCP connector surfaces.

## 1. The Connector Is a Carrier Adapter, Not an ION Identity

The current connector protocol states the correct invariant in operational form:

```text
ION orchestrates.
Cursor carries.
Codex carries.
ChatGPT browser carries.
MCP carries.
No carrier is ION identity.
```

This is the same carrier/role distinction from the earlier journal, but now applied to an actual connector target.

The ChatGPT Browser carrier profile records the project-facing callsign `Sev`, but the callsign is a continuity label for the watched browser carrier. It does not grant Steward, Relay, Persona, production, live execution, credential, or deploy authority.

The callsign is useful because continuity needs a stable front surface. It is dangerous if treated as role authority.

Correct recognition:

```text
Sev = project-facing callsign for a ChatGPT Browser carrier surface.
Sev ≠ ION identity.
Sev ≠ Steward.
Sev ≠ Persona.
Sev ≠ Relay.
```

## 2. V120 Guardrails Are Current Adapter Guardrails, Not Final Ontology

The current connector contract exposes a bounded set of tools. The inspected manifest reports 42 allowed tools, including status, context, file read/search/tree, receipts, artifact transfer, bounded Codex queue requests, task return, agent invocation, carrier messages, and selected action receipt surfaces.

The forbidden families remain explicit:

```text
arbitrary shell
arbitrary file write
direct delete
git push
credential access
browser computer control
provider API calls
unbounded local filesystem access
production deployment
direct acceptance of unproofed worker output
```

That is the current safe MVP posture.

The newer full-carrier MCP parity protocol adds a second crucial distinction: these bounded restrictions are not necessarily the final theoretical ceiling for ChatGPT Browser as a carrier. They are the current adapter safety boundary.

This matters because two opposite errors are possible:

```text
Error A: ChatGPT Browser is only ever a read/status management lane.
Error B: ChatGPT Browser now has arbitrary local control.
```

The current truth is between them:

```text
ChatGPT Browser is a full carrier target in architectural ambition, but current implementation authority is bounded by explicit adapter guardrails, confirmations, proof gates, receipts, and non-production status.
```

## 3. Adapter Failure Is Not Core Failure

The full-carrier parity protocol introduces a vital failure-classification rule:

```text
If a carrier cannot perform a capability, classify adapter/transport/policy failure before declaring ION core failure.
```

This is a major anti-regression rule. It prevents a weak or partially connected browser adapter from causing false architectural conclusions.

Examples:

```text
If a ChatGPT connector cannot create a Codex work packet, inspect tool schema, confirmation gate, tunnel, and connector adapter.
If a hosted preview exits, inspect preview entry point and tunnel state.
If IDE can edit files but browser cannot, treat it as adapter capability gap until core packet law is proven missing.
```

The earlier journal’s evidence stratification becomes operational here. Current ION needs failure classes such as:

```text
ION_CORE_FAILURE
CARRIER_ADAPTER_FAILURE
TRANSPORT_FAILURE
AUTH_OR_CONFIRMATION_FAILURE
CAPABILITY_NOT_YET_IMPLEMENTED
POLICY_BLOCK_WORKING_AS_DESIGNED
```

Without that classification, every connector hiccup becomes a doctrine crisis.

## 4. Connector Tools Must Not Collapse Into Social Authority

The connector can expose a tool named like an action. That does not mean the action has authority to mutate truth.

The lawful chain remains:

```text
tool call
→ confirmation/gate if bounded write
→ packet/receipt creation
→ worker or local adapter action
→ proof-bearing return
→ Steward or template/action integration
→ receipt/state update
```

A connector tool is an adapter entry point, not a Steward decision.

The journal should carry this recognition rule forward:

```text
Every connector tool must be read as a transport for ION packet law, not a replacement for ION packet law.
```

## 5. Entry Settlement

The ChatGPT Browser MCP connector is one of the clearest current tests of ION’s ontology.

If ION handles it correctly, the browser becomes a powerful carrier surface while remaining subordinate to packets, templates, gates, receipts, and state.

If ION handles it poorly, the browser becomes either a powerless dashboard or an overclaimed pseudo-Steward.

The correct target is sharper:

```text
full-carrier ambition through staged adapter proof, not authority by convenience.
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 35

## ChatOps Browser Extension, YAML Action Bridge, and Approval-Scoped Transduction

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_35_chatops_browser_extension
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
live_execution_claim: false
entry_focus: ontology of the browser extension and local ChatOps bridge
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry is not a runnable action block. It intentionally does not contain a fenced YAML block whose first key is `ion_action`.

That detail is not cosmetic. The current extension lane is designed to parse candidate action blocks from ChatGPT output. A documentation artifact must avoid accidentally becoming an action candidate.

## 1. The Browser Extension Is a Transduction Layer

The ChatOps runtime gives the watched browser carrier a new practical path:

```text
ChatGPT renders a strict YAML/code block
→ extension detects and validates it
→ Braden previews and approves
→ local daemon receives the approved action
→ ION writes an action packet, draft, receipt, Codex work packet, or GitHub issue draft
```

This is not general browser automation. It is not an agent with hands. It is a transduction layer from watched chat text into local ION packet/receipt space.

The distinction is subtle and important:

```text
browser extension ≠ filesystem authority
browser extension ≠ shell authority
browser extension ≠ production authority
browser extension ≠ Steward
browser extension = candidate parser + approval UI + submitter to local policy daemon
```

The extension makes chat operational, but only through approval-scoped translation.

## 2. The First Key Rule Is Runtime-Relevant

The current ChatOps brief instructs the carrier to emit one YAML/code block whose first YAML key is `ion_action` when ION should act.

That rule gives the extension a clear parse boundary. It prevents ordinary prose from becoming an action. It also means future documents must be careful not to include accidental runnable examples.

Safe documentation should prefer:

```text
ion_action_example:
  schema: ion.chatops.action.v1
  ...
```

rather than a fenced block beginning with the actual runnable key.

This is a new documentation hygiene law created by the existence of a parser.

Before ChatOps, a markdown journal could casually show a sample action. After ChatOps, sample action blocks can become operational candidates if rendered in the watched surface.

## 3. Daemon Policy Is Narrow and Useful

The current local daemon policy is intentionally narrow:

```text
listen_host: 127.0.0.1
listen_port: 8767
supported MVP intents:
  register_artifact
  write_file_draft
  create_codex_work_packet
  create_github_issue_draft
hard-gated intents:
  delete_file
  overwrite_protected_file
  push_main
  access_credential
  production_deploy
  broad_shell
```

That is the right early shape. It converts the browser’s high-level intent into bounded local artifacts without granting host-level power.

The supported intents are not random. They match the current transition ION needs:

```text
register artifact -> preserve evidence without overclaiming
write file draft -> create reviewable draft under allowed paths
create Codex work packet -> send local implementation work to proper worker lane
create GitHub issue draft -> prepare data-plane coordination without push authority
```

## 4. The ChatOps Bridge Is an Approval Membrane, Not Steward Integration

Braden approval is required for submit. That matters. But Braden approval of a ChatOps action is not identical to Steward integration of resulting work.

The sequence remains layered:

```text
Braden approves the action packet submission.
ION/daemon records or materializes the bounded action.
Codex/local worker may perform the work.
Worker return must include context/template proof.
Steward/template action gate accepts or rejects the result.
Receipts record what actually landed.
```

This prevents an approval click from silently becoming state acceptance.

## 5. Parser Smoke Matters, but It Is Not Whole-System Proof

A focused parser smoke test passed in this sandbox from repo root:

```text
node ION/09_integrations/browser_extension/ion_chatops_bridge/tests/live_smoke_parser_simulation.js
```

The result reported:

```text
ok: true
panel: true
candidate: ion_chatops_candidate
action_id: sev-20260505-0001-smoke
rendered_dom_detected: 1
page_fallback_blocks: 2
```

This proves the simulated parser path can find the expected candidate. It does not prove production browser installation, live localhost daemon liveness, human UI approval in the operator’s actual browser, or end-to-end persistence on the local machine.

Correct proof claim:

```text
focused parser simulation passed in sandbox.
```

Incorrect proof claim:

```text
the live browser extension is fully operational everywhere.
```

## 6. Entry Settlement

The ChatOps bridge gives ION one of its most important new carrier affordances:

```text
watched language can become bounded local action without pretending language is authority.
```

That is exactly ION’s deeper thesis. The system does not trust fluency. It builds a bridge that requires parseability, approval, policy validation, packet materialization, and receipts.

The browser extension is therefore not a convenience plugin. It is a test of whether ION can turn chat into governed state transition candidates without letting chat become law.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 36

## Codex CLI, Codex Work Queue, Agent Broker, and the Difference Between Worker Power and State Authority

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_36_codex_queue_and_agent_broker
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
live_execution_claim: false
entry_focus: Codex CLI worker carrier, queued work, proof-gated returns, and multi-agent reuse of existing owners
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry does not invoke Codex CLI and does not process the current queue.

It records the meaning of the queue/agent surfaces currently present in the repo.

## 1. Codex CLI Is Now the Preferred Local Worker Carrier

V125 explicitly separates Codex CLI from older Codex IDE/extension surfaces.

The intended operating relationship is:

```text
ChatGPT Browser / GPT-5.5 Pro = coordinator, long-horizon reasoning, decision receipts, connector-visible state
Codex CLI = local bounded filesystem/build/test worker carrier
ION = governing runtime, packets, templates, proof gates, receipts, state surfaces, and cockpit projection
```

This is a strong carrier split. It means the browser should not pretend to be the local builder when Codex CLI is the better local worker, and Codex CLI should not pretend to be ION or Steward merely because it can edit files and run tests.

Codex CLI’s power is local execution. ION’s power is lawful state acceptance.

## 2. Queueing Is Not Execution

The current Codex queue contains 24 total requests with 8 queued for the Codex carrier. Several queued requests are near-duplicates around ChatOps runtime hardening and “state the exact bounded work” prompts.

This creates a live queue-hygiene lesson:

```text
a queued packet is not work completed;
a duplicate queued packet is not extra authority;
a stale queued packet may be evidence of operator pressure, not current priority;
a queue runner ready verdict does not mean all queued work should run blindly.
```

The correct next move is classification before execution:

```text
1. group near-duplicates;
2. identify newest/current objective;
3. preserve older queue items as evidence;
4. mark superseded or merge when lawful;
5. execute only the bounded survivor packet;
6. require proof-bearing return.
```

This is not bureaucracy. It prevents repeated local workers from solving yesterday’s request after today’s bridge changed.

## 3. Agent Invocation Broker Is Reuse, Not a Parallel Agent System

The inspected agent invocation broker reports:

```text
verdict: ION_AGENT_INVOCATION_BROKER_READY
agent_count: 16
no_parallel_agent_system_created: true
raw_backend_output_state_policy: RAW_CODEX_OUTPUT_NOT_ACCEPTED_WITHOUT_TASK_RETURN_PROOF_GATES
```

That is a healthy design signal.

The broker reuses:

```text
agent roster registry
agent context system registry
Codex work queue
Codex CLI execution packet
task returns
proof gates
carrier messages
```

This matters because the earlier journal warned against roleplay-agent proliferation. A new agent system would be dangerous if it created separate truth, separate queues, separate authority, or separate acceptance paths.

The current broker’s strongest virtue is that it does not attempt to become a second ION.

## 4. Raw Codex Output Must Remain Proposal

Codex is powerful because it can operate in the local filesystem. That same power makes it dangerous if its output is treated as accepted state.

The required return shape remains:

```text
### CONTEXT PROOF
### TEMPLATE ACTION PROOF
### RESULT
```

A Codex return must show:

```text
root proof
active packet used
files read
files changed
tests run
receipts/view models emitted
boundaries not crossed
remaining blockers
```

Only after proof-gated intake and Steward/template integration can the result land.

The key sentence:

```text
Codex can make patches; ION decides whether patches become state.
```

## 5. Queue Failure Classification Must Be Precise

The current queue runner declares failure classes:

```text
BACKEND_CODEX_FAILURE
CARRIER_ADAPTER_FAILURE
CODEX_CLI_FAILURE
DAEMON_FAILURE
ION_CORE_FAILURE
```

This is crucial. A blocked task return should not automatically indict the whole architecture. It may be malformed proof, missing local Codex installation, stale active run state, adapter failure, daemon gap, or core bug.

ION’s next maturity step is to require every blocked queue run to name the smallest accurate failure class.

## 6. Entry Settlement

Codex CLI and the agent broker are where ION’s ontology meets builder reality.

The current architecture is promising because it does not say:

```text
Let agents do things and trust them.
```

It says:

```text
Queue bounded work, route it through the local worker carrier, capture proof, validate proof, integrate or reject, and emit receipts.
```

That is ION’s core in action.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 37

## GitHub Data Plane, First Commit Boundary, and Public-State Non-Inflation

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_37_github_data_plane
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
push_claim: false
entry_focus: GitHub as data plane, not authority plane
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry does not push to GitHub, commit code, or authorize repository publication.

It records the current meaning of the GitHub data-plane surfaces.

## 1. GitHub Is a Large-Data Plane, Not Steward

The current repo has a configured local git origin:

```text
https://github.com/ION-operations/ion-codex.git
```

The GitHub data-plane audit reports readiness while also reporting:

```text
has_commits: false
first_commit_status: NO_LOCAL_COMMITS_YET
worktree_clean: false
untracked_count: 45 top-level buckets
commit_allowed_by_audit: false
push_allowed_by_audit: false
network_access_used: false
```

This is an excellent example of mature representational integrity. The audit can say the data-plane setup is configured and ready for review, while refusing to claim commit/push authority.

## 2. Public Visibility Does Not Create Truth

GitHub can preserve large artifacts, support issues, enable collaboration, and provide a remote data plane. It does not decide which ION state is true.

Correct chain:

```text
ION state/proof/receipts -> reviewed commit candidate -> human/policy gate -> Git commit/push/issue artifact
```

Incorrect chain:

```text
GitHub file exists -> therefore current ION law
```

This matters because public repositories can intensify stale-authority risk. Once a stale file is visible in GitHub, future workers may treat it as more official than local active packets.

GitHub must therefore carry state classification, not erase it.

## 3. First Commit Is a Bootstrap Gate

No local commits exist in the inspected repo. That is not a failure by itself. It means the first commit is a special governance event.

A first commit should not be a bulk dump that makes every untracked surface equally canonical. It should be a reviewed bootstrap state with:

```text
exact paths staged
secret scan
validation command results
lifecycle classification of hot/archive/containment surfaces
rollback path
receipt
human gate or policy gate
explicit non-production posture
```

The audit’s refusal to allow push is therefore healthy.

## 4. GitHub Issue Drafts Fit ChatOps Better Than Git Push

The ChatOps daemon supports `create_github_issue_draft`, not `git_push`.

That is the right early integration. A GitHub issue draft can express work, evidence, blockers, or review requests without mutating the public code state. It is a coordination artifact, not an authority operation.

This matches ION’s preference:

```text
prepare evidence before mutation;
draft before publication;
receipt before integration;
human gate before public push.
```

## 5. Entry Settlement

GitHub is valuable because ION needs a large-data plane. It is dangerous if mistaken for the authority plane.

The current repo’s audit surfaces preserve the right distinction:

```text
configured remote, no commits, no push authority, no network mutation, first commit requires gates.
```

That is exactly the posture a proof-gated continuity system should take before exposing itself publicly.

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 38

## Packaging Hygiene, Missing Authority References, and Test-Claim Precision

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_38_packaging_hygiene_and_claim_precision
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
entry_focus: small inconsistencies that matter because they affect future carrier trust
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry is not a repair patch.

It records practical inconsistencies that should influence future repair planning.

## 1. Missing README Reference

The shell `pyproject.toml` references:

```text
ION/README.md
```

In the inspected archive, that file is absent.

This does not break ordinary source inspection. It may break packaging/build metadata paths or create confusion for future workers. Because `ION/README.md` is referenced by package metadata, it should be classified:

```text
intentionally absent / retired / needs restoration / needs pyproject update
```

Do not silently ignore it. Do not automatically invent it. First classify.

## 2. Repo Authority References Historical/Missing Surfaces

Several older or supporting surfaces referenced by startup or authority docs appear absent in the inspected archive, including examples such as:

```text
ION/STATUS.md
ION/PLAN.md
ION/MASTER_ORCHESTRATION_INDEX.md
ION/docs/README.md
ION/AGENT_CONTRACT.md
```

Some may be intentionally retired. Some may be historical aliases. Some may be actual missing support files. The current mount contract is strong enough to prevent these from automatically becoming blockers, but the references still deserve lifecycle classification.

The right repair is not:

```text
create all missing files from scratch.
```

The right repair is:

```text
for each referenced missing surface, decide retired/superseded/restored/alias/required, then emit a containment or restoration receipt.
```

## 3. Full-Test Claims Must Stay Fresh

A previous inspection of this extracted repo reported:

```text
254 passed in 9.65s
```

During this addendum pass, a full pytest run timed out partway through the dot stream in the sandbox. That may reflect environment, timeout behavior, changed command conditions, or a specific hanging test. It should not be exaggerated.

Correct claim:

```text
Prior full-suite pass was observed. Fresh full-suite rerun in this sandbox timed out. Focused ChatOps parser simulation passed.
```

Incorrect claim:

```text
Full current test suite passes now.
```

Test claim precision is not pedantry. ION’s representational integrity depends on not letting old validation receipts become fresh proof.

## 4. Small Hygiene Issues Are Not Small Under Carrier Mount

A missing README reference, stale startup surface, duplicate queued request, or ambiguous test receipt may look minor. But each can become a carrier drift seed.

A weak carrier can overreact to any one of them:

```text
missing README -> invent new overview as authority;
missing AGENT_CONTRACT -> create new agent doctrine;
duplicate queued work -> run wrong packet;
old test pass -> claim current validation;
stale V116 language -> ignore V119/V125 mount law.
```

Therefore hygiene work should be routed through lifecycle classification and patch preflight, not casual cleanup.

## 5. Entry Settlement

The current repo is operationally strong enough to inspect and reason over, but it still contains friction points that future carriers may misread.

The correct posture is:

```text
ready does not mean frictionless;
missing does not mean absent essence;
reference does not mean authority;
old pass does not mean fresh proof;
small inconsistency can become large drift if not classified.
```

---

# ION Ontological Journal — GPT-5.5 Entry 39

## Journal-to-Executable Bridge After ChatOps: First Handles Must Reuse Current Owners

```yaml
journal_id: ion_ontological_journal_gpt55
entry_id: entry_39_journal_to_executable_bridge_after_chatops
created_at: 2026-05-05
status: WITNESS_ARTIFACT_NOT_CANON
production_claim: false
implementation_claim: false
entry_focus: update Entry 32's executable-consequence plan against current ChatOps/Codex/MCP owners
```

## 0. Boundary

This entry does not create the templates proposed in Entry 32.

It updates the proposed executable consequences so they route through the current repo’s actual owners.

## 1. Entry 32 Was Correct, But Its Next Step Must Be Narrower

Entry 32 said the journal should start making small executable handles instead of continuing indefinitely as beautiful prose.

That remains correct.

But the current repo has moved enough that the first handles should not be introduced as a free-floating `V117_JOURNAL_EXECUTABLE_HANDLES` patch. They should be introduced as narrow extensions of existing surfaces.

The current owners already include:

```text
ION_MOUNT_CONTRACT.md
ION_CURRENT_OPERATING_PACKET_V119.md
ChatGPT Browser MCP connector contract
ChatOps YAML action protocol
ChatOps local daemon policy
Codex CLI carrier protocol
Codex work queue runner
agent invocation broker
template action gate
carrier message queue
GitHub data plane audit
active state integrity audit
```

New handles should bind to those owners.

## 2. Updated First Handle Set

The proposed first handles should be reframed as follows.

### 2.1 Patch Preflight

Old candidate:

```text
PATCH_PREFLIGHT_TEMPLATE.md
```

Current-root route:

```text
extend or add a small template under implementation/review templates;
require it before ChatOps `write_file_draft` or Codex work packets that mutate protocol/kernel/registry surfaces;
connect it to template-action proof and Codex queue receipts;
do not create a parallel approval system.
```

Minimum fields:

```text
target paths
owner paths
existing mature surfaces searched
duplicate/sediment risk
authority ceiling
allowed output
forbidden side effects
validation command
rollback/containment path
new_system: false unless explicitly justified
```

### 2.2 Organ Recall

Old candidate:

```text
ORGAN_RECALL_TEMPLATE.md
```

Current-root route:

```text
bind to containment-preservation law and search sufficiency;
use before claiming a missing subsystem or creating a new one;
record searched current/donor/historical owners;
output classification: found / missing / stale / duplicate / intentionally retired / needs restoration.
```

### 2.3 Nemesis Review

Old candidate:

```text
NEMESIS_REVIEW_TEMPLATE.md
```

Current-root route:

```text
route through agent invocation broker when used as a worker request;
require proof-bearing return;
prevent Nemesis from becoming an unconstrained personality;
make review result candidate evidence until integrated.
```

### 2.4 Search Sufficiency Receipt

Old candidate:

```text
SEARCH_SUFFICIENCY_RECEIPT.md
```

Current-root route:

```text
connect to file search/tree/list tools and current active owner paths;
require enough evidence before a worker may claim absence;
include stale/current/donor boundary.
```

### 2.5 Node Missing Event

Old candidate:

```text
NODE_MISSING_EVENT
```

Current-root route:

```text
connect to active state integrity audit and lifecycle/containment receipts;
do not let it become a deletion alarm only;
model missing, retired, moved, contained, superseded, and never-existed separately.
```

### 2.6 Non-Idle Lane Registry

Old candidate:

```text
NON_IDLE_LANE_REGISTRY
```

Current-root route:

```text
explicitly mark non-background/non-autonomous unless an actual daemon/automation authority exists;
use for approved beneficial work proposals, not hidden execution;
prefer ChatOps Codex work packet draft or carrier message queue over imaginary background work.
```

## 3. ChatOps Makes Executable Handles More Dangerous and More Useful

Before ChatOps, a proposed template was mostly passive. After ChatOps, a ChatGPT browser carrier can emit an action candidate that writes a draft, creates a Codex work packet, or registers an artifact.

That means the journal-to-executable bridge needs stronger preflight.

A future assistant should not simply say:

```text
I will create these six templates.
```

It should first produce a bounded action proposal that names:

```text
which existing owner is extended;
why no existing template suffices;
what paths may be touched;
what validation will run;
what receipt will prove containment;
what authority is not claimed;
whether the proposed file is draft, witness, protocol candidate, or active template.
```

## 4. The Best Immediate Workboard

For the current repo, the best next workboard implied by the journal is not “write foundation canon.” It is:

```text
1. queue hygiene for the 8 queued Codex work requests;
2. ChatOps runtime hardening around parser, daemon validation, approval receipts, and duplicate action IDs;
3. Sev re-entry checklist tied to ion_status + ion_tool_manifest + context brief;
4. patch preflight draft that reuses template-action proof and ChatOps/Codex queue owners;
5. lifecycle classification of missing referenced startup/support docs;
6. first-commit GitHub data-plane gate, if and only if Braden wants public remote state.
```

That workboard directly changes future worker behavior. It is more useful than another broad ontology pass.

## 5. Entry Settlement

The journal has reached its executable threshold, but the current root already has enough owners that new handles must be small, owner-bound, and gate-aware.

The strongest sentence now is:

```text
The journal should not become a second operating system; it should emit small handles that plug into the operating system ION already has.
```

The immediate law for future work:

```text
reuse owners first;
classify failure precisely;
write drafts before law;
avoid runnable action examples in passive docs;
route implementation through ChatOps/Codex queues only with proof and receipts;
never let the journal outrank the runtime.
```
